<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch4 — T2 silences for Wisdom as holistic inner character and orientation -->

**T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries**

- *T2.1.1* — _Is this characteristic explicitly located at the spirit level in the verse evidence?_
  → Wisdom as constituted character (M15-A) is not explicitly located at the spirit level in the sub-group's verses. The spirit is the origin channel for the giving of wisdom (VCG02: Exo 31:3 — Bezalel filled with the Spirit receives wisdom; Dan 5:14 — spirit of the gods associated with wisdom in Daniel), but the constituted wisdom itself is located in the heart (Pro 16:23 VCG03 anchor). Spirit-level location of the constituted wisdom: silent.
- *T2.5.1* — _Does the verse evidence surface any soul-level location beyond heart and mind for this characteristic?_
  → No additional soul-level locations in M15-A's evidence beyond heart and mind.
- *T2.5.3* — _If the evidence is silent, note this explicitly._
  → No soul-level locations beyond heart and mind are evidenced for these sub-groups.
- *T2.8.1* — _Does sustained operation of this characteristic leave a constitutional deposit in the body or its design — including DNA or generational con…_
  → No evidence in M15-A's verse corpus of wisdom leaving a body-deposit. The speech-mouth link is expressive, not depositional. Silence.
<!-- /EVIDENCE -->

<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch4 — T3 findings for Wisdom as holistic inner character and orientation -->

**T3 — The Inner Faculties**

- *T3.1.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the perceptive faculty — the inner senses including hearing, sight, taste, touch, smell, and spiritual disce…_
  → VCG01 (Pro 16:23): "a wise man's heart guides his mouth" — wisdom perceives the appropriate and guides expression. VCG04 (froneō): perception directed toward things of God vs things of flesh — wisdom-perception is orientation-perception. VCG08 (H7922 se.khel, Neh 8:8): grasping the meaning of Scripture — intelligibility as wisdom's perceptive mode.
- *T3.1.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair the perceptive faculty in the person?_
  → Both: wisdom includes perceptive capacity (VCG08 understanding Scripture) and produces perceptive outcomes (the wise person sees what others miss). Wisdom is a wisdom-for-perceiving-rightly, not raw perception.
- *T3.1.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with perception reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Governance perception (VCG03 Solomon's governance discernment), directional perception (VCG04 things of God vs flesh), intelligibility perception (VCG08 understanding Scripture). Wisdom's perceptive range is oriented and directional — it perceives in relation to God and right action.
- *T3.10.1* — _Does this characteristic engage conscientiousness — the integrated response of moral awareness, volition, and action — and if so, how?_
  → VCG03 (Pro 10:14): accumulating and guarding knowledge is conscientious inner practice. VCG04 (froneō): sustained directional orientation requires conscientious maintenance.
- *T3.10.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscientiousness in the person?_
  → Wisdom enables and deepens conscientiousness: the constituted wise character produces consistent, thoughtful, disciplined engagement with obligations. Wisdom cannot bypass or impair conscientiousness while remaining genuine wisdom — the loss of conscientiousness signals the loss of wisdom.
- *T3.10.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscientiousness reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Wisdom's enabling of conscientiousness reveals it as a character-forming rather than merely capacity-conferring characteristic. Wisdom does not give the person a tool to be conscientious with; it forms the inner constitution from which conscientiousness naturally flows.
- *T3.11.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the relational capacity — the constitutional equipment for genuine connection with another person — and if s…_
  → VCG05 (froneō — shared inner orientation, Phil 2:2): wisdom as shared communal inner state — wisdom-as-unity-of-mind. VCG03 (governance wisdom, 1Ki 3:9): wisdom as the capacity for just relational governance.
- *T3.11.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair relational capacity in the person?_
  → VCG05 (shared orientation): relational harmony as a mode of wisdom expression.
- *T3.11.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with relational capacity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Relational depth is governance-oriented and communal-unity oriented. Wisdom enables right governance of relationships; its relational depth is mediated through character and judgment.
- *T3.2.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the cognitive faculty — knowing, understanding, discerning — and if so, how?_
  → VCG03 (1Ki 3:9): governance judgment. VCG04 (froneō): directional orientation of the mind. VCG08 (Neh 8:8 se.khel): comprehension of meaning. Cognitive processes: orientation-formation, governance-judgment, meaning-comprehension.
- *T3.2.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair cognition in the person?_
  → M15-A operates at the integrative-orientational level: wisdom is cognition that has been directed, formed, and constituted — it is not raw reasoning but constituted inner orientation that produces consistent cognitive fruit.
- *T3.2.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with cognition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Depth: VCG07 (wisdom of this age) names the deepest cognitive orientation — the framework from which the person perceives everything. Wisdom is depth-constitutive.
- *T3.3.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the memory faculty — the holding and retrieving of inner-being reality across time — and if so, how?_
  → VCG09 (Pro 9:10 — "the beginning of wisdom is the fear of the LORD"): wisdom is built on the accumulated knowing of God's character and ways. Memory of who God is and what he has done is the basis of wisdom.
- *T3.3.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair memory in the person?_
  → VCG03 (Pro 10:14 cha.kham in wisdom corpus): wisdom accumulated and held — "the wise lay up knowledge" applies to wisdom as well as knowledge. Wisdom is stored as constituted character.
- *T3.3.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with memory reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T3.4.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the affective faculty — feeling and emotional experience — and if so, how?_
  → VCG04 (froneō, Rom 8:5-8): setting the mind on the flesh produces death; setting the mind on the Spirit produces life and peace. Wisdom-orientation produces affective outcomes (peace). VCG09 (Pro 9:10): "fear of the LORD" as the wisdom-foundation — fear as an affective orientation.
- *T3.4.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair affect in the person?_
  → Wisdom produces affect secondarily: wisdom-as-character produces peace (via right orientation), but is not itself affective.
- *T3.4.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with affect reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T3.5.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the creative faculty — imagination and the capacity to originate — and if so, how?_
  → VCG10 (M15-A inner creative design): "all wise-hearted men in whom the LORD had put wisdom and understanding to know how to do" (Exo 36:1) — wisdom as inner creative capacity for sacred construction. The one sub-group in M15 where creative design is explicitly named.
- *T3.5.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair creativity in the person?_
  → VCG10 (Exo 36:1 — craftsmen wisdom-endowed for sacred construction): wisdom enables and deepens creativity — the Spirit-given wisdom directly produces craft skill and creative design capacity. Wisdom is the inner precondition of the creative act in this evidence.
- *T3.5.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with creativity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Wisdom's direct engagement with creativity (VCG10 Exo 36:1) reveals it as the most broadly enabling of M15's characteristics — it is the only sub-group where creative capacity is explicitly constituted by the characteristic's reception. Wisdom is integrative: it includes creative, governance, communicative, and moral dimensions.
- *T3.6.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the volitional faculty — the capacity to choose — and if so, how?_
  → VCG04 (froneō, Rom 8:5-8): setting the mind on the Spirit vs the flesh — the wisdom-orientation requires volitional commitment. VCG06 (self-attributed wisdom): the volitional stance of claiming wisdom as a personal possession.
- *T3.6.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair volition in the person — including its three aspects: capacity, interaction with …_
  → All three: volitionally received (the person who asks — Jas 1:5), maintained (the wise person who accumulates and guards), refused (the person who rejects wisdom's call — Pro 1:24-33).
- *T3.6.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with volition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T3.7.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the agency faculty — the capacity to act, initiate, and make happen — and if so, how?_
  → VCG01 (Pro 16:23): wisdom guides the mouth — communicative agency. VCG03 (1Ki 3:9): governance agency. VCG10 (Exo 36:1): creative-constructive agency.
- *T3.7.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair agency in the person?_
  → Governance agency (VCG03), communicative agency (VCG01), creative-constructive agency (VCG10), life-directional agency (VCG04).
- *T3.7.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with agency reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Wisdom's consistent agency-conferral (governance, communicative, creative) reveals that it is not a contemplative but a productive characteristic: wisdom IS the inner constitution that generates effective action. Its agency-pattern is wide and consistent — wherever wisdom is constituted in the person, agency follows.
- *T3.8.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the moral evaluation faculty — the capacity to assess against a standard of right, wrong, good, and true — a…_
  → VCG04 (froneō, Rom 8:5-8): the directional orientation of wisdom is constitutively moral — setting the mind on flesh or Spirit is a moral evaluation of orientation. VCG06 (self-attributed wisdom): morally problematic inner posture named.
- *T3.8.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair moral evaluation in the person?_
  → Mixed: wisdom's orientation toward God (VCG04 froneō Spirit vs flesh) is constitutively moral. Other dimensions acquire moral significance through direction.
- *T3.8.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with moral evaluation reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Wisdom's moral engagement is orientation-based: wisdom's moral significance lies in its direction (toward God = constitutively moral; toward self = constitutively problematic). The pattern reveals wisdom as a morally charged characteristic whose charge is determined by its orientation, not its possession.
- *T3.9.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the conscience — the acute inner witness of sin, guilt, and conviction — and if so, how?_
  → VCG03 (Pro 10:14): "the wise lay up knowledge" — wisdom governs the inner moral faculty by accumulating the content conscience draws on. Wisdom provides the governance context for conscience.
- *T3.9.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscience in the person?_
  → Wisdom operates alongside conscience: wisdom provides the framework, character, and content from which conscience judges. They are structurally parallel but distinct.
- *T3.9.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscience reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Wisdom's indirect conscience engagement (providing governance-framework and content for conscience) reveals it as the constituting context of conscience rather than conscience itself. Wisdom shapes the inner moral framework from which conscience draws its material.

**Key verses for Wisdom as holistic inner character and orientation:**

**Dan 2:20** (H2452 chokh.mah) [M15-A-VCG01]
> Dan 2:20 Daniel answered and said : “ Blessed be the name of God forever and ever , to whom belong wisdom and might .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "to him belong wisdom and might" — wisdom as God's own attribute

**Jam 1:5** (G4678 sofia) [M15-A-VCG02]
> Jam 1:5 If any of you lacks wisdom , let him ask God , who gives generously to all without reproach , and it will be given him .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "if any lacks wisdom, let him ask God who gives generously" — wisdom is not self-generated; it is asked for and given

**Pro 16:23** (H2450 cha.kham) [M15-A-VCG03]
> Pro 16:23 The heart of the wise makes his speech judicious and adds persuasiveness to his lips .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "heart of the wise makes his speech judicious" — wisdom in the heart shapes outward speech

**Rom 8:5** (G5426 froneō) [M15-A-VCG04]
> Rom 8:5 For those who live according to the flesh set their minds on the things of the flesh , but those who live according to the Spirit set their minds on the things of the Spirit .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "set their minds on things of flesh / Spirit" — froneō as the determinative inner orientation; flesh-minded or Spirit-minded describes the whole person

**Phili 2:2** (G5426 froneō) [M15-A-VCG05]
> Phili 2:2 complete my joy by being of the same mind , having the same love , being in full accord and of one mind .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "being of the same mind" — froneō as the inner orientation of the whole community

**Pro 26:12** (H2450 cha.kham) [M15-A-VCG06]
> Pro 26:12 Do you see a man who is wise in his own eyes ? There is more hope for a fool than for him .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "a man who is wise in his own eyes — more hope for a fool" — self-attributed wisdom as worse than foolishness; inner self-assessment as the problem

**1Cor 1:21** (G4678 sofia) [M15-A-VCG07]
> 1Cor 1:21 For since , in the wisdom of God , the world did not know God through wisdom , it pleased God through the folly of what we preach to save those who believe .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "world did not know God through wisdom" — sophia as the instrument that failed to reach God

**Neh 8:8** (H0995 bin) [M15-A-VCG08]
> Neh 8:8 They read from the book , from the Law of God , clearly , and they gave the sense , so that the people understood the reading .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "they gave the sense so that the people understood the reading" — bin activated by clear exposition; the inner faculty grasps meaning when the word is made clear

**Psa 111:10** (H7922 se.khel) [M15-A-VCG09]
> Psa 111:10 The fear of the Lord is the beginning of wisdom ; all those who practice it have a good understanding . His praise endures forever !
_Meaning of the term here:_ "all who practice it have good understanding" — se.khel as the fruit of practicing the fear of the Lord

**Exo 31:4** (H2803G cha.shav) [M15-A-VCG10]
> Exo 31:4 to devise artistic designs , to work in gold , silver , and bronze ,
_Meaning of the term here:_ "to devise artistic designs" — cha.shav explicitly names the inner act of design, not just execution

**T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries**

- *T2.1.2* — _Does the evidence indicate that this characteristic originates in or is primarily a spirit-level phenomenon?_
  → Same pattern: Spirit-given understanding (Exo 31 corpus in VCG02). The Spirit gives; the heart receives.
- *T2.1.3* — _What does spirit-level location reveal about the nature and depth of this characteristic?_
  → Where the Spirit is named as the giver of wisdom/understanding (VCG02 corpus: Exo 31:3), this reveals that the gift transcends the person's own capacity — it is not self-generated or achievable through effort alone. The Spirit's involvement marks these characteristics as deeply covenantal — they are given in the context of specific divine assignments (Bezalel for sanctuary work, Solomon for governance, Daniel for prophetic interpretation). The depth of what is given exceeds normal human capacity: "the spirit of the holy gods" in Daniel marks wisdom/understanding as a divine-grade endowment placed in a human person.
- *T2.1.4* — _If the evidence is silent on spirit-level location, note this explicitly._
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T2.10.1* — _Does this characteristic move across constitutional levels — from spirit to soul, from soul to body, or across boundaries in other direction…_
  → Job 38:36 (VCG02 anchor): God places understanding → human person. VCG06 (Luk 24:45): Christ opens minds. Movement: divine → human-soul. Ear → understanding → governance: body-input → soul → action.
- *T2.10.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about the sequence or pattern of that movement?_
  → Pattern: divine placing/opening → heart-constituted faculty → practical governance. The sequence is linear: received → held → exercised.
- *T2.10.3* — _If no constitutional movement is evidenced, note this explicitly._
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T2.2.1* — _Is this characteristic identified in the verse evidence as a soul-level phenomenon?_
  → 1Ki 3:9 (VCG03 anchor): "a discerning heart" — heart-level = soul-level. Luk 24:45: "opened their minds" — mind-level = soul-level. Both confirmed soul-level.
- *T2.2.2* — _What does soul-level location reveal about this characteristic's place in the innermost personal experience?_
  → 1Ki 3:9: understanding at the heart level reveals it as the faculty that equips the person for governance from the inside out. Soul-level understanding governs the person's navigation of all situations.
- *T2.2.3* — _If the evidence is silent on soul-level location, note this explicitly._
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T2.3.1* — _Does the verse evidence locate this characteristic in the heart?_
  → 1Ki 3:9 (VCG03 anchor): "give your servant a discerning [understanding] heart." Definitionally heart-located.
- *T2.3.2* — _What does the heart-location reveal — what aspect of the heart's integrating function (knowing, willing, feeling, moral awareness) does this…_
  → 1Ki 3:9: understanding in the heart engages the heart's discerning function — distinguishing right from wrong. M15-B engages the heart as the discerning faculty.
- *T2.3.3* — _If the evidence is silent on heart-location, note this explicitly._
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T2.4.1* — _Does the verse evidence locate this characteristic in the mind?_
  → Luk 24:45 (VCG06 anchor): "he opened their minds [nous] so they could understand." The mind (nous) is explicitly named as the site of understanding's opening.
- *T2.4.2* — _What does mind-location reveal — what aspect of the mind's function (thought, discernment, understanding) does this characteristic engage?_
  → Luk 24:45: nous as the site of opening reveals understanding engaging the mind's receptive-comprehension function.
- *T2.4.3* — _If the evidence is silent on mind-location, note this explicitly._
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T2.5.2* — _If so, what is that location, and what does it reveal?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T2.6.1* — _Does the verse evidence link this characteristic to a specific body part?_
  → The ear as input: understanding receives through hearing (the ear mediates the reception of disclosed meaning). VCG06 (Luk 24:45): minds opened to understand — but the hearing/receiving body-link for understanding is the ear. VCG07: translation involves the ear-understanding-mouth chain.
- *T2.6.2* — _If so, what is Scripture doing by making that link — is it emphatic, functional, expressive, indicative, or mediating?_
  → The ear-understanding link is mediating: the ear is the receiving body-part through which understanding enters. Scripture uses the ear-body-part because hearing is the primary mode of receiving disclosed meaning (faith comes by hearing, Rom 10:17 proximate).
- *T2.6.3* — _If no body-part link is evidenced, note this explicitly._
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T2.7.1* — _Where a body-characteristic link exists, which direction does it run — does the soul express through the body, does the body feed back to th…_
  → Bidirectional: body → soul (ear hears, understanding receives); soul → body (understanding governs speech in VCG07 translation context). Both directions evidenced.
- *T2.7.2* — _What is the consequence of that directionality for understanding the characteristic?_
  → The bidirectionality reveals understanding as a relational faculty — it receives from outside (ear → understanding) and governs what it produces (understanding → speech in interpretation). Understanding is an interface faculty.

  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]

  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T2.9.1* — _Where does this characteristic originate constitutionally — is it generated from within the person, received from outside, bestowed by God, …_
  → Divine placing (Job 38:36 VCG02 anchor); formation through practice (Heb 5:14 VCG05 anchor); Christ's opening act (Luk 24:45 VCG06 anchor). Multiple origin modes, all pointing to divine-mediated constitution.
- *T2.9.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about whether the origin is singular or multiple?_
  → Multiple: divine placing, practice-formed, Christ-opened. All converge on divine-mediated constitution; the mechanisms differ.
- *T2.9.3* — _Does the origin of this characteristic change across different contexts evidenced in Scripture?_
  → Different contexts produce different mechanisms: prophetic context (Daniel) → Spirit-given; governance context (Solomon) → direct gift; formation context (Heb 5:14) → practice; resurrection context (Luk 24:45) → Christ's opening. The origin-mechanism changes by context.

**T3 — The Inner Faculties**

- *T3.1.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the perceptive faculty — the inner senses including hearing, sight, taste, touch, smell, and spiritual disce…_
  → VCG03 (1Ki 3:9): the discerning heart as the perceptive faculty for governance. VCG06 (Luk 24:45): Christ opening the disciples' minds — the perceptive faculty opened to receive disclosed content. M15-B is constitutively perceptive: understanding IS the act of perceiving distinctions.
- *T3.1.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair the perceptive faculty in the person?_
  → M15-B IS a form of perception. Bin, suniēmi name the perceptive act itself. Understanding does not produce perception as a secondary outcome — it is the perceptive act.
- *T3.1.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with perception reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Range: understanding God's ways, prophecy, teaching, strategic situations. The range is broad but coherent: understanding is always the act of grasping the meaning-structure of something.
- *T3.10.1* — _Does this characteristic engage conscientiousness — the integrated response of moral awareness, volition, and action — and if so, how?_
  → VCG05 (Heb 5:14): training discernment through constant practice is quintessential conscientiousness.
- *T3.10.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscientiousness in the person?_
  → Understanding enables conscientiousness: the trained faculty (VCG05 Heb 5:14) is itself the product of conscientious practice, and it then enables more conscientious moral discrimination. Understanding deepens conscientiousness by sharpening the ability to discern what careful engagement requires.
- *T3.10.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscientiousness reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Understanding's conscientiousness-engagement (through the trained aisthētērion) reveals it as a formable faculty: understanding grows through conscientious practice, and grown understanding enables more conscientious life. The relationship is mutually reinforcing.
- *T3.11.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the relational capacity — the constitutional equipment for genuine connection with another person — and if s…_
  → VCG07 (M15-B — sustained reasoned argument engaging the inner person, dialegō): understanding as the faculty that enables sustained relational discourse.
- *T3.11.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair relational capacity in the person?_
  → VCG07 (dialegō): sustained reasoned engagement with another is a relational mode of understanding-in-action.
- *T3.11.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with relational capacity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Relational depth in understanding is primarily communicative-discursive — enabling sustained intellectual engagement in relationship.
- *T3.2.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the cognitive faculty — knowing, understanding, discerning — and if so, how?_
  → VCG06 (Luk 24:45): opening of the mind to disclosed content. VCG03 (1Ki 3:9): perceptive discernment in governance. Cognitive processes: opening, grasping, discerning.
- *T3.2.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair cognition in the person?_
  → M15-B operates at the grasping/perceiving level — the cognitive act of receiving and comprehending. It is the receptive-cognitive function.
- *T3.2.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with cognition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Both surface and depth: surface (VCG08 grasping meaning) and depth (VCG06 Christ opening the mind — the deepest opening of understanding).
- *T3.3.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the memory faculty — the holding and retrieving of inner-being reality across time — and if so, how?_
  → VCG06 (Luk 24:45 corpus): Christ enabling the disciples to understand what they had experienced and heard — memory of events and words now opened to comprehension.
- *T3.3.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair memory in the person?_
  → VCG05 (Heb 5:14): trained understanding held as a formed inner capacity — the result of accumulated practice stored as discernment-capacity.
- *T3.3.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with memory reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T3.4.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the affective faculty — feeling and emotional experience — and if so, how?_
  → VCG06 (Luk 24:45): the disciples' understanding opened → joy and worship follow (Luk 24:52-53). Understanding produces affective response.
- *T3.4.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair affect in the person?_
  → Understanding produces affect secondarily — understanding opened produces joy and worship (Luk 24:52-53).
- *T3.4.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with affect reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T3.6.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the volitional faculty — the capacity to choose — and if so, how?_
  → VCG05 (Heb 5:14): trained understanding requires volitional discipline in practice. VCG06 (Luk 24:45): opening of understanding is divine initiative, but the disciples' continued engagement with Scripture is volitional.
- *T3.6.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair volition in the person — including its three aspects: capacity, interaction with …_
  → Volitionally received (Heb 5:14 training); maintained (through sustained practice); and blocked (hardened hearts — M15-B VCG04 judicial withholding, which presupposes prior volitional hardening).
- *T3.7.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the agency faculty — the capacity to act, initiate, and make happen — and if so, how?_
  → VCG06 (Luk 24:45 → 24:46-49): understanding opened → the disciples are sent out. Understanding confers mission agency.
- *T3.7.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair agency in the person?_
  → Mission agency (Luk 24), communicative-teaching agency (Ne 8:8), governance agency (1Ki 3:9).
- *T3.7.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with agency reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Understanding's agency pattern (mission, teaching, governance) reveals it is a faculty in service of engagement, not an end in itself. Opening of understanding is always followed by movement outward — the opened-understanding person is sent.
- *T3.8.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the moral evaluation faculty — the capacity to assess against a standard of right, wrong, good, and true — a…_
  → VCG05 (Heb 5:14 aisthētērion): "discernment trained to distinguish good from evil" — the faculty of understanding trained for moral evaluation. Understanding is morally formative.
- *T3.8.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair moral evaluation in the person?_
  → Understanding acquires moral significance through direction and training. VCG05: trained discernment for moral distinction is the explicit moral engagement.
- *T3.8.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with moral evaluation reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Understanding's moral engagement is acquired through training (VCG05 Heb 5:14): understanding trained to distinguish good from evil is understanding morally directed. The pattern reveals understanding as morally neutral in itself but capable of moral formation — it becomes morally significant through disciplined direction.
- *T3.9.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the conscience — the acute inner witness of sin, guilt, and conviction — and if so, how?_
  → VCG05 (Heb 5:14 aisthētērion): the trained discernment for moral distinction is the developed conscience-function. Understanding trained for good/evil distinction is conscience in its trained form.
- *T3.9.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscience in the person?_
  → Heb 5:14 aisthētērion: trained understanding IS trained conscience — the ability to distinguish good from evil is the trained moral faculty.
- *T3.9.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscience reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Understanding's conscience engagement (trained aisthētērion, Heb 5:14) reveals understanding as the faculty that, when properly formed, becomes the conscience-capacity. Understanding is conscience in its cognitive-trained form.

<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch4 — T3 silences for Understanding as inner perceptive faculty -->

**T3 — The Inner Faculties**

- *T3.5.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the creative faculty — imagination and the capacity to originate — and if so, how?_
  → Understanding as perceptive faculty does not directly constitute creative capacity.
- *T3.5.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair creativity in the person?_
  → Understanding does not directly enable, deepen, bypass, or impair creativity in M15-B's evidence. Understanding grasps what is; creativity produces what is not yet. Silence confirmed.
- *T3.5.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with creativity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Understanding's silence on creativity reveals it as a receptive-perceptive faculty, not a generative one. Understanding grasps what exists; it does not produce what does not yet exist. The silence is definitional, not incidental.
- *T3.6.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with volition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → VCG01 (God's divine understanding) is silent on human volition.
<!-- /EVIDENCE -->

**T2 — Constitutional Location and Boundaries**

- *T2.1.4* — _If the evidence is silent on spirit-level location, note this explicitly._
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T2.10.1* — _Does this characteristic move across constitutional levels — from spirit to soul, from soul to body, or across boundaries in other direction…_
  → VCG03 (Jos 4:24 anchor): God's redemptive acts → historical knowledge → national-communal knowing. Movement: divine act → collective inner knowing. VCG04: human covenantal knowing moves toward God — human → God direction. VCG11: intimate knowing spans soul and body simultaneously.
- *T2.10.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about the sequence or pattern of that movement?_
  → Multiple patterns: divine self-disclosure → human knowing (redemptive-historical). Human seeking → received knowing (covenantal). Practical interaction → situational knowing (operational). The patterns are context-differentiated.
- *T2.10.3* — _If no constitutional movement is evidenced, note this explicitly._
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T2.2.1* — _Is this characteristic identified in the verse evidence as a soul-level phenomenon?_
  → Hos 6:3 (VCG04 anchor): the human relational knowing of God is an inner orientation (pressing on to know) — soul-level. Pro 1:7 (VCG06 anchor): knowledge as inner endowment — soul-level. Covenantal knowledge operates at the soul's orientation-level.
- *T2.2.2* — _What does soul-level location reveal about this characteristic's place in the innermost personal experience?_
  → Hos 6:3: covenantal knowledge at the soul level reveals it as a relational orientation that constitutes the person's innermost relationship to God. Soul-level knowing is not peripheral — it is the animating centre of the person's covenantal life.
- *T2.2.3* — _If the evidence is silent on soul-level location, note this explicitly._
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]

  → Hos 6:3 (VCG04 anchor): "press on to know the LORD" — the pressing on is a heart-orientation. Pro 1:7 (VCG06 anchor): the wise lay up knowledge — in Proverbs, the heart is the assumed site of inner endowments. The heart as site is not always named explicitly for knowledge but is consistently assumed in the wisdom-literature context.
- *T2.3.2* — _What does the heart-location reveal — what aspect of the heart's integrating function (knowing, willing, feeling, moral awareness) does this…_
  → Hos 6:3: the relational-covenantal knowing engages the heart's orientation function — the heart presses toward God. M15-C engages the heart as the relational-orientating faculty.
- *T2.3.3* — _If the evidence is silent on heart-location, note this explicitly._

  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]

  → VCG11 (Gen 4:1 anchor): ya.da in sexual knowing — the body as the whole person's intimate knowing. The body-knowledge link here is the most comprehensive in the cluster: intimate knowing involves the whole person including the body.

VCG04 (Hos 6:3): human covenantal knowing arises from pressing toward God — the human origin of knowing is oriented toward and dependent on the divine. VCG06 (Pro 1:7): knowledge begins with fear of the LORD — divine-covenantal origin.

- *T2.9.3* — _Does the origin of this characteristic change across different contexts evidenced in Scripture?_
  → Divine omniscient knowing (context: God's self-sufficient being). Covenantal knowing (context: covenant relationship). Practical knowing (context: everyday situational navigation). Intimate knowing (context: marital union). The origin varies radically by context — this is the most context-sensitive sub-group in the cluster regarding origin.

**T3 — The Inner Faculties**

- *T3.1.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the perceptive faculty — the inner senses including hearing, sight, taste, touch, smell, and spiritual disce…_
  → VCG01 (Psa 139:6): divine comprehensive perception. VCG04 (Hos 6:3): human pursuit-perception of God. VCG10 (Gen 12:11): practical situational perception. VCG11 (Gen 4:1): intimate personal perception. M15-C spans the full perceptive spectrum — widest range in the cluster.
- *T3.1.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair the perceptive faculty in the person?_
  → Both: ya.da names the act of knowing (perception as act) and the state of having known (knowledge as possession). The characteristic is perception-as-act and perception-as-product simultaneously.
- *T3.1.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with perception reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Widest perceptive range in M15: material (VCG10), relational (VCG04, VCG11), moral (VCG07), propositional (VCG08), divine-comprehensive (VCG01).
- *T3.10.1* — _Does this characteristic engage conscientiousness — the integrated response of moral awareness, volition, and action — and if so, how?_
  → VCG06 (Pro 10:14): "the wise lay up knowledge" — conscientious accumulation. VCG04 (Hos 6:3 "let us press on"): diligent pursuit.
- *T3.10.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscientiousness in the person?_
  → Knowledge enables conscientiousness through provision of content: knowing God's requirements (VCG04, VCG07) gives the conscientious person material to act upon. The accumulation of knowledge (VCG06) is itself a conscientious act. Knowledge whose moral content is grasped enables conscientiousness; knowledge held without moral engagement produces the person who knows but does not act.
- *T3.10.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscientiousness reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Knowledge's conscientiousness-engagement through content-provision reveals it as the moral-informational substrate of conscientiousness. The conscientious person acts on what they know; knowledge without conscientiousness remains inert.
- *T3.11.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the relational capacity — the constitutional equipment for genuine connection with another person — and if s…_
  → M15-C is constitutively relational at its covenantal core. VCG02 (Amos 3:2): divine knowing as election. VCG04 (Hos 6:3): human pursuing God. VCG11 (Gen 4:1): intimate knowing as deepest relational capacity.
- *T3.11.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair relational capacity in the person?_
  → Relational knowing IS M15-C's covenantal core. Ya.da is fundamentally relational knowing — not knowing-about but knowing-in-relationship.
- *T3.11.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with relational capacity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → M15-C has the greatest relational depth in the cluster: VCG11 (intimate union), VCG02 (divine elective knowing), VCG04 (covenantal pursuit). The relational depth ranges from electoral covenant to sexual intimacy — the full spectrum of relational knowing.
- *T3.2.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the cognitive faculty — knowing, understanding, discerning — and if so, how?_
  → VCG08 (Job 19:25): conviction-formation. VCG04 (Hos 6:3): pursuit-cognition. VCG06 (Pro 10:14): accumulation. VCG09 (Act 17:30): cognitive re-orientation through repentance.
- *T3.2.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair cognition in the person?_
  → M15-C operates at the knowing-integrating level: recognition, relationship, and conviction are integrated — not analysis-only but recognition-through-relationship.
- *T3.2.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with cognition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → M15-C spans surface (VCG10 practical recognition) to depth (VCG08 conviction through suffering, VCG01 divine comprehensive knowing). Strongly weighted toward depth.
- *T3.3.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the memory faculty — the holding and retrieving of inner-being reality across time — and if so, how?_
  → VCG03 (Exo 7:5; Jos 4:24): redemptive knowing is built on memorial acts. VCG06 (Pro 10:14): knowledge as stored inner content ("lay up"). Memory is both basis and product of M15-C knowing.
- *T3.3.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair memory in the person?_
  → VCG06 (Pro 10:14): "the wise lay up knowledge" explicitly describes organised inner holding of knowledge-content.
- *T3.3.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with memory reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T3.4.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the affective faculty — feeling and emotional experience — and if so, how?_
  → VCG04 (Hos 6:3): pressing on to know the Lord carries desire-orientation. VCG05 (1Sa 2:12): absence of knowing the Lord is paired with destructive behaviour — lacking knowing produces destructive affect-expression.
- *T3.4.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair affect in the person?_
  → Knowledge is primarily cognitive-relational; affect is its consequence.
- *T3.6.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the volitional faculty — the capacity to choose — and if so, how?_
  → VCG04 (Hos 6:3 "let us press on"): volitional pursuit. VCG05 (1Sa 2:12 — not knowing as chosen condition): volitional refusal. VCG06 (Pro 10:14 — "lay up"): volitional accumulation.
- *T3.6.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair volition in the person — including its three aspects: capacity, interaction with …_
  → All three: volitionally received (VCG04 pursuit), maintained (VCG06 "lay up"), refused (VCG05 chosen not-knowing).
- *T3.6.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with volition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → VCG01 and VCG02 (divine knowing) are silent on human volition.
- *T3.7.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the agency faculty — the capacity to act, initiate, and make happen — and if so, how?_
  → VCG08 (Job 19:25): conviction enables sustained advocacy through suffering. VCG04: knowing God orients the whole life. VCG10: practical knowing enables correct action.
- *T3.7.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair agency in the person?_
  → Advocacy agency through suffering (VCG08), covenantal life-orientation agency (VCG04), practical navigation agency (VCG10).
- *T3.7.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with agency reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Knowledge's agency pattern spans individual conviction-advocacy (VCG08) through practical situational action (VCG10) to life-orientation (VCG04). The width of the pattern reveals that knowledge is not merely cognitive possession but motivating orientation — it moves the person.
- *T3.8.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the moral evaluation faculty — the capacity to assess against a standard of right, wrong, good, and true — a…_
  → VCG07 (Gen 2:9): the tree of the knowledge of good and evil. VCG02 (Amos 3:2): God's elective knowing implies moral accountability.
- *T3.8.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair moral evaluation in the person?_
  → Mixed: VCG07 identifies constitutively moral knowing (good/evil). The broader corpus shows knowledge acquires moral significance through direction.
- *T3.8.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with moral evaluation reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Knowledge's moral engagement spans the full moral spectrum: constitutively moral (VCG07 good/evil knowledge), morally consequential (VCG02 elective knowing implies accountability), morally neutral (VCG10 practical knowing). The pattern reveals knowledge as a morally differentiated characteristic — its moral character depends on its object and mode.
- *T3.9.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the conscience — the acute inner witness of sin, guilt, and conviction — and if so, how?_
  → VCG08 (Job 19:25 — conviction of Redeemer): conscience-proximate conviction. VCG07 (moral knowing): the knowledge-base from which conscience draws its material.
- *T3.9.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscience in the person?_
  → M15-C supplies the content for conscience (moral knowledge VCG07) but is not conscience itself. The relationship: M15-C provides knowing-material; conscience uses it.
- *T3.9.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscience reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Knowledge's conscience-adjacency (providing moral knowing-content from which conscience draws) reveals it as the content-supplier to conscience, not conscience itself. M15-C and conscience are structurally related: knowledge provides what conscience uses.

  → Psa 73:16: discernment at the soul level is revealed as the inner process of working through what the person cannot immediately resolve. Soul-level discernment is the person in active engagement with difficult reality.

  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T2.4.1* — _Does the verse evidence locate this characteristic in the mind?_
  → G1252 diakrinō (VCG02 anchor: 1Cor 11:31): the inner discriminating act — the mind's evaluative function. G3053 logismos (VCG07 anchor: Rom 2:15): "cognitive argumentation" — the mind's deliberative function.
- *T2.4.2* — _What does mind-location reveal — what aspect of the mind's function (thought, discernment, understanding) does this characteristic engage?_
  → 1Cor 11:31 (diakrinō): evaluative discrimination — the mind's judging function. Rom 2:15 (logismos): argumentation — the mind's deliberative function.
- *T2.4.3* — _If the evidence is silent on mind-location, note this explicitly._
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T2.5.1* — _Does the verse evidence surface any soul-level location beyond heart and mind for this characteristic?_
  → VCG05 (Psa 34:8 anchor, H2938 ta.am): "taste and see that the LORD is good" — the palate as a figure for inner discernment. The tasting-faculty (sensory-experiential dimension of the soul) is engaged as the image for discernment. This is a unique soul-faculty reference within the cluster.
- *T2.5.2* — _If so, what is that location, and what does it reveal?_
  → Psa 34:8 (VCG05 anchor): the palate (ta.am — to taste/perceive) as figure for inner discernment reveals that discernment has an intuitive-sensory dimension within the soul — not merely analytical but also tasted/experienced. The palate-image extends the discernment faculty beyond pure cognition to include the dimension of experiential inner sensing. This is the closest M15 comes to engaging a non-cognitive soul faculty directly.
- *T2.5.3* — _If the evidence is silent, note this explicitly._
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T2.6.1* — _Does the verse evidence link this characteristic to a specific body part?_
  → VCG05 (Psa 34:8 anchor): ta.am — the palate as body-figure for inner discernment. The tongue/palate is the body-part image for the discernment faculty.
- *T2.6.2* — _If so, what is Scripture doing by making that link — is it emphatic, functional, expressive, indicative, or mediating?_
  → Psa 34:8: the palate-discernment link is figurative: "taste and see" invites the listener to use inner discernment as they would use physical tasting — direct, immediate, experiential. The body-part link is a teaching device that reveals that discernment has an experiential-intuitive dimension, not only an analytical one.
- *T2.6.3* — _If no body-part link is evidenced, note this explicitly._
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T2.7.1* — _Where a body-characteristic link exists, which direction does it run — does the soul express through the body, does the body feed back to th…_
  → VCG05 (Psa 34:8): the palate-image runs soul → body in its figurative direction: inner discernment is LIKE the palate's testing. The figure is descriptive, not a literal body-soul directional claim.

  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]

  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T2.9.1* — _Where does this characteristic originate constitutionally — is it generated from within the person, received from outside, bestowed by God, …_
  → VCG01 (Isa 52:13): sa.khal as an inner quality received from divine alignment with God's purposes. VCG06 (Gen 3:1): a.rum — the shrewd quality exists in the creature without a stated divine-gift origin; it appears as a constitutional creaturely capacity that can serve either direction. Mixed origins: some discernment is divinely-constituted, some appears creaturely-natural.
- *T2.9.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about whether the origin is singular or multiple?_
  → Two types: divinely-given effective prudence (VCG01) and creaturely-constitutional shrewd perceptiveness (VCG06). The origin question has two answers.

  → All show context-sensitive origin patterns consistent with the cluster's overall structure.

**T3 — The Inner Faculties**

- *T3.1.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the perceptive faculty — the inner senses including hearing, sight, taste, touch, smell, and spiritual disce…_
  → VCG05 (Job 12:11): the palate testing food as the model for inner discernment-perception. VCG01 (Isa 52:13 sa.khal): perceptive discernment of God's ways. M15-D IS a form of perception — discernment is constitutively perceptive.
- *T3.1.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair the perceptive faculty in the person?_
  → M15-D IS constitutively perceptive. Sa.khal, diakrinō, ta.am all name the discriminating perceptive act.
- *T3.1.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with perception reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Range: prudent-action perception (VCG01), self-evaluative perception (VCG02), gustatory-testing perception (VCG05). All directed at discriminating distinctions.
- *T3.10.1* — _Does this characteristic engage conscientiousness — the integrated response of moral awareness, volition, and action — and if so, how?_
  → VCG01 (sa.khal): sustained successful discernment implies conscientiousness. VCG06 (a.rum): the prudent person is consistently careful.
- *T3.10.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscientiousness in the person?_
  → Discernment enables and constitutes conscientiousness: the discerning person is by definition the one who does not act rashly but evaluates before acting. Sa.khal (VCG01) and a.rum (VCG06) both describe the person whose care in judgment IS conscientiousness in action. M15-D may be the closest inner-being characteristic to conscientiousness in its operational form.
- *T3.10.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscientiousness reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → M15-D's deep enabling of conscientiousness confirms it as the evaluation-faculty that makes conscientiousness operationally possible. Without discernment, conscientiousness has no method; with discernment, it has both motivation and means.
- *T3.11.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the relational capacity — the constitutional equipment for genuine connection with another person — and if s…_
  → VCG03 (Gen 15:6): divine crediting is relational — God's evaluative act directed toward Abraham in covenant. VCG06 (a.rum): the prudent person reads and manages relational contexts.
- *T3.11.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair relational capacity in the person?_
  → Relational context shapes discernment (VCG06 prudent person in social contexts) but M15-D is not constitutively relational in the way M15-C is.
- *T3.11.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with relational capacity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Discernment's relational depth is mediated through evaluation and judgment rather than knowing-in-relationship. The discerning person evaluates relationships; M15-C's knower enters them.
- *T3.2.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the cognitive faculty — knowing, understanding, discerning — and if so, how?_
  → VCG04 (Gen 38:15 cha.shav): assessment from observation. VCG07 (2Cor 10:4 logismos): cognitive argumentation/strongholds. VCG03 (Gen 15:6): divine imputing/crediting. Processes: assessment, discrimination, imputation, argumentation.
- *T3.2.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair cognition in the person?_
  → M15-D operates at the evaluative-cognitive level: forming assessments, making discriminations, reckoning weights.
- *T3.2.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with cognition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Depth cognition dominates: VCG03 (divine crediting), VCG07 (strongholds requiring divine weaponry). Surface cognition in VCG04 and VCG05.
- *T3.4.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the affective faculty — feeling and emotional experience — and if so, how?_
  → VCG02 (1Cor 11:31): self-discernment has affective consequence (examined person avoids judgment). VCG05 (Job 12:11 ta.am): gustatory image has affective overtones.
- *T3.4.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair affect in the person?_
  → Discernment is not constitutively affective; affect arises from the outcomes of discernment.
- *T3.6.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the volitional faculty — the capacity to choose — and if so, how?_
  → VCG01 (Isa 52:13): committed discerning-action. VCG02 (1Cor 11:31 "if we judged ourselves"): volitional self-examination.
- *T3.6.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair volition in the person — including its three aspects: capacity, interaction with …_
  → Volitionally exercised (VCG02 self-examination), sustained (VCG01 pattern of sa.khal), and blocked (VCG06 cunning misdirected — a.rum when directed wrongly).
- *T3.7.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the agency faculty — the capacity to act, initiate, and make happen — and if so, how?_
  → VCG01 (Isa 52:13): discernment enabling exaltation. VCG07 (2Cor 10:4): demolishing strongholds — spiritual warfare agency.
- *T3.7.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair agency in the person?_
  → Effective world-action agency (VCG01), spiritual warfare agency (VCG07), governance-judicial agency (VCG03).
- *T3.7.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with agency reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Discernment's agency is consistently effective: sa.khal produces success (VCG01), divine crediting produces righteous standing (VCG03), trained discernment produces moral life (VCG05). The pattern reveals discernment as an enabling characteristic — it is the inner evaluation that makes effective action possible.
- *T3.8.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the moral evaluation faculty — the capacity to assess against a standard of right, wrong, good, and true — a…_
  → M15-D is constitutively moral-evaluative: discriminating (VCG02), crediting (VCG03), thinking (VCG04) all involve moral evaluation. VCG03 (Gen 15:6): divine crediting of faith as righteousness is the paradigmatic moral-evaluative act.
- *T3.8.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair moral evaluation in the person?_
  → M15-D is constitutively moral-evaluative: the core function of discernment is making distinctions that carry moral weight.
- *T3.8.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with moral evaluation reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → M15-D is constitutively engaged with moral evaluation throughout — it IS an evaluative faculty. The pattern reveals discernment as the moral-evaluative sub-group of the cluster: every VCG involves discrimination that carries moral weight.
- *T3.9.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the conscience — the acute inner witness of sin, guilt, and conviction — and if so, how?_
  → M15-D is the sub-group most directly connected to conscience in M15. VCG02 (diakrinō, 1Cor 11:31): self-evaluation before God as conscience-function. VCG07 (logismos, Rom 2:15): "their thoughts meanwhile accusing or excusing them" — conscience explicitly.
- *T3.9.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscience in the person?_
  → M15-D functions as or alongside conscience most directly: VCG02 diakrinō self-examination and VCG07 logismos accusation/excuse are the conscience-functions of the cluster.
- *T3.9.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscience reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → M15-D's deep conscience engagement (self-examination, accusation/excuse logismos) reveals discernment as the conscience-proximate sub-group of the cluster. M15-D is as close as any M15 characteristic comes to being conscience itself, especially in its self-examination and logismos functions.

  → VCG05 (tasting-as-discernment) is more reflexive than volitional.

**Key verses for Discernment and practical judgment:**

**Isa 52:13** (H7919A sa.khal) [M15-D-VCG01]
> Isa 52:13 Behold , my servant shall act wisely ; he shall be high and lifted up , and shall be exalted .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "my servant shall act wisely; he shall be high and lifted up" — sa.khal as Servant-mission character

**1Cor 11:31** (G1252 diakrinō) [M15-D-VCG02]
> 1Cor 11:31 But if we judged ourselves truly, we would not be judged .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "if we judged ourselves truly, we would not be judged" — reflexive diakrinō; self-discernment

**Gen 15:6** (H2803H cha.shav) [M15-D-VCG03]
> Gen 15:6 And he believed the Lord , and he counted it to him as righteousness .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "counted it to him as righteousness" — God's inner act of moral reckoning; faith assessed and credited

**Psa 73:16** (H2803J cha.shav) [M15-D-VCG04]
> Psa 73:16 But when I thought how to understand this , it seemed to me a wearisome task,
_Meaning of the term here:_ "when I thought how to understand this, it seemed wearisome" — cha.shav as the sustained inner effort to make sense of a problem

**Psa 34:8** (H2938 ta.am) [M15-D-VCG05]
> Psa 34:8 Oh, taste and see that the Lord is good ! Blessed is the man who takes refuge in him !
_Meaning of the term here:_ "taste and see that the Lord is good" — ta.am as experiential inner apprehension; the invitation to direct inner experience of God's character

**Gen 3:1** (H6175 a.rum) [M15-D-VCG06]
> Gen 3:1 Now the serpent was more crafty than any other beast of the field that the Lord God had made . He said to the woman , “Did God actually say , ‘You shall not eat of any tree in the garden ’?”
_Meaning of the term here:_ "the serpent was more crafty" — a.rum in its dark register; the same shrewdness serving deception

**Rom 2:15** (G3053 logismos) [M15-D-VCG07]
> Rom 2:15 They show that the work of the law is written on their hearts , while their conscience also bears witness , and their conflicting thoughts accuse or even excuse them
_Meaning of the term here:_ "conflicting thoughts accuse or excuse" — logismos as moral inner reasoning functioning alongside conscience

**T3 — The Inner Faculties**

- *T3.1.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the perceptive faculty — the inner senses including hearing, sight, taste, touch, smell, and spiritual disce…_
  → VCG08 (Pro 6:6 pronoia): observation as the basis for purposive foresight. M15-E engages perception primarily as input to planning, not as its core function.
- *T3.1.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair the perceptive faculty in the person?_
  → M15-E uses perception as input but is itself a volitional-deliberative act, not a perceptive one.
- *T3.1.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with perception reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Perceptive range is secondary: observation feeds foresight (VCG08 ant). Other VCGs focus on the volitional-deliberative act.
- *T3.10.1* — _Does this characteristic engage conscientiousness — the integrated response of moral awareness, volition, and action — and if so, how?_
  → VCG08 (Pro 6:6 pronoia): observational and conscientious preparation (learn from the ant). VCG02: apostolic considered judgment is a conscientious exercise.
- *T3.10.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscientiousness in the person?_
  → Counsel enables and deepens conscientiousness: the person who plans deliberately (VCG05), who seeks wise input (VCG04), and who calibrates purpose to eschatological reality (VCG02) is the conscientious planner. Self-enclosed or rash purposing bypasses conscientiousness by substituting self-focus for careful deliberate purposing.
- *T3.10.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscientiousness reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → M15-E's conscientiousness-enabling through deliberate planning reveals purposive intent as the volitional dimension of conscientiousness. The conscientious person both evaluates (M15-D) and plans deliberately (M15-E) — the two sub-groups together constitute the evaluative-volitional structure of conscientious inner life.
- *T3.11.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the relational capacity — the constitutional equipment for genuine connection with another person — and if s…_
  → VCG04 (2Sa 16:23): the counseling relationship as primary relational interface. VCG03: divine counsel as the basis of the God-human governance relationship.
- *T3.11.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair relational capacity in the person?_
  → The counselor-counselee relationship is the characteristic relational form of purposive counsel (VCG04).
- *T3.11.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with relational capacity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Governance-relational depth: structured by authority and wisdom (VCG04 — the counselor-king relationship), not covenantal intimacy.
- *T3.2.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the cognitive faculty — knowing, understanding, discerning — and if so, how?_
  → VCG05 (Pro 16:9 cha.shav): inner cognitive devising. VCG02 (gnōmē, 1Cor 7:25): deliberate considered judgment. VCG06 (za.mam, Gen 11:6): unified purposing.
- *T3.2.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair cognition in the person?_
  → M15-E operates at the deliberative-cognitive level: forming plans, resolving purposes, devising strategies. Prospective cognition.
- *T3.2.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with cognition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Depth: VCG03 (divine irresistible purpose), VCG06 (irrevocable human unified purpose). All three core VCGs involve deep-formed purposing.
- *T3.3.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the memory faculty — the holding and retrieving of inner-being reality across time — and if so, how?_
  → VCG08 (Pro 6:6 pronoia): the ant provides a memory-pattern. Planning draws on accumulated wisdom-content (M15-A/C). Memory provides the stock from which purposes are formed.
- *T3.4.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the affective faculty — feeling and emotional experience — and if so, how?_
  → VCG01 (Matt 1:19 boulomai): Joseph's resolution reflects compassion alongside purpose. VCG07 (Exo 7:23): Pharaoh's refusal to attend is affect-charged (hardness).
- *T3.4.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair affect in the person?_
  → Purposive intent is primarily volitional-cognitive; affect provides colour to the purposing.
- *T3.5.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the creative faculty — imagination and the capacity to originate — and if so, how?_
  → VCG05 (Pro 16:9 cha.shav devising): the heart devising its way is the inner creative-planning act. M15-E is the closest the cluster comes to inner creativity in its planning/devising mode.
- *T3.5.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair creativity in the person?_
  → VCG05 (Pro 16:9 cha.shav — the heart devising its way): the devising function of purposive intent is the closest M15-E comes to enabling creativity — the inner cognitive planning act that conceives something not yet in existence. M15-E enables a form of generative inner purposing.
- *T3.5.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with creativity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → M15-E's partial engagement with creativity (through the devising function of cha.shav) reveals purposive intent as the sub-group where inner life moves closest to creative generation — conceiving what does not yet exist in order to direct action toward it.
- *T3.6.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the volitional faculty — the capacity to choose — and if so, how?_
  → M15-E is the most volitionally characterised sub-group. VCG01 (boulomai): will/deliberate intention. VCG05: the heart planning ITS way. VCG06 (za.mam): unified volitional purposing.
- *T3.6.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair volition in the person — including its three aspects: capacity, interaction with …_
  → Volitionally formed (VCG05 heart plans), maintained (VCG02 considered judgment held), and refused (VCG04 — counsel rejected, as when David ignored Ahithophel later through Hushai's counter-counsel).
- *T3.6.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with volition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → VCG08 (pronoia — foresight) is more cognitive than volitional.
- *T3.7.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the agency faculty — the capacity to act, initiate, and make happen — and if so, how?_
  → M15-E is pre-eminently an agency sub-group. VCG03: divine agency expressed through irresistible purpose. VCG05 (Pro 16:9): human heart planning produces action.
- *T3.7.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair agency in the person?_
  → Divine sovereign agency (VCG03), governance-counseling agency (VCG04), personal purposive life-direction agency (VCG05), collective purposing agency (VCG06).
- *T3.7.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with agency reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → M15-E's agency is the most explicit in the cluster: every VCG moves toward action. The pattern reveals purposive intent as a constitutively action-directed characteristic — it is not possible to have genuine counsel/purpose that does not produce directed action (or, in God's case, historical outcome).
- *T3.8.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the moral evaluation faculty — the capacity to assess against a standard of right, wrong, good, and true — a…_
  → VCG05 includes both good devising (Pro 16:9) and evil devising (Mic 2:1). VCG03: divine sovereign purpose is the moral ground against which all human counsel is measured.
- *T3.8.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair moral evaluation in the person?_
  → M15-E is not constitutively moral-evaluative. Purposive planning is moral when directed rightly, immoral when directed against God or neighbour.
- *T3.8.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with moral evaluation reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → M15-E's moral engagement is mixed: VCG03 (divine counsel) is the moral absolute; VCG05 can be directed toward good or evil devising. The pattern reveals purposive intent as morally directional — it takes on the moral character of what it purposes toward.
- *T3.9.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the conscience — the acute inner witness of sin, guilt, and conviction — and if so, how?_
  → VCG07 (Exo 7:23 inverse): Pharaoh's deliberate refusal to attend to God's signs is conscience-adjacent — the faculty of inward attention deliberately closed.

  → VCG03, VCG05, VCG06, VCG08 are silent on affective engagement.

- *T3.9.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscience reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → The near-silence of conscience in M15-E reveals that purposive intent is not constitutively conscience-engaged. M15-E is a volitional-deliberative characteristic that operates largely independently of conscience-function — conscience constrains or enables the purposing but is not its defining faculty.

**2Pe 3:9** (G1014 boulomai) [M15-E-VCG01]
> 2Pe 3:9 The Lord is not slow to fulfill his promise as some count slowness , but is patient toward you , not wishing that any should perish , but that all should reach repentance .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "not wishing that any should perish, but that all should reach repentance" — divine salvific desire

**Rev 17:17** (G1106 gnōmē) [M15-E-VCG02]
> Rev 17:17 for God has put it into their hearts to carry out his purpose by being of one mind and handing over their royal power to the beast , until the words of God are fulfilled .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "God has put it into their hearts to carry out his purpose... until the words of God are fulfilled" — gnōmē divinely placed; human deliberate purpose as instrument of divine sovereignty

**Isa 14:24** (H3289 ya.ats) [M15-E-VCG03]
> Isa 14:24 The Lord of hosts has sworn : “ As I have planned , so shall it be, and as I have purposed , so shall it stand ,
_Meaning of the term here:_ "as I have planned, so shall it be; as I have purposed, so shall it stand"

**2Sa 16:23** (H3289 ya.ats) [M15-E-VCG04]
> 2Sa 16:23 Now in those days the counsel that Ahithophel gave was as if one consulted the word of God ; so was all the counsel of Ahithophel esteemed, both by David and by Absalom .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "counsel of Ahithophel as if one consulted the word of God"

**Jer 29:11** (H2803I cha.shav) [M15-E-VCG05]
> Jer 29:11 For I know the plans I have for you, declares the Lord , plans for welfare and not for evil , to give you a future and a hope .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "plans for welfare and not for evil, to give you a future and a hope"

**Lam 2:17** (H2161 za.mam) [M15-E-VCG06]
> Lam 2:17 The Lord has done what he purposed ; he has carried out his word , which he commanded long ago ; he has thrown down without pity ; he has made the enemy rejoice over you and exalted the might of your foes .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "the Lord has done what he purposed" — divine za.mam fulfilled in Jerusalem's fall

**Exo 7:23** (H7896K shit) [M15-E-VCG07]
> Exo 7:23 Pharaoh turned and went into his house , and he did not take even this to heart .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "he did not take even this to heart" — shit-refusal; heart closed to what should have registered

**Rom 13:14** (G4307 pronoia) [M15-E-VCG08]
> Rom 13:14 But put on the Lord Jesus Christ , and make no provision for the flesh , to gratify its desires .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "make no provision for the flesh, to gratify its desires" — pronoia as forward-provision planning; here refused toward the flesh
