**T3 — The Inner Faculties**

- *T3.1.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the perceptive faculty — the inner senses including hearing, sight, taste, touch, smell, and spiritual disce…_
  → VCG04 (Dan 7:28 se.khal): focused contemplative attention on received content. VCG02 (Matt 1:20 enthumeomai): reflective perception of a complex situation. M15-F is second-order perception — dwelling on what has already been perceived.
- *T3.1.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair the perceptive faculty in the person?_
  → M15-F uses received perception as its material but is itself a dwelling activity, not a new perceptive act.
- *T3.1.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with perception reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Range: inward (VCG04 Daniel's vision), retrospective (VCG02 Joseph), receptive (VCG03 God's law). All directed at received content.
- *T3.10.1* — _Does this characteristic engage conscientiousness — the integrated response of moral awareness, volition, and action — and if so, how?_
  → VCG03 (Psa 119:97 "all the day"): sustained meditative return is quintessential conscientiousness.
- *T3.10.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscientiousness in the person?_
  → Meditation deepens conscientiousness: sustained "all the day" engagement with God's law (VCG03) is the discipline of the conscientious person. Meditation sustains the inner attention that conscientiousness requires. The perversion of meditation (VCG01 self-enclosed monologue) bypasses conscientiousness by substituting self-focus for God-directed attention.
- *T3.10.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscientiousness reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → M15-F's deepening of conscientiousness through sustained practice reveals meditation as the inner discipline that sustains conscientiousness over time. Conscientiousness can be momentarily present in any person; meditation is what makes it habitual and deep.
- *T3.11.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the relational capacity — the constitutional equipment for genuine connection with another person — and if s…_
  → VCG03 (Psa 119:97): meditation on God's law is a relational act — directed toward God in love.
- *T3.11.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair relational capacity in the person?_
  → God-directed meditation is M15-F's relational mode (VCG03).
- *T3.11.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with relational capacity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Positive relational form: meditation-toward-God in love (VCG03). Negative form: self-enclosed deliberation (VCG01).
- *T3.2.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the cognitive faculty — knowing, understanding, discerning — and if so, how?_
  → VCG01 (Luk 12:17 dialogizomai): interior monologue. VCG03 (Psa 119:97 si.ach): sustained meditative dwelling. VCG02 (Matt 1:20 enthumeomai): structured reflection.
- *T3.2.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair cognition in the person?_
  → M15-F operates at the dwelling-cognitive level: sustained recycling attention to held content.
- *T3.2.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with cognition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Depth in VCG03 (Psa 119 — day-long dwelling that deepens love and understanding). Surface in VCG01 (self-deliberative inner monologue).
- *T3.3.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the memory faculty — the holding and retrieving of inner-being reality across time — and if so, how?_
  → VCG03 (Psa 119:97): meditation is sustained return to received content — memory holds what meditation dwells upon. Meditation is memory-in-motion.
- *T3.3.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair memory in the person?_
  → VCG03: the meditated content (God's law, his acts) is held in inner memory as the basis of sustained dwelling.
- *T3.3.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with memory reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T3.4.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the affective faculty — feeling and emotional experience — and if so, how?_
  → VCG03 (Psa 119:97): "Oh how I love your law!" — meditation is saturated with affective love. VCG04 (Dan 7:28): keeping the vision in heart despite fear — affect as the context of meditative holding.
- *T3.4.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair affect in the person?_
  → M15-F is constitutively affect-engaged at its richest (VCG03 — meditation deepens love). This is distinctive: M15-F is the sub-group where cognition and affect are most interwoven.
- *T3.4.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with affect reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T3.6.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the volitional faculty — the capacity to choose — and if so, how?_
  → VCG03 (Psa 119:97 "all the day"): volitional commitment to sustained return. VCG04 (Dan 7:28): volitional holding of the vision in heart.
- *T3.6.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair volition in the person — including its three aspects: capacity, interaction with …_
  → Volitionally sustained (VCG03 "all the day"). VCG01 deliberative self-monologue is partly involuntary (anxiety-driven).
- *T3.6.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with volition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T3.7.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the agency faculty — the capacity to act, initiate, and make happen — and if so, how?_
  → VCG03 (Psa 119:99): meditation produces understanding that exceeds teachers — cognitive-practical agency. VCG01 (Luk 12:17 inverse): self-enclosed deliberation produces defective agency (the rich fool).
- *T3.7.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair agency in the person?_
  → Cognitive-practical wisdom agency (VCG03), appropriate response to revelation agency (VCG04).
- *T3.7.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with agency reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Meditation's agency pattern is indirect: VCG03 produces wisdom that confers agency; VCG04 produces appropriate response to revelation. The pattern reveals M15-F as an enabling rather than directly agentive characteristic — it deepens the capacities that then produce agency.
- *T3.8.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the moral evaluation faculty — the capacity to assess against a standard of right, wrong, good, and true — a…_
  → VCG01 (dialogismos, Rom 1:21): futile/corrupt inner reasoning as the morally-evaluated negative form. VCG03: meditation on God's law is explicitly sanctifying.
- *T3.8.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair moral evaluation in the person?_
  → M15-F is morally neutral in form; morally weighted by its object and direction (God-directed vs self-enclosed).
- *T3.8.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with moral evaluation reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → M15-F's moral engagement is object-dependent: meditation on God's law is morally formative (VCG03); self-enclosed deliberation is morally problematic (VCG01 negative). The pattern reveals M15-F as morally neutral in form, morally shaped by direction — identical structural activity produces opposite moral outcomes depending on orientation.
- *T3.9.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the conscience — the acute inner witness of sin, guilt, and conviction — and if so, how?_
  → VCG02 (Matt 1:20 enthumeomai): Joseph's morally complex situation worked through in reflection — conscience-engaged inner state. VCG01 (dialogismos, Rom 2:15): the accusation/excuse dynamics.
- *T3.9.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscience in the person?_
  → VCG02 and VCG01 (negative) both overlap with conscience-function: the inner deliberation that weighs moral complexity.
- *T3.9.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscience reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → M15-F's secondary conscience engagement reveals the meditative mode as the form conscience takes when working through complex situations. Conscience meditates when it cannot resolve immediately.

**T3 — The Inner Faculties**

- *T3.5.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the creative faculty — imagination and the capacity to originate — and if so, how?_
  → M15-F is receptive-dwelling, not creative producing.
- *T3.5.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair creativity in the person?_
  → M15-F is receptive-dwelling, not generative. Silence confirmed.
- *T3.5.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with creativity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → M15-F's silence on creativity reveals meditation as a receptive-sustaining activity. The meditative person dwells on what has been given; they do not generate new content in the meditative act.

_Meaning of the term here:_ 'discerning the thoughts and intentions of the heart' — enthumesis (arising) paired with and distinguished from ennoia (held)

_Meaning of the term here:_ 'I considered the horns' — se.khal as sustained inner contemplation of the visionary scene; distinct from wisdom/prudence uses in M15-A


### 4.7 Inner thought-content — the mind's formed thoughts

<!-- AI WRITE: Chapter 4 §4.7 (Inner thought-content — the mind's formed thoughts)
     LENGTH: ~800-1500 words per characteristic
     FOCUS: Write a deep-dive on where in the inner person this characteristic sits (heart, mind, will, conscience, soul, spirit, faculty, body) and which inner capacities it engages (perception, thought, memory, feeling, conscience, will, agency). **T3 — The Inner Faculties**

- *T3.1.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the perceptive faculty — the inner senses including hearing, sight, taste, touch, smell, and spiritual disce…_
  → VCG01 (2Cor 4:4 noēma): blinding targets thought-content (the output of perception), not the perceptive act. M15-G is the content produced by perception, not the perceptive activity.
- *T3.1.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair the perceptive faculty in the person?_
  → M15-G is the content produced by perception — the outcome, not the activity.
- *T3.10.1* — _Does this characteristic engage conscientiousness — the integrated response of moral awareness, volition, and action — and if so, how?_
  → VCG01 (2Cor 10:5): disciplined management of thought-content requires sustained conscientious attention.
- *T3.10.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscientiousness in the person?_
  → Governing thought-content enables conscientiousness: the discipline of taking every thought captive (VCG01 2Cor 10:5) is the inner discipline from which conscientious outer action grows. Ungoverned thought-content (VCG01 blinded noēmata) impairs conscientiousness by distorting the cognitive substrate from which careful engagement arises.
- *T3.10.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscientiousness reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → M15-G's role (enabling conscientiousness through governed thought-content, impairing it through ungoverned thought) reveals thought-content as the inner substrate that determines the quality of the conscientious person's outer life. Inner discipline precedes outer discipline.
- *T3.11.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the relational capacity — the constitutional equipment for genuine connection with another person — and if s…_
  → VCG01 (2Cor 4:4): blinded noēmata prevent the person from seeing the glory of Christ — relational consequence of captured thought-content.
- *T3.11.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair relational capacity in the person?_
  → Relational function mediated through the content's moral orientation.
- *T3.11.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with relational capacity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Relational depth mediated entirely through content's moral orientation.
- *T3.2.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the cognitive faculty — knowing, understanding, discerning — and if so, how?_
  → VCG01 (2Cor 4:4 noēma): formed cognitive content as target of spiritual warfare. VCG02 (Dan 4:5 ra.yon): spontaneous thought-content arising from inner states.
- *T3.2.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair cognition in the person?_
  → M15-G is the content-holding register: the storage and output level of cognition.
- *T3.2.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with cognition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Depth: VCG01 (noēma as strongholds — entrenched cognitive structures). VCG02 (alarming thoughts disturbing the whole person).
- *T3.3.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the memory faculty — the holding and retrieving of inner-being reality across time — and if so, how?_
  → VCG02 (Dan 4:5): Nebuchadnezzar's dream-thoughts and troubled memory of them. VCG01 (noēmata as strongholds): entrenched long-term cognitive content.
- *T3.3.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair memory in the person?_
  → VCG01 (noēmata as persistent strongholds): the thought-content is stored and entrenched — it does not dissipate but persists as structured inner content.
- *T3.3.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with memory reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T3.4.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the affective faculty — feeling and emotional experience — and if so, how?_
  → VCG02 (Dan 4:5): alarming thoughts produce affective disturbance. VCG01 (noēma blinded): thought-content determines affective orientation.
- *T3.4.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair affect in the person?_
  → M15-G is deeply affect-linked: thought-content produces or is produced by affective states (VCG02 — fear generates alarming thoughts; thoughts generate more fear). The relationship is bidirectional.
- *T3.6.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the volitional faculty — the capacity to choose — and if so, how?_
  → VCG01 (2Cor 10:5): "take every thought captive" — volitional management of thought-content required.
- *T3.6.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair volition in the person — including its three aspects: capacity, interaction with …_
  → Volitional capture required (VCG01 2Cor 10:5); VCG02 dream-thoughts arising non-volitionally.
- *T3.6.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with volition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T3.7.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the agency faculty — the capacity to act, initiate, and make happen — and if so, how?_
  → VCG01 (2Cor 10:5): taking thoughts captive is spiritual warfare agency. VCG03 (2Chr 1:10): God-given knowledge enables governance agency.
- *T3.7.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair agency in the person?_
  → Spiritual warfare agency (VCG01 taking captive), governance agency (VCG03 knowledge enabling leadership).
- *T3.7.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with agency reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → The agency pattern in M15-G is contested: VCG01 (blinded noēmata) produces absence of agency toward God; VCG01 (captured thoughts) produces spiritual warfare agency; VCG03 produces governance agency. The pattern reveals thought-content as a precondition of agency whose quality determines the quality of the agency it enables.
- *T3.8.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the moral evaluation faculty — the capacity to assess against a standard of right, wrong, good, and true — a…_
  → VCG01 (noēma): blinded minds produce inability to see the gospel — moral-spiritual consequence of captured thought-content. VCG01 (2Cor 10:5): taking thoughts captive to obey Christ is the moral discipline of the inner cognitive domain.
- *T3.8.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair moral evaluation in the person?_
  → M15-G is morally significant through content: the noēmata are either aligned with the knowledge of God or opposed to it.
- *T3.8.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with moral evaluation reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → M15-G's moral engagement is through content quality: blinded noēmata produce moral blindness; Christ-aligned thought-content produces moral obedience (2Cor 10:5). The pattern reveals thought-content as morally determinative at the inner level — the thought precedes the moral act.
- *T3.9.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the conscience — the acute inner witness of sin, guilt, and conviction — and if so, how?_
  → VCG01 (noēma) provides the content-register from which conscience draws; VCG01 (G1963 epinoia): thought/purpose potentially opposing divine ordering.
- *T3.9.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscience reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → M15-G's silence on conscience as a named function reveals that thought-content is the substrate of conscience rather than its operation. Conscience uses thought-content; thought-content does not constitute conscience.

**Key verses for Inner thought-content — the mind's formed thoughts:**

**2Cor 4:4** (G3540 noēma) [M15-G-VCG01]
> 2Cor 4:4 In their case the god of this world has blinded the minds of the unbelievers , to keep them from seeing the light of the gospel of the glory of Christ , who is the image of God .
_Meaning of the term here:_ 'the god of this world has blinded the minds of the unbelievers' — noema as what is spiritually blinded; the inner formed thought-content that cannot see the gospel

**Psa 139:17** (H7454 re.a) [M15-G-VCG02]
> Psa 139:17 How precious to me are your thoughts , O God ! How vast is the sum of them!
_Meaning of the term here:_ 'How precious to me are your thoughts, O God! How vast is the sum of them!' — re.a of God's thoughts toward the human; the same term now runs in the opposite direction; reciprocal

**2Ch 1:11** (H4093 mad.da) [M15-G-VCG03]
> 2Ch 1:11 God answered Solomon , “ Because this was in your heart , and you have not asked for possessions , wealth , honor , or the life of those who hate you, and have not even asked for long life , but have asked for wisdom and knowledge for yourself that you may govern my people over whom I have made you king ,
_Meaning of the term here:_ 'Because this was in your heart... you have asked for wisdom and knowledge' — heart named; the knowing is heart-located

  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T2.10.1* — _Does this characteristic move across constitutional levels — from spirit to soul, from soul to body, or across boundaries in other direction…_
  → VCG01 (Col 3:16): divine word → inner person (movement: outside → inside). VCG02 (1Cor 14:19): inner word → spoken word → community formation (movement: inside → outside → communal).
- *T2.10.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about the sequence or pattern of that movement?_
  → Pattern: divine word given → received into inner person → expressed outward through speech and community formation. The logos completes the cycle: given → held → expressed → community shaped.
- *T2.10.3* — _If no constitutional movement is evidenced, note this explicitly._
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T2.2.1* — _Is this characteristic identified in the verse evidence as a soul-level phenomenon?_
  → Col 3:16 (VCG01 anchor): "dwell in you richly" — the word dwells within the person at the inner-life level = soul-level engagement. The logos as inner phenomenon is soul-located.
- *T2.2.2* — _What does soul-level location reveal about this characteristic's place in the innermost personal experience?_
  → Col 3:16: the word dwelling "richly" at the soul level reveals that the logos-engagement characteristic is not a surface phenomenon — it constitutes the inner life at its deepest accessible register.
- *T2.2.3* — _If the evidence is silent on soul-level location, note this explicitly._
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T2.3.1* — _Does the verse evidence locate this characteristic in the heart?_
  → Col 3:16 (VCG01 anchor): "with thankfulness in your hearts to God" — the word's dwelling produces heart-engagement. The logos addresses the heart.
- *T2.3.2* — _What does the heart-location reveal — what aspect of the heart's integrating function (knowing, willing, feeling, moral awareness) does this…_
  → Col 3:16: the heart responds with thankfulness to the word's dwelling. M15-H engages the heart's receiving and responding function — the heart as the site where the word takes up residence.
- *T2.3.3* — _If the evidence is silent on heart-location, note this explicitly._

  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]

  → Soul → body direction for expression (inner word → spoken word through mouth). Body → soul direction for reception (spoken word through ear → inner reception). Bidirectional.
- *T2.7.2* — _What is the consequence of that directionality for understanding the characteristic?_
  → The bidirectionality of logos reveals it as the central communicative characteristic of the cluster: it is both received (word enters through hearing → inner dwelling) and expressed (inner word → spoken word → community formation). The logos is the characteristic that most completely spans the receiving-and-expressing arc.

  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]

  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]

  → VCG01 (Col 3:16): "the word of Christ" — divine origin. VCG02 (1Cor 14:19): human speech originating from the mind. Bidirectional origin: divine word given, human word produced.

**T3 — The Inner Faculties**

- *T3.1.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the perceptive faculty — the inner senses including hearing, sight, taste, touch, smell, and spiritual disce…_
  → VCG01 (1Cor 1:18): the logos reveals the state of the hearer's inner perceptive capacity — the same word is perceived as folly or power depending on inner state. M15-H is a diagnostic of perception, not itself perception.
- *T3.1.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair the perceptive faculty in the person?_
  → M15-H is a revelatory instrument — it produces perception (or reveals its absence) but is not itself a perceptive faculty.
- *T3.1.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with perception reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → Range is differentiated by the inner condition of the perceiver: the same logos perceived as folly or power (VCG01).
- *T3.10.1* — _Does this characteristic engage conscientiousness — the integrated response of moral awareness, volition, and action — and if so, how?_
  → VCG01 (Col 3:16 "richly"): conscientious reception. VCG02 (Col 4:6 "always"): conscientious speech discipline.
- *T3.10.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscientiousness in the person?_
  → The logos deepens conscientiousness in reception (Col 3:16 "let it dwell richly" — volitional, sustained, open receiving) and expression (Col 4:6 "always gracious" — disciplined, caring speech). M15-H's conscientiousness is the word carefully received and carefully given.
- *T3.10.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscientiousness reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → M15-H's conscientiousness-engagement in both reception and expression reveals it as the characteristic whose practice requires sustained, caring attention in both directions. The logos is never casually received or casually given in the conscientious person's life.
- *T3.11.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the relational capacity — the constitutional equipment for genuine connection with another person — and if s…_
  → M15-H is constitutively relational: the logos is always in motion between persons (VCG01 Col 3:16 mutual teaching; VCG02 gracious speech shaped for the other).
- *T3.11.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair relational capacity in the person?_
  → M15-H is constitutively relational — the logos is by nature communicative, requiring a sender and receiver.
- *T3.11.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with relational capacity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → M15-H's relational depth: the highest form is divine word entering the human inner person (VCG01 Col 3:16 — divine-human relational depth through the logos); the human form is gracious speech shaped for the other (VCG02).
- *T3.2.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the cognitive faculty — knowing, understanding, discerning — and if so, how?_
  → VCG01 (1Cor 1:18): the logos disrupts and reorients cognitive categories. VCG03 (Gal 5:14): cognitive compression — the whole law held in one principle.
- *T3.2.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair cognition in the person?_
  → M15-H operates at the transformative-cognitive level: the logos disrupts and reorients.
- *T3.2.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with cognition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → VCG01: depth cognitive transformation — the word of the cross reshapes the deepest cognitive frameworks.
- *T3.3.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the memory faculty — the holding and retrieving of inner-being reality across time — and if so, how?_
  → Col 3:16: "let the word of Christ dwell in you richly" — the logos held in memory and inner possession as its transforming medium.
- *T3.3.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair memory in the person?_
  → Col 3:16: "dwell in you richly" — the logos is stored and accumulated in the inner person as a rich inner holding.
- *T3.3.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with memory reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T3.4.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the affective faculty — feeling and emotional experience — and if so, how?_
  → VCG01 (1Cor 1:18): the logos produces power-response (for the saved) or offence (for those perishing). VCG02 (Col 4:6): gracious speech as an affective discipline.
- *T3.4.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair affect in the person?_
  → M15-H is not constitutively affective, but its reception and expression carry affective loading.
- *T3.4.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with affect reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T3.5.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the creative faculty — imagination and the capacity to originate — and if so, how?_
  → VCG02 (Col 4:6): gracious speech requires creative shaping — finding the right form for each person and context.
- *T3.5.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair creativity in the person?_
  → VCG02 (Col 4:6 — gracious speech seasoned with salt): the communicated word requires creative shaping — finding the right form for each person and context is a creative act. M15-H enables communicative creativity.
- *T3.5.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with creativity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → M15-H's engagement with creative shaping (gracious speech requiring creative form) reveals it as the characteristic where creativity most naturally appears in the expression direction. The logos must be shaped creatively for each communicative context.
- *T3.6.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the volitional faculty — the capacity to choose — and if so, how?_
  → VCG01 (Col 3:16 "let the word dwell"): volitional receiving and holding. VCG02 (Col 4:6 "let your speech be"): volitional discipline in expression.
- *T3.6.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair volition in the person — including its three aspects: capacity, interaction with …_
  → Volitionally received (VCG01 "let it dwell") and volitionally expressed (VCG02 "let your speech be").
- *T3.6.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with volition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T3.7.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the agency faculty — the capacity to act, initiate, and make happen — and if so, how?_
  → VCG02 (Col 4:6): gracious speech as communicative agency. VCG01 (1Cor 14:19): intelligible speech that reaches the inner person.
- *T3.7.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair agency in the person?_
  → Communicative-formative agency (VCG02), community-building agency (VCG01 Col 3:16).
- *T3.7.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with agency reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → The logos's agency pattern is consistently communal-formative: VCG02 (gracious speech) builds the other; VCG01 (Col 3:16) forms and sustains community. The pattern reveals M15-H as the characteristic whose agency is always directed toward others — logos agency is relational, not individual.
- *T3.8.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the moral evaluation faculty — the capacity to assess against a standard of right, wrong, good, and true — a…_
  → VCG03 (Gal 5:14): the logos as the single moral principle summarising the law. VCG02: gracious vs harmful speech — the logos is morally evaluated by its effect.
- *T3.8.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair moral evaluation in the person?_
  → VCG01 (Jn 15:3): the logos as morally purifying. VCG03: logos as moral principle. M15-H is morally significant throughout but not uniformly in a single direction — the logos both purifies and convicts.
- *T3.8.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with moral evaluation reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → M15-H's moral engagement is multiform: logos as moral principle (VCG03 Gal 5:14), logos as moral purifier (VCG01 Jn 15:3), logos as morally evaluated in expression (VCG02). The pattern reveals M15-H as morally active throughout — the word is never morally neutral, always morally effective in one direction or another.
- *T3.9.1* — _Does this characteristic engage the conscience — the acute inner witness of sin, guilt, and conviction — and if so, how?_
  → The logos penetrates to conscience level (Heb 4:12 corpus — logos discerning the thoughts and intentions of the heart).
- *T3.9.2* — _Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscience in the person?_
  → The logos reaches conscience through the word's penetrating, discerning function (Heb 4:12 corpus).
- *T3.9.3* — _What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscience reveal about the nature of this characteristic?_
  → M15-H's conscience engagement through the word's penetrating function reveals M15-H as the characteristic that can reach conscience from outside. The logos is the external word that cuts to the conscience-level — the one characteristic in M15 that reaches conscience directly from without.

### 5.1 Wisdom as holistic inner character and orientation

<!-- AI WRITE: Chapter 5 §5.1 (Wisdom as holistic inner character and orientation)
     LENGTH: ~800-1500 words per characteristic
     FOCUS: Write on how this characteristic moves — between God and the human person, between persons, in covenant, against opposition — and how it is formed, deepens, is tested, is transformed across time. Use the evidence below.
     CITE (must quote at least 2 verbatim): Dan 2:20; Jam 1:5; Pro 16:23; Rom 8:5

<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch5 — T4 findings for Wisdom as holistic inner character and orientation -->

**T4 — Relational Interfaces**

- *T4.1.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating from God toward the human person — and if so, how?_
  → VCG02 (1Ki 3:12 — wisdom given to Solomon; Exo 31:3 — Spirit filling craftsmen with wisdom): God places wisdom into specific persons as a divine act. VCG01 (Prov 8 — wisdom as God's attribute): the divine wisdom is the pattern that human wisdom images.
- *T4.1.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about the basis on which God extends this characteristic — is it conditional, unconditional, covenantal, or re…_
  → VCG02: divine initiative in response to human request (Solomon's prayer) or divine sovereign bestowing (Bezalel, Spirit-filling). Both modes are present.
- *T4.1.3* — _What does God's extension of this characteristic reveal about his disposition toward the human person?_
  → VCG02 (1Ki 3:12): Solomon's wisdom enables governance excellence. VCG10 (Exo 36:1): craftsmen enabled for creative construction.
- *T4.2.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in the human person's movement toward God — in seeking, supplication, worship, or…_
  → VCG04 (froneō, Rom 8:5-8): setting the mind on the Spirit — wisdom-orientation directed toward God as its fundamental human-to-God movement.
- *T4.2.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about the inner posture required for this movement?_
  → VCG04: the prior Spirit-direction that sets the mind's orientation toward God. Wisdom-toward-God requires the Spirit's prior work of orientation.
- *T4.2.3* — _What does the human-to-God direction of this characteristic reveal about the person's relationship with God?_
  → The wisdom-orientation directed toward God (froneō Spirit, VCG04) reveals the human-divine relationship as one of orientation: the person's inner directional constitution is either aligned with God or against him. Wisdom-toward-God reveals that the relationship is constitutive of the person's deepest inner character — not a transactional posture but an orientation of the whole self.
- *T4.3.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic being extended by one person toward another — and if so, how does it operate in that giving…_
  → VCG01 (Pro 16:23): wisdom guides the mouth — speech as the giving form. VCG04 (froneō, Phil 2:2-5): shared orientation as communal giving. The wise person's life and speech give wisdom to others.
- *T4.3.2* — _What inner conditions or orientations in the giver enable genuine extension of this characteristic?_
  → Speech (wisdom guiding the mouth), shared orientation (communal accord, Phil 2:2), and governance judgment (just decision-making).
- *T4.3.3* — _What does the evidence reveal about what the person must have received or become before they can genuinely give this characteristic?_
  → VCG03 (wisdom constituted as character): the giver must first be wise — character enables transmission. Wisdom cannot be transmitted from an empty vessel.
- *T4.4.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic being received by a person from another — and if so, how does it operate in that reception?_
  → VCG03 (Pro 1:5 — "let the wise hear and increase in learning"): wisdom received from human wisdom-bearers.
- *T4.4.2* — _What inner conditions enable or block reception of this characteristic from another person?_
  → VCG03 (Pro 1:5): the wise person who continues to hear and increase — the receptive posture of the already-wise, characterised by humility to receive more.
- *T4.4.3* — _What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic from another but does not receive it?_
  → VCG07 (1Cor 1:18-25): the person who encounters the wisdom of the cross and does not receive it regards it as folly (mōria). The inner state is one of intellectual contempt — the wisdom-word is processed through a framework that reverses its value. The person who does not receive wisdom from another remains in their unreformed inner orientation, now confirmed in it by the encounter.
- *T4.5.1* — _Does the evidence indicate whether this characteristic operates differently within existing relational bonds versus across relational distan…_
  → VCG06 (self-attributed wisdom): the person who believes themselves wise is closed to receiving from others — wisdom as a self-boundary. VCG07 (wisdom of this age): those whose inner orientation is worldly wisdom are bounded from receiving divine wisdom.
- *T4.5.2* — _Does this characteristic operate within covenantal contexts only, or does it cross covenantal boundaries?_
  → VCG07: the worldly-wisdom orientation is the boundary limit — those within it cannot receive divine wisdom from without. The boundary is orientation-constituted.
- *T4.5.3* — _What does the evidence reveal about the relational scope of this characteristic — who is included and who is not?_
  → VCG09 (fear of the LORD as entry-point): wisdom's relational scope is covenantal — available to all who enter the posture of reverential acknowledgment of God. VCG07 (worldly wisdom): those whose orientation is self-determined wisdom are excluded.
- *T4.6.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in relation to other spiritual beings — angelic or adversarial — and if so, how?_
  → VCG01 (Jas 3:15-17): wisdom from above vs earthly-natural-demonic wisdom — the adversarial being's wisdom as the alternative to divine wisdom. VCG02 (1Ki 3:12): divine giving of wisdom as the background against which adversarial operations are implicitly opposed.
- *T4.6.2* — _Is this characteristic a site of adversarial activity — something that can be attacked, distorted, or weaponised by adversarial spiritual po…_
  → Jas 3:15 (earthly-natural-demonic wisdom): adversarial transmission of counterfeit wisdom. VCG02 (Spirit of God giving wisdom to craftsmen): divine transmission.
- *T4.6.3* — _Is this characteristic communicated, strengthened, or mediated through angelic ministry in the evidence?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]

**T5 — Formative and Developmental Dimension**

- *T5.1.1* — _Does this characteristic produce transformation in the person — and if so, does it change the person's condition, the person's orientation t…_
  → VCG03 (Pro 4:18): "the path of the righteous is like the light of dawn, which shines brighter and brighter until full day." Wisdom grows progressively. VCG09 (Pro 9:10 — fear of the LORD as beginning): the beginning point presupposes a trajectory of deepening.
- *T5.1.2* — _Is the transformation produced by this characteristic reversible or irreversible in the verse evidence?_
  → Both: wisdom deepens (the path grows brighter) and the person is transformed by wisdom's forming of character over time.
- *T5.1.3* — _If the evidence is silent on transformation, note this explicitly._
  → Progressive and long-term: the path growing brighter until full day implies a sustained trajectory. No evidence of sudden wisdom-formation except divine sovereign bestowing (VCG02 Solomon's prayer answered).
- *T5.2.1* — _Does the verse evidence describe a sequence of inner states through which this characteristic moves the person — a before, during, and after…_
  → Sequence: encounter with God's revelation (through law, teaching, experience) → humility and receptivity ("beginning of wisdom: fear of the LORD") → growing possession of wisdom-as-character → expressed in governance, speech, and life.
- *T5.2.2* — _What are those states, and what does the sequence reveal about how this characteristic works?_
  → Fear of the LORD (Pro 9:10): the reverential acknowledgment of God's authority is the prior inner state that opens the person to wisdom.
- *T5.2.3* — _If the evidence is silent on sequence, note this explicitly._
  → Governance capacity (VCG03 Solomon), creative excellence (VCG10 craftsmen), right-directed life (VCG04 froneō Spirit), and community unity (VCG05 shared orientation).
- *T5.3.1* — _What mechanism does this characteristic use to produce change in the person — discipline, encounter, gradual formation, sudden transformatio…_
  → Formation: divine bestowing (VCG02 Spirit-endowment), fear of the LORD (VCG09), hearing and accumulating (VCG03). Deepening: sustained practice in living wisely. Loss: self-attributed wisdom (VCG06) — the person who claims wisdom is closed to receiving it; foolishness as the failure to pursue (Pro 1 inverse).
- *T5.3.2* — _Does the evidence distinguish between mechanisms in different contexts?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T5.3.3* — _If the evidence is silent on mechanism, note this explicitly._
  → VCG06 (self-attributed wisdom) and VCG07 (worldly wisdom orientation): the primary resistance mechanisms. The person who is wise in their own eyes cannot receive wisdom; the person whose orientation is toward the world's wisdom is closed to divine wisdom.
- *T5.4.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in relation to suffering or affliction — as a response to it, a product of it, or…_
  → VCG09 (Psa 119:71 — "it is good for me that I was afflicted, that I might learn your statutes"): suffering deepens wisdom through the learning it enforces. VCG01 (the cross as the wisdom of God — 1Cor 1:18-25): the ultimate wisdom is expressed through and produced by suffering.
- *T5.4.2* — _Does suffering deepen, test, reveal, or produce this characteristic in the person?_
  → VCG01 (1Cor 1:18-25): the wisdom of God is revealed through the cross — suffering as the vehicle of divine wisdom-disclosure. The cross does not produce wisdom in the abstract but discloses the wisdom already in God.
- *T5.5.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic participating in the longer arc of character formation and sanctification — shaping the per…_
  → VCG04 (froneō Spirit vs flesh, Rom 8:5-8): setting the mind on the Spirit is both wisdom-expression and sanctification-mode. The wisdom-oriented person is being sanctified through their orientation. VCG09 (fear of the LORD): the beginning of sanctification and wisdom coincide.
- *T5.5.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about the role of this characteristic in that longer arc?_
  → VCG01 (1Cor 1:18-25): Christ IS the wisdom of God (1Cor 1:24, 30). Christlikeness in M15-A is the formation of the inner life into the pattern of the one who embodied divine wisdom — wisdom as Christlikeness.
- *T5.6.1* — _Does the verse evidence point this characteristic toward an eschatological fullness — a future state toward which its present operation is o…_
  → VCG07 (1Cor 1:18-25 — wisdom of this age "passing away"): the wisdom of this age is temporally bounded — eschatological wisdom displaces it. VCG01 (Prov 8:22-31 — wisdom at creation): Wisdom was with God before creation and will be with God eschatologically. The eschatological form of wisdom is the wisdom of the cross now vindicated (1Cor 1:24).
- *T5.6.2* — _What does the present experience of this characteristic anticipate about its future fullness?_
  → The wisdom of the cross now vindicated and revealed (1Cor 1:24) — Christ as God's wisdom is the eschatological form.
- *T5.6.3* — _If the evidence is silent on eschatological trajectory, note this explicitly._
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]

**T5 — Formative and Developmental Dimension**

- *T5.4.3* — _If the evidence is silent on the relationship to suffering, note this explicitly._

- *T5.7.1* — _Where T2.8 has identified a constitutional deposit from sustained operation of this characteristic, what developmental consequence does that…_
  → No body-deposit. VCG01 (wisdom guiding the mouth): the mouth is the body's instrument, not the deposit site. The governing is from wisdom in the heart; the body expresses but does not deposit.
- *T5.7.2* — _Does the evidence indicate generational consequence — a deposit carried forward beyond the individual?_
  → No generational consequence of wisdom evidenced in M15-A's VCG corpus. Wisdom is not named as a quality transmitted biologically or generationally. No evidence of generational deposit.
- *T5.7.3* — _If T2.8 found no deposit, note this explicitly and close T5.7._
  → T2.8 found no body deposit for any sub-group of M15. T5.7 closes for all sub-groups. No deposit consequence to trace for any characteristic in this cluster.

<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch5 — T1 findings for Wisdom as holistic inner character and orientation -->

**T1 — Definition**

- *T1.1.1* — _What is this characteristic called in the programme — and what does the name itself signal about its essential nature?_
  → H2450 cha.kham (wise) / H2452 chokh.mah (wisdom): root ch-kh-m — skilled, experienced, constituted in discernment. G4678 sofia: skilled in high sense. The name signals: constituted character quality, not mere information. Pro 16:23 (VCG03 anchor).
- *T1.1.2* — _What do the primary Hebrew and Greek terms reveal at the definitional level — before deeper lexical analysis begins?_
  → Cha.kham (adjective → adjectival noun) reveals wisdom as character-state. Chokh.mah (noun) reveals it as a substantive inner reality. Sofizo (causative verb) reveals it as something another can produce in a person. The terms collectively show: wisdom is a constituted quality held in the heart that governs the whole person's operation. Pro 16:23 (VCG03 anchor).
- *T1.1.3* — _Does the name carry directional, relational, or constitutional implications that orient the enquiry from the outset?_
  → Constitutional (the wise person IS); directional (toward God, VCG09; toward worldly ends, VCG07); relational (wisdom given by God to the asker, Jam 1:5 VCG02 anchor).
- *T1.2.1* — _What kind of inner-being phenomenon does this characteristic appear to be — an act, a disposition, a condition, a quality, or something else…_
  → A constituted disposition functioning as orientation, quality, and operative capacity simultaneously. Pro 16:23 (VCG03 anchor): not an act performed but a quality exercised from the heart's constitution.
- *T1.2.2* — _Is this characteristic simple in structure or does it appear to have constituent elements at first encounter?_
  → Compound: VCG structure reveals five constituent elements: constituted character (VCG03), directional orientation (VCG04), perceptive intelligibility (VCG08), covenantal grounding (VCG09), creative-design capacity (VCG10). Pro 16:23 (VCG03 anchor).
- *T1.2.3* — _What is the current best working description of this characteristic — encapsulating its constitutional location, the faculties it primarily …_
  → A divinely-endowed constituted quality of the whole person, grounded in covenantal orientation toward God, expressed in the governance of mind, speech, and action, and distinguished from self-attributed or world-oriented substitutes. Primary constitutional location: heart and mind. Pro 16:23, Jam 1:5, Rom 8:5.
- *T1.3.1* — _What is the structural opposite of this characteristic — the inner-being reality that stands against or excludes it?_
  → G0781 asofos (unwise); VCG06 (self-attributed wisdom, Pro 26:12 anchor); VCG07 (worldly wisdom, 1Cor 1:21 anchor). Three types of opposite: absence, counterfeit, and inversion.
- *T1.3.2* — _What does this characteristic explicitly exclude or resist?_
  → Self-sufficient wisdom (VCG06); worldly orientation (VCG07: 1Cor 1:21); unguarded speech and unrestrained impulse (VCG03 corpus).
- *T1.3.3* — _What is this characteristic not — where does it end and something else begin?_
  → Wisdom (M15-A) is not: mere cognition (M15-B/C boundary); self-generated achievement (VCG06 counterfeit); worldly prudence (VCG07). It ends where mere information-holding (M15-C) begins and where mere perceptive act (M15-B) begins.
- *T1.4.1* — _In what distinct ways does this characteristic operate within the inner person?_
  → Five modes: constituted character (VCG03: Pro 16:23), directional orientation (VCG04: Rom 8:5), intelligibility/perceptive grasping (VCG08: Neh 8:8), covenantal formation (VCG09: Psa 111:10), creative-design inner forming (VCG10: Exo 31:4).
- *T1.4.2* — _Does this characteristic operate differently depending on context, direction, or constitutional level?_
  → VCG01 (divine level: wisdom inheres in God), VCG02 (given level: entering human via endowment), VCG03 (held level: constituted character), VCG04 (directional level: froneō at mind-orientation). The operating mode follows the constitutional level.
- *T1.4.3* — _Does this characteristic have a communicative or speech-based mode of operation — and if so, how does it function?_
  → Pro 16:23 (VCG03 anchor): wisdom governs speech. 1Cor 2:13 (VCG07 corpus): speech either taught by human wisdom or by the Spirit. Wisdom has a speech mode.
- *T1.5.1* — _What is the first or most immediate inner-being response to receiving or encountering this characteristic?_
  → VCG08 (Neh 8:8): cognitive opening — the people understood what was read. Jam 1:5 (VCG02 anchor): the asking posture — immediate orientation toward God.
- *T1.5.2* — _Is the immediate response consistent across the verse evidence, or does it vary?_
  → Consistent in structure (cognitive opening, orientation toward God) but varies by mode of encounter (receiving endowment vs encountering wisdom in another vs meeting self-attributed substitute).
- *T1.5.3* — _Where the verse evidence is silent on immediate response, note this explicitly._
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T1.6.1* — _What does this characteristic produce in the inner being over time?_
  → Pro 16:23 (VCG03 corpus): judicious speech, restraint of impulse, teachability. Psa 111:10 (VCG09 anchor): covenantal fidelity.
- *T1.6.2* — _What states, qualities, capacities, or orientations does sustained exposure to or possession of this characteristic establish?_
  → Judicious speech, restraint, teachability, covenantal fidelity (evidence: Pro 16:23, Psa 111:10 as above).
- *T1.6.3* — _Does the sustained effect differ from the immediate response — and if so, how?_
  → Uniformly yes across all sub-groups. The immediate response is a specific act or opening; the sustained effect is a constituted quality or orientation formed over time. The pattern is consistent across the cluster: encounter/reception → immediate cognitive/volitional/affective opening → sustained formation of character/orientation/capacity. This is a cluster-level pattern.
- *T1.7.1* — _What inner conditions or orientations enable genuine reception of this characteristic?_
  → Fear of the Lord (Psa 111:10 VCG09 anchor); humility-in-asking (Jam 1:5 VCG02 anchor); attentive hearing (VCG08: Neh 8:8).
- *T1.7.2* — _What inner conditions block, distort, or prevent reception?_
  → Self-sufficiency (VCG06: Pro 26:12 — wise in own eyes); worldly orientation (VCG07: 1Cor 1:21).
- *T1.7.3* — _What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic but does not receive it?_
  → VCG06 (Pro 26:12 anchor): "there is more hope for a fool than for a person wise in their own eyes" — self-wisdom as the inner state forecloses reception more completely than simple ignorance.
- *T1.8.1* — _What is the primary inner-being dimension of this characteristic from the programme's dimension vocabulary?_
  → Cognitive-constitutive (constituted quality of heart-and-mind). Secondary: volitional (direction), relational (covenantal), creative (VCG10). Evidence: Pro 16:23 (heart of wise → judicious speech), Rom 8:5 (froneō — mind-orientation).
- *T1.8.2* — _What evidence from the verse evidence supports this classification?_
  → Pro 16:23: heart of the wise → governing character. Rom 8:5: froneō as directed-mind act.
- *T1.8.3* — _Does this characteristic carry secondary dimensions — and if so, what are they, and do they compete with the primary classification?_
  → Volitional, relational, creative — secondary dimensions do not compete with cognitive-constitutive primary; they extend it. Pro 16:23 (heart governing output) is unambiguously primary.

**Key verses for Wisdom as holistic inner character and orientation:**

**Dan 2:20** (H2452 chokh.mah) [M15-A-VCG01]
> Dan 2:20 Daniel answered and said : “ Blessed be the name of God forever and ever , to whom belong wisdom and might .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "to him belong wisdom and might" — wisdom as God's own attribute

**Jam 1:5** (G4678 sofia) [M15-A-VCG02]
> Jam 1:5 If any of you lacks wisdom , let him ask God , who gives generously to all without reproach , and it will be given him .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "if any lacks wisdom, let him ask God who gives generously" — wisdom is not self-generated; it is asked for and given

**Pro 16:23** (H2450 cha.kham) [M15-A-VCG03]
> Pro 16:23 The heart of the wise makes his speech judicious and adds persuasiveness to his lips .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "heart of the wise makes his speech judicious" — wisdom in the heart shapes outward speech

**Rom 8:5** (G5426 froneō) [M15-A-VCG04]
> Rom 8:5 For those who live according to the flesh set their minds on the things of the flesh , but those who live according to the Spirit set their minds on the things of the Spirit .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "set their minds on things of flesh / Spirit" — froneō as the determinative inner orientation; flesh-minded or Spirit-minded describes the whole person

**Phili 2:2** (G5426 froneō) [M15-A-VCG05]
> Phili 2:2 complete my joy by being of the same mind , having the same love , being in full accord and of one mind .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "being of the same mind" — froneō as the inner orientation of the whole community

**Pro 26:12** (H2450 cha.kham) [M15-A-VCG06]
> Pro 26:12 Do you see a man who is wise in his own eyes ? There is more hope for a fool than for him .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "a man who is wise in his own eyes — more hope for a fool" — self-attributed wisdom as worse than foolishness; inner self-assessment as the problem

**1Cor 1:21** (G4678 sofia) [M15-A-VCG07]
> 1Cor 1:21 For since , in the wisdom of God , the world did not know God through wisdom , it pleased God through the folly of what we preach to save those who believe .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "world did not know God through wisdom" — sophia as the instrument that failed to reach God

**Neh 8:8** (H0995 bin) [M15-A-VCG08]
> Neh 8:8 They read from the book , from the Law of God , clearly , and they gave the sense , so that the people understood the reading .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "they gave the sense so that the people understood the reading" — bin activated by clear exposition; the inner faculty grasps meaning when the word is made clear

**Psa 111:10** (H7922 se.khel) [M15-A-VCG09]
> Psa 111:10 The fear of the Lord is the beginning of wisdom ; all those who practice it have a good understanding . His praise endures forever !
_Meaning of the term here:_ "all who practice it have good understanding" — se.khel as the fruit of practicing the fear of the Lord

**Exo 31:4** (H2803G cha.shav) [M15-A-VCG10]
> Exo 31:4 to devise artistic designs , to work in gold , silver , and bronze ,
_Meaning of the term here:_ "to devise artistic designs" — cha.shav explicitly names the inner act of design, not just execution


### 5.2 Understanding as inner perceptive faculty

**T4 — Relational Interfaces**

- *T4.1.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating from God toward the human person — and if so, how?_
  → VCG02 (Job 38:36 — divine placing of understanding into the person). VCG06 (Luk 24:45): Christ opening the disciples' minds — the most direct NT instance of divine-to-human understanding transmission.
- *T4.1.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about the basis on which God extends this characteristic — is it conditional, unconditional, covenantal, or re…_
  → VCG06 (Luk 24:45): Christ initiates the opening of understanding — purely divine initiative, not a response to the disciples' request. VCG02 (Job 38:36): divine sovereign placing.
- *T4.1.3* — _What does God's extension of this characteristic reveal about his disposition toward the human person?_
  → VCG06 (Luk 24:45 → 24:47): understanding opened → mission capacity. The disciples move from confusion to commission.
- *T4.2.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in the human person's movement toward God — in seeking, supplication, worship, or…_
  → VCG02 (1Cor 11:31 in M15-D, but proximate): self-discernment directed toward God. VCG01 (sa.khal corpus): attending to God's acts.
- *T4.2.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about the inner posture required for this movement?_
  → VCG05 (Heb 5:14): willingness to be trained. VCG06: openness to receive divine disclosure.
- *T4.2.3* — _What does the human-to-God direction of this characteristic reveal about the person's relationship with God?_
  → The human-to-God direction of understanding (attending to God's acts, opening to his teaching) reveals the relationship as one of receptive discipleship: the person is constituted as learner before God. The understanding-toward-God posture is the posture of the creature who needs to receive comprehension from outside themselves.
- *T4.3.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic being extended by one person toward another — and if so, how does it operate in that giving…_
  → VCG07 (dialegō): sustained Scripture-based engagement with others — understanding given through teaching and argumentation.
- *T4.3.2* — _What inner conditions or orientations in the giver enable genuine extension of this characteristic?_
  → Teaching and argumentation (dialegō) — the transmission of understanding through sustained engagement with the Scriptures.
- *T4.3.3* — _What does the evidence reveal about what the person must have received or become before they can genuinely give this characteristic?_
  → The one who understands can transmit through teaching — prior possession of the understanding enables the gift.
- *T4.4.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic being received by a person from another — and if so, how does it operate in that reception?_
  → VCG07 (M15-B — dialegō): understanding received through sustained discourse from a teacher/apostle.
- *T4.4.2* — _What inner conditions enable or block reception of this characteristic from another person?_
  → VCG07: openness to sustained engagement and argument. VCG05 (Heb 5:14): willingness to be trained.
- *T4.4.3* — _What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic from another but does not receive it?_
  → The person who encounters sustained Scripture-based teaching but does not receive it has been exposed without being opened. The inner state is defended — the perceptive faculty that could be opened remains closed. Judicial hardening (VCG04 inverse) is the sustained form of this non-reception.
- *T4.5.1* — _Does the evidence indicate whether this characteristic operates differently within existing relational bonds versus across relational distan…_
  → VCG04 (M15-B — judicial withholding): God can withhold understanding as a judicial act — a divine boundary on understanding.
- *T4.5.2* — _Does this characteristic operate within covenantal contexts only, or does it cross covenantal boundaries?_
  → VCG04: judicial withholding — divine decision is the boundary in this case.
- *T4.5.3* — _What does the evidence reveal about the relational scope of this characteristic — who is included and who is not?_
  → VCG06 (Luk 24:45): the disciples as specific recipients of Christ's opening of understanding — a particular relational circle. Excluded: those under judicial hardening (VCG04), those who remain in immaturity (VCG05 inverse).
- *T4.6.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in relation to other spiritual beings — angelic or adversarial — and if so, how?_
  → VCG04 (M15-B — judicial withholding): God closing understanding. VCG06 (Luk 24:45): Christ opening understanding — both divine positive and negative operations on the perceptive faculty.
- *T4.6.2* — _Is this characteristic a site of adversarial activity — something that can be attacked, distorted, or weaponised by adversarial spiritual po…_
  → VCG04 (M15-B): God both gives and withholds understanding through his divine action on the inner perceptive faculty.
- *T4.6.3* — _Is this characteristic communicated, strengthened, or mediated through angelic ministry in the evidence?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]

**T5 — Formative and Developmental Dimension**

- *T5.1.1* — _Does this characteristic produce transformation in the person — and if so, does it change the person's condition, the person's orientation t…_
  → VCG05 (Heb 5:14): understanding trained through constant practice — progressive formation. VCG06 (Luk 24:45): Christ's opening as the beginning of a new capacity, not the completion of it.
- *T5.1.2* — _Is the transformation produced by this characteristic reversible or irreversible in the verse evidence?_
  → Both: the understanding faculty deepens (VCG05 training); and the person is transformed by opened understanding (VCG06 — from confusion to commission).
- *T5.1.3* — _If the evidence is silent on transformation, note this explicitly._
  → Two modes: progressive (VCG05 training through practice) and instantaneous (VCG06 Christ's opening — a definitive act that opens the faculty).
- *T5.2.1* — _Does the verse evidence describe a sequence of inner states through which this characteristic moves the person — a before, during, and after…_
  → Sequence: undiscerning state (milk-only, Heb 5:13) → training-by-practice → trained discernment (mature, Heb 5:14). For divine opening: closed understanding → Christ's act → opened to comprehend Scripture.
- *T5.2.2* — _What are those states, and what does the sequence reveal about how this characteristic works?_
  → Openness and volitional intent (VCG05 training). Receptive hearing (VCG07 dialegō).
- *T5.2.3* — _If the evidence is silent on sequence, note this explicitly._
  → VCG06 (Luk 24:45 → mission): mission capacity and joyful worship (Luk 24:52-53). VCG05 (Heb 5:14): mature Christian life characterised by moral discernment.
- *T5.3.1* — _What mechanism does this characteristic use to produce change in the person — discipline, encounter, gradual formation, sudden transformatio…_
  → Formation: constant practice (VCG05 Heb 5:14), divine opening (VCG06 Luk 24:45), sustained discourse (VCG07). Deepening: continued training. Loss: judicial withholding (VCG04) or moral hardening.
- *T5.3.2* — _Does the evidence distinguish between mechanisms in different contexts?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T5.3.3* — _If the evidence is silent on mechanism, note this explicitly._
  → VCG04 (judicial withholding): hardened hearts cannot understand. Moral blockage is the primary loss mechanism.
- *T5.4.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in relation to suffering or affliction — as a response to it, a product of it, or…_
  → VCG05 (Heb 5:14): the training that forms discernment implies disciplined effort — which can include difficulty. The maturity toward which understanding-training is directed is explicitly eschatologically tested.
- *T5.4.3* — _If the evidence is silent on the relationship to suffering, note this explicitly._
  → Suffering's role is largely silent in M15-B's direct VCG evidence. The training of VCG05 may involve difficulty but suffering is not named as its mechanism. Silence confirmed for M15-B.
- *T5.5.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic participating in the longer arc of character formation and sanctification — shaping the per…_
  → VCG05 (Heb 5:14): trained discernment for moral distinction is a mark of sanctified maturity. VCG06 (Luk 24:45 → 24:47): opened understanding enables preaching repentance for the forgiveness of sins — the mission of sanctification.
- *T5.5.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about the role of this characteristic in that longer arc?_
  → VCG06 (Luk 24:45): Christ opens the disciples' understanding — Christlikeness in M15-B is opened and taught by Christ himself.
- *T5.6.1* — _Does the verse evidence point this characteristic toward an eschatological fullness — a future state toward which its present operation is o…_
  → VCG06 (1Cor 13:12 proximate): "now I know in part; then I shall know fully." Full understanding is an eschatological event. VCG03 (1Ki 3:9): the gift of understanding is a present partial gift that awaits eschatological completion.
- *T5.6.2* — _What does the present experience of this characteristic anticipate about its future fullness?_
  → Full knowing (1Cor 13:12) — the eschatological form is comprehensive understanding, which the present partial form anticipates.
- *T5.6.3* — _If the evidence is silent on eschatological trajectory, note this explicitly._
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]

  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]

<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch5 — T1 findings for Understanding as inner perceptive faculty -->

**T1 — Definition**

- *T1.1.1* — _What is this characteristic called in the programme — and what does the name itself signal about its essential nature?_
  → H0995 bin / H8394 te.vu.nah: root b-y-n — to separate, distinguish, perceive. G4920 suniēmi / G4907 sunesis: to bring together into comprehension. The name signals: active perceptive-separating-gathering — understanding is the act of discerning distinctions and unifying them into grasp. Isa 40:28 (VCG01 anchor).
- *T1.1.2* — _What do the primary Hebrew and Greek terms reveal at the definitional level — before deeper lexical analysis begins?_
  → Bin (verb) reveals it as an active perceptive act. Te.vu.nah (noun) reveals it as the faculty that performs the act. Sunesis (noun) reveals the comprehension produced. Suniēmi (verb) reveals the act of bringing together. The terms show: understanding is both a faculty (te.vu.nah, sunesis) and an exercise of that faculty (bin, suniēmi). 1Ki 3:9 (VCG03 anchor).
- *T1.1.3* — _Does the name carry directional, relational, or constitutional implications that orient the enquiry from the outset?_
  → Receptive direction built in (the perceptive faculty receives what is given); relational (understanding given by God, Job 38:36 VCG02 anchor; opened by Christ, Luk 24:45 VCG06 anchor).
- *T1.2.1* — _What kind of inner-being phenomenon does this characteristic appear to be — an act, a disposition, a condition, a quality, or something else…_
  → A perceptive faculty — the inner capacity to receive, distinguish, and grasp. Heb 5:14 (VCG05 anchor): formable; Isa 6:10 (VCG04 anchor): blockable. A dynamic capacity, not a static holding.
- *T1.2.2* — _Is this characteristic simple in structure or does it appear to have constituent elements at first encounter?_
  → Constituent elements: receptive-perceptive act (VCG06), constituted faculty (VCG03), formed-through-practice capacity (VCG05), and the blocked/withheld negative mode (VCG04). Heb 5:14 (VCG05 anchor).
- *T1.2.3* — _What is the current best working description of this characteristic — encapsulating its constitutional location, the faculties it primarily …_
  → The inner capacity to receive, distinguish, and grasp what is disclosed — divine revelation, situation, meaning. Constituted in the person by divine endowment, formed through practice, exercised in receiving disclosed content, and capable of blockage. Primary location: heart (1Ki 3:9) and mind (Luk 24:45). Isa 40:28, 1Ki 3:9, Luk 24:45.
- *T1.3.1* — _What is the structural opposite of this characteristic — the inner-being reality that stands against or excludes it?_
  → G0801 asunetos (senseless/without understanding); VCG04 blockage pattern (Isa 6:10 anchor: the closed inner faculty).
- *T1.3.2* — _What does this characteristic explicitly exclude or resist?_
  → Hardness of heart (VCG04: Isa 6:10); spiritual dullness; inability to grasp disclosed meaning.
- *T1.3.3* — _What is this characteristic not — where does it end and something else begin?_
  → Understanding (M15-B) is not: constituted wisdom-character (M15-A); held knowledge (M15-C); evaluative discernment (M15-D). It ends where its perceptive act produces its results — those results then belong to M15-C (knowledge) or serve M15-A (wisdom).
- *T1.4.1* — _In what distinct ways does this characteristic operate within the inner person?_
  → Four modes: habitual discernment capacity (VCG03: 1Ki 3:9), receptive grasping of revealed content (VCG06: Luk 24:45), formation through practice (VCG05: Heb 5:14), judicial blockage (VCG04: Isa 6:10).
- *T1.4.2* — _Does this characteristic operate differently depending on context, direction, or constitutional level?_
  → VCG01 (divine: unsearchable), VCG02 (given: placed in human), VCG03 (constituted: exercised habitually), VCG06 (receptive: opening to revealed content). Same pattern as M15-A.
- *T1.4.3* — _Does this characteristic have a communicative or speech-based mode of operation — and if so, how does it function?_
  → VCG07 (2 verses): understanding at the translation/interpretation boundary — making meaning communicable across language barriers. Suniēmi enables intelligible communication.
- *T1.5.1* — _What is the first or most immediate inner-being response to receiving or encountering this characteristic?_
  → Luk 24:45 (VCG06 anchor): minds opened → Scripture comprehended. The immediate response is cognitive opening — a new capacity to grasp what was previously closed.
- *T1.5.2* — _Is the immediate response consistent across the verse evidence, or does it vary?_
  → Consistent: cognitive opening or enabling capacity across all modes.
- *T1.5.3* — _Where the verse evidence is silent on immediate response, note this explicitly._
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T1.6.1* — _What does this characteristic produce in the inner being over time?_
  → Heb 5:14 (VCG05 anchor): habitual discernment faculty, mature inner capacity for moral navigation.
- *T1.6.2* — _What states, qualities, capacities, or orientations does sustained exposure to or possession of this characteristic establish?_
  → Mature discernment faculty, governance capacity (Heb 5:14, 1Ki 3:9).
- *T1.6.3* — _Does the sustained effect differ from the immediate response — and if so, how?_
  → Uniformly yes across all sub-groups. The immediate response is a specific act or opening; the sustained effect is a constituted quality or orientation formed over time. The pattern is consistent across the cluster: encounter/reception → immediate cognitive/volitional/affective opening → sustained formation of character/orientation/capacity. This is a cluster-level pattern.
- *T1.7.1* — _What inner conditions or orientations enable genuine reception of this characteristic?_
  → Humility (1Ki 3:9: acknowledging inadequacy); practice (Heb 5:14 VCG05 anchor); openness to divine opening (Luk 24:45 VCG06 anchor — the disciples cannot open their own minds).
- *T1.7.2* — _What inner conditions block, distort, or prevent reception?_
  → Hardness of heart (VCG04: Isa 6:10); spiritual dullness; asunetos state (G0801).
- *T1.7.3* — _What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic but does not receive it?_
  → VCG04 (Isa 6:10 anchor): the judicially-closed inner state — hears but does not understand, sees but does not perceive. The faculty is active at surface level; closed at depth.
- *T1.8.1* — _What is the primary inner-being dimension of this characteristic from the programme's dimension vocabulary?_
  → Cognitive-perceptive (the faculty of receiving and grasping). Secondary: volitional (formed through practice), moral-evaluative (distinguishing good from evil). Evidence: Isa 40:28, 1Ki 3:9, Heb 5:14.
- *T1.8.2* — _What evidence from the verse evidence supports this classification?_
  → Isa 40:28: God's understanding as model. Heb 5:14: training by practice. Luk 24:45: opened minds.
- *T1.8.3* — _Does this characteristic carry secondary dimensions — and if so, what are they, and do they compete with the primary classification?_
  → Volitional (practice) and moral-evaluative (distinguishing) are secondary and serve the primary perceptive function. No competition.

### 5.3 Knowledge as inner content and covenantal knowing

<!-- AI WRITE: Chapter 5 §5.3 (Knowledge as inner content and covenantal knowing)
     LENGTH: ~800-1500 words per characteristic
     FOCUS: Write on how this characteristic moves — between God and the human person, between persons, in covenant, against opposition — and how it is formed, deepens, is tested, is transformed across time. Use the evidence below.
     CITE (must quote at least 2 verbatim): Psa 139:6; Amo 3:2; Jos 4:24; Hos 6:3
     SOURCE: All evidence for this characteristic on this lens is in the blocks below.
     AVOID: jargon; do not cite finding-id, tier code, or VCG code in the prose
-->

<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch5 — T4 findings for Knowledge as inner content and covenantal knowing -->

**T4 — Relational Interfaces**

- *T4.1.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating from God toward the human person — and if so, how?_
  → VCG01 (Psa 139:6): God's comprehensive knowing of the human — total, inescapable, prior to any human act. VCG02 (Amos 3:2): God's elective knowing — initiating covenant relationship through his knowing act.
- *T4.1.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about the basis on which God extends this characteristic — is it conditional, unconditional, covenantal, or re…_
  → VCG03 (Exo 7:5): God's redemptive acts initiate knowing. The initiative is entirely divine: not human inquiry but divine self-disclosure through historical action.
- *T4.1.3* — _What does God's extension of this characteristic reveal about his disposition toward the human person?_
  → VCG04 (Hos 6:3): knowing God is life-orienting. VCG12 (Hab 2:14): eschatological knowing of God fills the earth — the ultimate constitutive effect.
- *T4.2.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in the human person's movement toward God — in seeking, supplication, worship, or…_
  → VCG04 (Hos 6:3): "let us press on to know the LORD" — human pursuit of knowing God. VCG08: Job's assertions of knowing his Redeemer — addressed toward God.
- *T4.2.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about the inner posture required for this movement?_
  → VCG04: volitional pursuit. VCG06: accumulated knowledge of God's ways. VCG08: sustained faith-conviction.
- *T4.2.3* — _What does the human-to-God direction of this characteristic reveal about the person's relationship with God?_
  → The pursuit of knowing the LORD (Hos 6:3 VCG04) and Job's assertion of knowing his Redeemer (VCG08) reveal the relationship as covenantal-personal: the human presses toward the knowing of a Person, not facts about a person. The human-to-God knowing-direction reveals a relationship that can be pressed into, deepened, and sustained through affliction.
- *T4.3.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic being extended by one person toward another — and if so, how does it operate in that giving…_
  → VCG06 (Pro 10:14): "lips of the wise spread knowledge" — human-to-human transmission as teaching. VCG08: testimony-assertion as giving conviction to others.
- *T4.3.2* — _What inner conditions or orientations in the giver enable genuine extension of this characteristic?_
  → Testimony and teaching (VCG06 lips; VCG08 assertion). Not mystical impartation.
- *T4.3.3* — _What does the evidence reveal about what the person must have received or become before they can genuinely give this characteristic?_
  → VCG06: the wise person who has "laid up" knowledge — accumulated inner holding enables transmission.
- *T4.4.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic being received by a person from another — and if so, how does it operate in that reception?_
  → VCG04 (Hos 6:3): communal "let us" — receiving as community. VCG06: the learner receiving from the wise.
- *T4.4.2* — _What inner conditions enable or block reception of this characteristic from another person?_
  → VCG04: volitional pursuit ("let us"). VCG06: the contrast with the fool implies receptivity as the condition — openness and pursuit.
- *T4.4.3* — _What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic from another but does not receive it?_
  → VCG05 (1Sa 2:12 — not knowing the LORD): the person who encounters the knowledge of God and does not receive it remains in the covenant-outside position, characterised by destructive behaviour. The inner state is one of chosen not-knowing — the knowledge offered does not find a receptive inner condition.
- *T4.5.1* — _Does the evidence indicate whether this characteristic operates differently within existing relational bonds versus across relational distan…_
  → VCG05 (1Sa 2:12): not knowing the Lord as relational boundary marker. VCG09 (Act 17:30): culpable ignorance as boundary between former times and present accountability.
- *T4.5.2* — _Does this characteristic operate within covenantal contexts only, or does it cross covenantal boundaries?_
  → Covenantal status is the primary boundary-defining principle: those who know the Lord and those who do not.
- *T4.5.3* — _What does the evidence reveal about the relational scope of this characteristic — who is included and who is not?_
  → VCG02 (Amos 3:2): divine elective knowing is covenantally bounded — Israel among all the families of the earth. VCG12 (Hab 2:14): the eschatological scope is universal — "the earth." The scope of knowledge moves from covenantally particular (VCG02) to eschatologically universal (VCG12).
- *T4.6.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in relation to other spiritual beings — angelic or adversarial — and if so, how?_
  → VCG07 (Gen 3): the serpent's role in offering knowledge of good and evil — adversarial transmission of moral knowing. VCG01 (Psa 139:6): God's comprehensive knowing.
- *T4.6.2* — _Is this characteristic a site of adversarial activity — something that can be attacked, distorted, or weaponised by adversarial spiritual po…_
  → VCG07 (Gen 3): adversarial offer of moral knowledge — the most consequential adversarial transmission of a knowledge-form in Scripture.
<!-- /EVIDENCE -->
