  → Evidence is not silent — VCG01, VCG02, VCG03 are explicit on divine knowing of and disclosing to the human. No silence to note.
- *T4.2.4* — _If the evidence is silent on human-to-God operation, note this explicitly._
  → Evidence is not silent — VCG04 (Hos 6:3 pursuit) and VCG08 (Job 19:25 assertion) are explicit. No silence.
- *T4.3.4* — _If the evidence is silent on the giving direction, note this explicitly._
  → Evidence is not silent — VCG06 ("lips of the wise spread knowledge") is explicit. No silence.
- *T4.4.4* — _If the evidence is silent on the receiving direction, note this explicitly._
  → Evidence is not silent — VCG06 and VCG04 establish the receiving-posture. No silence.

  → Evidence is not silent — VCG02 and VCG12 establish boundaries. No silence.

**T5 — Formative and Developmental Dimension**

- *T5.1.1* — _Does this characteristic produce transformation in the person — and if so, does it change the person's condition, the person's orientation t…_
  → VCG04 (Hos 6:3 "press on"): knowing God grows through pursuit. VCG06 (Pro 10:14 "lay up"): knowledge accumulates over time. VCG08 (Job 19:25): conviction deepened through testing in suffering.
- *T5.1.2* — _Is the transformation produced by this characteristic reversible or irreversible in the verse evidence?_
  → Both: knowledge-content deepens (VCG08 conviction through testing); and the person is transformed by the knowing of God (VCG04 — life-orientation shaped by knowing).
- *T5.1.3* — _If the evidence is silent on transformation, note this explicitly._
  → Progressive (VCG04 pressing on, VCG08 conviction through sustained testing). Exception: VCG03 — knowing through historical redemptive events can be instantaneous in historical terms.
- *T5.2.1* — _Does the verse evidence describe a sequence of inner states through which this characteristic moves the person — a before, during, and after…_
  → Covenantal sequence: encounter with God's disclosure → volitional pursuit → relational knowing → orientation-formation. Conviction sequence: initial faith → affliction → maintained conviction → vindication anticipated.
- *T5.2.2* — _What are those states, and what does the sequence reveal about how this characteristic works?_
  → Volitional pursuit (VCG04). Repentance (VCG09 — removing culpable ignorance). Election/covenant (VCG02 — divine choice is prior).
- *T5.2.3* — _If the evidence is silent on sequence, note this explicitly._
  → VCG08: sustained conviction enabling advocacy through suffering. VCG04: knowing God produces life-orientation. VCG06: accumulated knowledge produces the wise person's characteristic way of living.
- *T5.3.1* — _What mechanism does this characteristic use to produce change in the person — discipline, encounter, gradual formation, sudden transformatio…_
  → Formation: divine disclosure through historical events (VCG03), covenantal pursuit (VCG04), wise accumulation (VCG06). Deepening: sustained engagement through difficulty (VCG08). Loss: covenant-breach — not-knowing as relational rupture (VCG05).
- *T5.3.2* — _Does the evidence distinguish between mechanisms in different contexts?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T5.3.3* — _If the evidence is silent on mechanism, note this explicitly._
  → VCG05 (not-knowing as active resistance): Eli's sons as the type of chosen not-knowing. VCG09: culpable ignorance as sustained resistance.
- *T5.4.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in relation to suffering or affliction — as a response to it, a product of it, or…_
  → VCG08 (Job 19:25): the most direct evidence across M15. Job's knowledge of his Redeemer is forged and sustained through extreme suffering. The conviction is expressed through and tested by affliction.
- *T5.4.2* — _Does suffering deepen, test, reveal, or produce this characteristic in the person?_
  → VCG08: conviction-knowing deepened in suffering (though not solely produced by it). The suffering provides the context in which the knowing is tested and made explicit.
- *T5.5.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic participating in the longer arc of character formation and sanctification — shaping the per…_
  → VCG04 (Hos 6:3): knowing God is the covenantal orientation of the sanctified life. VCG08: conviction of the Redeemer shapes the person's posture before God throughout affliction.
- *T5.5.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about the role of this characteristic in that longer arc?_
  → VCG04: knowing God presses toward the pattern of the one who fully knows and is fully known. The covenantal-knowing trajectory carries toward knowing Christ (Phil 3:10 proximate).
- *T5.6.1* — _Does the verse evidence point this characteristic toward an eschatological fullness — a future state toward which its present operation is o…_
  → VCG12 (Hab 2:14): "the earth shall be full of the knowledge of the Lord as the waters cover the sea" — the most explicit eschatological statement in M15. Universal, comprehensive, saturating knowing of God is the eschatological telos of M15-C.
- *T5.6.2* — _What does the present experience of this characteristic anticipate about its future fullness?_
  → Universal knowing of God filling the earth as waters (Hab 2:14 VCG12) — the eschatological form is global, saturating, comprehensive knowing of the LORD.
- *T5.6.3* — _If the evidence is silent on eschatological trajectory, note this explicitly._
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T5.7.3* — _If T2.8 found no deposit, note this explicitly and close T5.7._
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]

**T5 — Formative and Developmental Dimension**

- *T5.4.3* — _If the evidence is silent on the relationship to suffering, note this explicitly._
  → Evidence is not silent — VCG08 (Job 19:25 — conviction forged in extreme suffering) is the primary suffering evidence in M15. No silence.
- *T5.5.3* — _If the evidence is silent on formation and sanctification, note this explicitly._
  → Evidence is not silent — VCG04 (knowing God as covenantal orientation) and VCG08 (conviction sustained through affliction) are sanctification-relevant. No silence.
- *T5.7.1* — _Where T2.8 has identified a constitutional deposit from sustained operation of this characteristic, what developmental consequence does that…_
  → No body-deposit. VCG11 (intimate knowing via union): knowing is not named as a body-deposit; it is relational-personal knowing of persons through union.
- *T5.7.2* — _Does the evidence indicate generational consequence — a deposit carried forward beyond the individual?_
  → No generational deposit evidenced directly in M15-C's VCGs. The covenant community's accumulated knowledge is culturally transmitted through teaching and liturgy, but M15-C's terms do not name a biological or constitutional deposit across generations. Silence on generational deposit.

<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch5 — T1 findings for Knowledge as inner content and covenantal knowing -->

**T1 — Definition**

- *T1.1.1* — _What is this characteristic called in the programme — and what does the name itself signal about its essential nature?_
  → H3045 ya.da (to know): the broadest Hebrew knowing word — spans from experiential/relational knowing to factual knowing to sexual knowing (VCG11). H1847 da.at (knowledge): the inner content of knowing. G6063 oida: to have seen and therefore know — a knowing that comes from having been present. The name signals: knowledge is fundamentally relational-experiential, not merely cognitive storage. Hos 6:3 (VCG04 anchor), Pro 1:7 (VCG06 anchor).
- *T1.1.2* — _What do the primary Hebrew and Greek terms reveal at the definitional level — before deeper lexical analysis begins?_
  → Ya.da (verb: to know in the full experiential-relational sense). Da.at (noun: the content of knowing). Oida (verb: to know from having been present or witnessed). Man.da / de.ah / de.a (various nouns for knowledge-content). The terms show knowledge as inherently relational and experiential — not an abstract repository but a living relational state. Gen 4:1 (VCG11 anchor) and Hos 6:3 (VCG04 anchor) reveal the range.
- *T1.1.3* — _Does the name carry directional, relational, or constitutional implications that orient the enquiry from the outset?_
  → Relational by nature: ya.da spans factual, relational, covenantal, and sexual knowing — the relational implication is constitutive of the term itself. Amo 3:2 (VCG02 anchor): "you only have I known" — the divine knowing is elective-covenantal, not merely informational.
- *T1.2.1* — _What kind of inner-being phenomenon does this characteristic appear to be — an act, a disposition, a condition, a quality, or something else…_
  → A relational-covenantal state — knowing as a living relational orientation, not merely an information-holding. Hos 6:3 (VCG04 anchor): pressing to know the LORD is a relational posture. Pro 1:7 (VCG06 anchor): knowledge as a valued inner endowment accumulated and transmitted.
- *T1.2.2* — _Is this characteristic simple in structure or does it appear to have constituent elements at first encounter?_
  → Complex: 12 VCGs reveal distinct kinds: divine comprehensive knowing (VCG01), covenantal elective knowing (VCG02), self-disclosing knowing (VCG03), human relational knowing (VCG04), ignorance/absence (VCG05), knowledge-as-inner-endowment (VCG06), moral knowledge (VCG07), settled conviction (VCG08), culpable ignorance (VCG09), practical knowing (VCG10), intimate knowing (VCG11), eschatological knowing (VCG12). Knowledge is the most structurally complex characteristic in the cluster.
- *T1.2.3* — _What is the current best working description of this characteristic — encapsulating its constitutional location, the faculties it primarily …_
  → The relational-covenantal inner state of knowing — spanning from God's comprehensive knowing of all things (VCG01) through the covenant-defining mutual knowing of God and people (VCG02/VCG04) to the content-based knowing of facts, persons, and skills (VCG10). Its defining mode is relational-experiential (ya.da), not merely cognitive storage. Its eschatological destiny is universal knowledge of the LORD (VCG12). Hos 6:3, Pro 1:7, Hab 2:14.
- *T1.3.1* — _What is the structural opposite of this characteristic — the inner-being reality that stands against or excludes it?_
  → VCG05 (Hos 4:6 anchor: not-knowing as destruction of the people); VCG09 (Rom 10:3 anchor: culpable ignorance). G0050 agnoeō (to be ignorant) is the lexical opposite.
- *T1.3.2* — _What does this characteristic explicitly exclude or resist?_
  → VCG05 (Hos 4:6): "my people are destroyed for lack of knowledge" — knowledge excludes and resists ignorance-as-destruction. VCB09 (Rom 10:3): self-righteousness that ignores God's righteousness — knowledge of God excludes the ignorance of self-directed seeking.
- *T1.3.3* — _What is this characteristic not — where does it end and something else begin?_
  → Knowledge (M15-C) is not: the perceptive faculty that grasps it (M15-B); the wisdom-character it serves (M15-A); the discernment that applies it (M15-D). Knowledge is the content held, not the faculty (M15-B) or the application (M15-D).
- *T1.4.1* — _In what distinct ways does this characteristic operate within the inner person?_
  → Multiple modes following the 12 VCGs: divine comprehensive knowing (VCG01: Psa 139:6), elective covenantal knowing (VCG02: Amo 3:2), self-disclosing knowing (VCG03: Jos 4:24), human relational knowing of God (VCG04: Hos 6:3), ignorance/absence (VCG05: Hos 4:6), knowledge-as-endowment (VCG06: Pro 1:7), moral knowledge (VCG07: Gen 2:17), settled conviction (VCG08: Rom 8:28), culpable ignorance (VCG09: Rom 10:3), practical knowing (VCG10: Gen 8:11), intimate knowing (VCG11: Gen 4:1), eschatological knowing (VCG12: Hab 2:14).
- *T1.4.2* — _Does this characteristic operate differently depending on context, direction, or constitutional level?_
  → VCG01–VCG03 (divine modes: comprehensive, elective, self-disclosing). VCG04–VCG10 (human modes: relational, absent, endowment, moral, conviction, ignorance, practical). VCG11 (intimate mode). VCG12 (eschatological mode). The operating mode maps precisely to the constitutional-relational level.
- *T1.4.3* — _Does this characteristic have a communicative or speech-based mode of operation — and if so, how does it function?_
  → VCG03 (self-disclosing knowing: Jos 4:24 — "that all the peoples of the earth may know that the hand of the LORD is mighty"). Knowledge is communicated — God discloses himself through historical acts so that the nations may know.
- *T1.5.1* — _What is the first or most immediate inner-being response to receiving or encountering this characteristic?_
  → VCG04 (Hos 6:3): pressing on to know — the immediate response to awakening to the reality of God-knowing is urgency of pursuit. VCG08 (Rom 8:28 anchor): oida as settled conviction — the immediate inner state produced by knowledge is certainty/stability.
- *T1.5.2* — _Is the immediate response consistent across the verse evidence, or does it vary?_
  → Consistent in the covenantal-relational register: pursuit, conviction, relational orientation. Varies by the kind of knowledge (practical knowing in VCG10 produces different immediate responses than covenantal knowing in VCG04).
- *T1.5.3* — _Where the verse evidence is silent on immediate response, note this explicitly._
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T1.6.1* — _What does this characteristic produce in the inner being over time?_
  → Hos 6:3 (VCG04 anchor) corpus: deepening covenantal relationship with God. Pro 1:7 (VCG06 anchor) corpus: accumulated inner wisdom that is guarded and transmitted. VCG08 (Rom 8:28): settled inner conviction that provides stability.
- *T1.6.2* — _What states, qualities, capacities, or orientations does sustained exposure to or possession of this characteristic establish?_
  → Deepening relational orientation, settled conviction, accumulated wisdom-endowment (Hos 6:3, Rom 8:28, Pro 1:7).
- *T1.6.3* — _Does the sustained effect differ from the immediate response — and if so, how?_
  → Uniformly yes across all sub-groups. The immediate response is a specific act or opening; the sustained effect is a constituted quality or orientation formed over time. The pattern is consistent across the cluster: encounter/reception → immediate cognitive/volitional/affective opening → sustained formation of character/orientation/capacity. This is a cluster-level pattern.
- *T1.7.1* — _What inner conditions or orientations enable genuine reception of this characteristic?_
  → Covenantal orientation (Hos 6:3 VCG04 anchor: "let us press on to know"); fear of the Lord (Pro 1:7 VCG06 anchor: "the fear of the LORD is the beginning of knowledge").
- *T1.7.2* — _What inner conditions block, distort, or prevent reception?_
  → VCG05 (Hos 4:6): "my people are destroyed for lack of knowledge" — implicit blocking by not seeking. VCG09 (Rom 10:3 anchor): self-righteousness blocks reception of God's righteousness/knowledge.
- *T1.7.3* — _What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic but does not receive it?_
  → VCG09 (Rom 10:3 anchor): self-righteousness — the person who encounters God's righteousness but is occupied by their own projects. VCG05 (Hos 4:6): the people destroyed for lack — not refusing exactly but not seeking.
- *T1.8.1* — _What is the primary inner-being dimension of this characteristic from the programme's dimension vocabulary?_
  → Relational-covenantal (knowing as relational state). Secondary: cognitive (held content), moral (knowledge of good and evil, VCG07). Evidence: Hos 6:3 (pressing to know the LORD), Gen 4:1 (ya.da in intimate knowing), Amo 3:2 (elective knowing).
- *T1.8.2* — _What evidence from the verse evidence supports this classification?_
  → Hos 6:3: relational pursuit. Amo 3:2: elective-covenantal knowing. Gen 4:1: intimate knowing.
- *T1.8.3* — _Does this characteristic carry secondary dimensions — and if so, what are they, and do they compete with the primary classification?_
  → Cognitive (content) dimension is secondary to relational-covenantal primary. In VCG10 (practical knowing), the relational dimension recedes — these may be in minor tension within the sub-group. The relational-covenantal is definitionally primary (Hos 6:3, VCG04 anchor).
<!-- /EVIDENCE -->


**Key verses for Knowledge as inner content and covenantal knowing:**

**Psa 139:6** (H1847 da.at) [M15-C-VCG01]
> Psa 139:6 Such knowledge is too wonderful for me; it is high ; I cannot attain it .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "such knowledge is too wonderful for me; it is high; I cannot attain it" — **FLAGGED: belongs in C-12 (divine knowledge)**

**Amo 3:2** (H3045 ya.da) [M15-C-VCG02]
> Amo 3:2 “You only have I known of all the families of the earth ; therefore I will punish you for all your iniquities .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "You only have I known of all the families of the earth" — God's elective knowing of Israel; ya.da as covenantal election

**Jos 4:24** (H3045 ya.da) [M15-C-VCG03]
> Jos 4:24 so that all the peoples of the earth may know that the hand of the Lord is mighty , that you may fear the Lord your God forever .”

**Hos 6:3** (H3045 ya.da) [M15-C-VCG04]
> Hos 6:3 Let us know ; let us press on to know the Lord ; his going out is sure as the dawn ; he will come to us as the showers , as the spring rains that water the earth .”
_Meaning of the term here:_ "let us know; let us press on to know the Lord" — covenantal knowing as the pursuit

**Hos 4:6** (H1847 da.at) [M15-C-VCG05]
> Hos 4:6 My people are destroyed for lack of knowledge ; because you have rejected knowledge , I reject you from being a priest to me. And since you have forgotten the law of your God , I also will forget your children .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "my people destroyed for lack of knowledge"

**Pro 1:7** (H1847 da.at) [M15-C-VCG06]
> Pro 1:7 The fear of the Lord is the beginning of knowledge ; fools despise wisdom and instruction .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "the fear of the Lord is the beginning of knowledge"

**Gen 2:17** (H1847 da.at) [M15-C-VCG07]
> Gen 2:17 but of the tree of the knowledge of good and evil you shall not eat , for in the day that you eat of it you shall surely die .”
_Meaning of the term here:_ "of the tree of the knowledge of good and evil you shall not eat" — da.at as what was placed off-limits; moral-constitutional boundary

**Rom 8:28** (G6063 oida) [M15-C-VCG08]
> Rom 8:28 And we know that for those who love God all things work together for good , for those who are called according to his purpose .

**Rom 10:3** (G0050 agnoeō) [M15-C-VCG09]
> Rom 10:3 For , being ignorant of the righteousness of God , and seeking to establish their own , they did not submit to God’s righteousness .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "ignorant of the righteousness of God" — agnoeō of God's righteousness producing self-righteousness

**Gen 8:11** (H3045 ya.da) [M15-C-VCG10]
> Gen 8:11 And the dove came back to him in the evening , and behold , in her mouth was a freshly plucked olive leaf . So Noah knew that the waters had subsided from the earth .

**Gen 4:1** (H3045 ya.da) [M15-C-VCG11]
> Gen 4:1 Now Adam knew Eve his wife , and she conceived and bore Cain , saying , “I have gotten a man with the help of the Lord .”

**Hab 2:14** (H3045 ya.da) [M15-C-VCG12]
> Hab 2:14 For the earth will be filled with the knowledge of the glory of the Lord as the waters cover the sea .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "earth will be filled with the knowledge of the glory of the Lord" — eschatological covenantal knowing filling all creation


### 5.4 Discernment and practical judgment

**T4 — Relational Interfaces**

- *T4.1.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating from God toward the human person — and if so, how?_
  → VCG03 (Gen 15:6): divine crediting of faith as righteousness. VCG01 (Isa 52:13): the Servant's sa.khal as divinely-attributed quality. VCG07 (2Cor 10:4): divine weapons supplied to demolish human strongholds.
- *T4.1.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about the basis on which God extends this characteristic — is it conditional, unconditional, covenantal, or re…_
  → VCG03 (Gen 15:6): God's evaluative response to Abraham's faith — divine initiative in the act of crediting.
- *T4.1.3* — _What does God's extension of this characteristic reveal about his disposition toward the human person?_
  → VCG03 (Gen 15:6): the human receives righteous-status through divine crediting. VCG01: sa.khal enables exaltation.
- *T4.2.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in the human person's movement toward God — in seeking, supplication, worship, or…_
  → VCG02 (1Cor 11:31): self-discernment before God. VCG01 (sa.khal corpus): attending to God's revealed acts and ways.
- *T4.2.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about the inner posture required for this movement?_
  → VCG02: willingness to self-examine. VCG01: attending to God's revealed acts and ways.
- *T4.2.3* — _What does the human-to-God direction of this characteristic reveal about the person's relationship with God?_
  → Self-discernment before God (VCG02 1Cor 11:31) reveals the relationship as one of honest accountability: the person who self-examines does so before a God who already knows and who has established the standard. Human-to-God discernment is self-evaluation in the presence of the divine Judge who credits rightly.
- *T4.3.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic being extended by one person toward another — and if so, how does it operate in that giving…_
  → VCG04 (cha.shav assessments): human assessments shared in discourse. VCG06 (a.rum): prudent person manages what they give in social contexts.
- *T4.3.2* — _What inner conditions or orientations in the giver enable genuine extension of this characteristic?_
  → Evaluative judgment expressed in speech or action.
- *T4.3.3* — _What does the evidence reveal about what the person must have received or become before they can genuinely give this characteristic?_
  → The prudent person (VCG06) who knows what to conceal and what to disclose governs the giving by inner discernment.
- *T4.4.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic being received by a person from another — and if so, how does it operate in that reception?_
  → VCG05 (ta.am): receiving in M15-D is testing-what-is-received — active evaluation of what comes in.
- *T4.4.2* — _What inner conditions enable or block reception of this characteristic from another person?_
  → VCG05 (ta.am): the palate that actually tastes rather than swallowing without testing — active evaluative receptivity.
- *T4.4.3* — _What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic from another but does not receive it?_
  → VCG05 (ta.am — the fool who does not taste/test): the person who encounters discernment from another and does not receive it acts rashly. The inner state is ungoverned-reactive — the evaluative faculty that could be engaged remains dormant or misdirected.
- *T4.5.1* — _Does the evidence indicate whether this characteristic operates differently within existing relational bonds versus across relational distan…_
  → VCG06 (a.rum): the prudent vs fool boundary — discernment as the character-marker that distinguishes.
- *T4.5.2* — _Does this characteristic operate within covenantal contexts only, or does it cross covenantal boundaries?_
  → Character is the boundary: the discerning person vs the one whose perceptive capacity is misdirected.
- *T4.5.3* — _What does the evidence reveal about the relational scope of this characteristic — who is included and who is not?_
  → VCG06 (a.rum — the prudent person): discernment's scope is characterological — those who have formed the wise perceptive character. VCG03 (Gen 15:6): the scope of divine crediting is faith-response — available to anyone who trusts as Abraham trusted.
- *T4.6.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in relation to other spiritual beings — angelic or adversarial — and if so, how?_
  → VCG07 (2Cor 10:4): strongholds and arguments include spiritually-adversarial cognitive structures.
- *T4.6.2* — _Is this characteristic a site of adversarial activity — something that can be attacked, distorted, or weaponised by adversarial spiritual po…_
  → VCG07 (2Cor 10:4-5): adversarial cognitive structures in the inner person — spiritual beings building strongholds in the mind.

  → Evidence is not silent — VCG02 self-examination before God. No silence.

  → Evidence is not silent — evaluative judgments expressed in speech and action. No silence.

  → Evidence is not silent — VCG05 (ta.am — active testing of what is received). No silence.

  → Evidence is not silent — VCG06 and VCG03 establish boundaries. No silence.

**T5 — Formative and Developmental Dimension**

- *T5.1.1* — _Does this characteristic produce transformation in the person — and if so, does it change the person's condition, the person's orientation t…_
  → VCG05 (Heb 5:14): discernment trained through repeated practice — progressive formation. VCG01 (sa.khal): producing success through sustained wise action implies ongoing formation.
- *T5.1.2* — _Is the transformation produced by this characteristic reversible or irreversible in the verse evidence?_
  → Both: discernment capacity deepens (VCG05 training); and discernment transforms the person (VCG01 — success in conduct; VCG02 — freedom from condemnation).
- *T5.1.3* — _If the evidence is silent on transformation, note this explicitly._
  → Progressive: VCG05 (Heb 5:14 "trained by constant practice" — no sudden formation except VCG03 instantaneous divine crediting).
- *T5.2.1* — _Does the verse evidence describe a sequence of inner states through which this characteristic moves the person — a before, during, and after…_
  → Training sequence: immature/undiscerning → exposure to training → developing discernment. Divine crediting sequence: faith-act → divine evaluation → righteous-status credited.
- *T5.2.2* — _What are those states, and what does the sequence reveal about how this characteristic works?_
  → VCG05: the prior state is undiscernment (solid food is for the mature, not infants). VCG03: faith-response (Abraham's trust) is prior to divine crediting.
- *T5.2.3* — _If the evidence is silent on sequence, note this explicitly._
  → VCG01: wise and successful action. VCG02: freedom from condemnation. VCG05: mature Christian life.
- *T5.3.1* — _What mechanism does this characteristic use to produce change in the person — discipline, encounter, gradual formation, sudden transformatio…_
  → Formation: constant practice (VCG05 Heb 5:14). Deepening: repeated self-examination (VCG02), sustained wise action (VCG01). Loss/perversion: misdirection of the perceptive faculty (VCG06 a.rum as cunning rather than wisdom when directed wrongly).
- *T5.3.2* — _Does the evidence distinguish between mechanisms in different contexts?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T5.3.3* — _If the evidence is silent on mechanism, note this explicitly._
  → VCG06 (a.rum misdirected): the neutral perceptive faculty becoming cunning when directed wrongly. The same capacity, wrongly directed, becomes its own perversion.
- *T5.4.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in relation to suffering or affliction — as a response to it, a product of it, or…_
  → VCG02 (1Cor 11:31): self-examination in the Eucharistic context — failure of self-discernment produces bodily illness and death (1Cor 11:30). The consequence of failed discernment is suffering.
- *T5.4.3* — _If the evidence is silent on the relationship to suffering, note this explicitly._
  → VCG02's consequence of bodily illness for failed discernment (1Cor 11:30) makes suffering a consequence of discernment-failure, not a formative agent of discernment itself. The formative relationship of suffering to discernment is largely silent. Partial silence confirmed.
- *T5.5.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic participating in the longer arc of character formation and sanctification — shaping the per…_
  → VCG02 (1Cor 11:31): self-discernment preventing judgment is a sanctification discipline. VCG05 (Heb 5:14): trained discernment as mark of mature Christian formation.
- *T5.5.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about the role of this characteristic in that longer arc?_
  → VCG01 (Isa 52:13): the Servant's sa.khal is the paradigm — Christlikeness in discernment is the successful, God-pleasing, redemptively-effective discernment the Servant models.
- *T5.6.1* — _Does the verse evidence point this characteristic toward an eschatological fullness — a future state toward which its present operation is o…_
  → VCG01 (Isa 52:13): the Servant's sa.khal producing exaltation — eschatological exaltation-through-discernment. VCG03 (Gen 15:6): justified standing before God as eschatological consequence of divine crediting.
- *T5.6.2* — _What does the present experience of this characteristic anticipate about its future fullness?_
  → Exaltation-through-discernment (Isa 52:13) and justified standing (Gen 15:6 VCG03) — both are partial eschatological forms in M15-D.
- *T5.7.3* — _If T2.8 found no deposit, note this explicitly and close T5.7._
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]

  → Evidence is not silent — VCG02 (self-discernment preventing judgment) and VCG05 (trained discernment as maturity-marker) are explicitly sanctification-linked. No silence.

  → No body-deposit. VCG05 (ta.am/tasting): the gustatory image is figurative for inner discernment; taste is the metaphor vehicle, not the deposit site.
- *T5.7.2* — _Does the evidence indicate generational consequence — a deposit carried forward beyond the individual?_
  → No generational deposit evidenced. Discernment is formed in each person individually through practice (VCG05) and divine crediting (VCG03). Silence.

<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch5 — T1 findings for Discernment and practical judgment -->

**T1 — Definition**

- *T1.1.1* — _What is this characteristic called in the programme — and what does the name itself signal about its essential nature?_
  → H7919A sa.khal (be prudent): to have practical inner sense that produces effective action. G1252 diakrinō: to judge/discriminate/doubt — the inner act of making evaluative distinctions. H6175 a.rum (prudent): sharp-eyed inner perceptiveness that can serve wisdom or cunning (directionally neutral). The name signals: discernment is applied perception — the inner act of making right distinctions in concrete situations. Gen 3:1 (VCG06 anchor), 1Cor 11:31 (VCG02 anchor).
- *T1.1.2* — _What do the primary Hebrew and Greek terms reveal at the definitional level — before deeper lexical analysis begins?_
  → Sa.khal (verb): practical inner sense → effective action. Diakrinō (verb): to judge/separate/doubt. A.rum (adjective): sharp perceptiveness — directionally neutral. Ta.am (verb): to taste — the palate as figure for inner discernment (Psa 34:8, VCG05 anchor). The terms reveal: discernment operates through both analytic distinction (diakrinō) and intuitive-perceptive sensitivity (ta.am, a.rum). 1Cor 11:31 (VCG02 anchor).
- *T1.1.3* — _Does the name carry directional, relational, or constitutional implications that orient the enquiry from the outset?_
  → Constitutional and directional: a.rum is neutral in direction (Gen 3:1: serpent; Prov: prudent person) — the inner quality is constitutional but its direction is morally determined by the object toward which it is applied.
- *T1.2.1* — _What kind of inner-being phenomenon does this characteristic appear to be — an act, a disposition, a condition, a quality, or something else…_
  → An applied perceptive act — the inner act of making right evaluative distinctions in concrete situations. 1Cor 11:31 (VCG02 anchor): self-judgment as a concrete application. Gen 15:6 (VCG03 anchor): divine crediting as evaluation.
- *T1.2.2* — _Is this characteristic simple in structure or does it appear to have constituent elements at first encounter?_
  → Constituent elements: prudent-effective action (VCG01), evaluative discrimination (VCG02), crediting/reckoning (VCG03), deliberative assessment (VCG04), palate-as-figure for inner discernment (VCG05), neutral shrewd perceptiveness (VCG06), cognitive argumentation (VCG07). Isa 52:13 (VCG01 anchor).
- *T1.2.3* — _What is the current best working description of this characteristic — encapsulating its constitutional location, the faculties it primarily …_
  → The applied inner perceptive act of making right evaluative distinctions in concrete situations — prudent assessment, moral discrimination, crediting, deliberative evaluation. Directionally neutral in some of its terms (a.rum serves wisdom or cunning; cha.shav devises for good or ill). Primary location: heart/inner reasoning. Isa 52:13, 1Cor 11:31, Gen 15:6.
- *T1.3.1* — _What is the structural opposite of this characteristic — the inner-being reality that stands against or excludes it?_
  → The undiscerning/senseless state; VCG04's pattern of wrong assessment (Psa 73:16 anchor: "when I thought how to understand this, it seemed to me a wearisome task"); VCG06's direction-inverted shrewdness (Gen 3:1: the serpent).
- *T1.3.2* — _What does this characteristic explicitly exclude or resist?_
  → Wrong assessment (VCG04: Psa 73:16); undiscriminating acceptance (VCG02: 1Cor 11:31 — self-judgment excludes unexamined receiving of the Lord's supper).
- *T1.3.3* — _What is this characteristic not — where does it end and something else begin?_
  → Discernment (M15-D) is not: the constituted wisdom-character (M15-A) it expresses; the perceptive faculty (M15-B) that feeds it; the knowledge content (M15-C) it applies. Discernment is the applied act of making right distinctions in situations.
- *T1.4.1* — _In what distinct ways does this characteristic operate within the inner person?_
  → Seven modes per VCG structure: prudent-effective action (VCG01: Isa 52:13), evaluative discrimination/doubt (VCG02: 1Cor 11:31), crediting/imputing (VCG03: Gen 15:6), deliberative assessment (VCG04: Psa 73:16), palate-figure for inner discernment (VCG05: Psa 34:8), neutral shrewd perceptiveness (VCG06: Gen 3:1), cognitive argumentation (VCG07: Rom 2:15).
- *T1.4.2* — _Does this characteristic operate differently depending on context, direction, or constitutional level?_
  → VCG06 (serpent: a.rum in adversarial-cunning context). VCG01 (Servant: sa.khal in divine-aligned action). The same inner quality operates differently by the direction it is pointed — toward God or toward self/adversarial ends.
- *T1.4.3* — _Does this characteristic have a communicative or speech-based mode of operation — and if so, how does it function?_
  → VCG07 (Rom 2:15 anchor): logismos — the cognitive argumentation that accuses or excuses before the conscience. This is an inner deliberative speech — the conscience as interior tribunal.
- *T1.5.1* — _What is the first or most immediate inner-being response to receiving or encountering this characteristic?_
  → VCG02 (1Cor 11:31): self-judgment in the immediate — the first response of activated discernment is self-examination. VCG05 (Psa 34:8 anchor): "taste and see that the LORD is good" — the immediate response to discernment-as-taste is experiential confirmation.
- *T1.5.2* — _Is the immediate response consistent across the verse evidence, or does it vary?_
  → Varies by mode: self-examination (VCG02), effective action (VCG01), taste-based confirmation (VCG05). Not uniform but consistently action-directed.
- *T1.5.3* — _Where the verse evidence is silent on immediate response, note this explicitly._
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T1.6.1* — _What does this characteristic produce in the inner being over time?_
  → Isa 52:13 (VCG01 anchor): effective wise action. 1Cor 11:31 (VCG02 anchor): self-awareness that avoids judgment. The sustained effect is: the person who exercises discernment over time develops reliable judgment.
- *T1.6.2* — _What states, qualities, capacities, or orientations does sustained exposure to or possession of this characteristic establish?_
  → Reliable judgment, self-awareness, effective action (Isa 52:13, 1Cor 11:31).
- *T1.6.3* — _Does the sustained effect differ from the immediate response — and if so, how?_
  → Uniformly yes across all sub-groups. The immediate response is a specific act or opening; the sustained effect is a constituted quality or orientation formed over time. The pattern is consistent across the cluster: encounter/reception → immediate cognitive/volitional/affective opening → sustained formation of character/orientation/capacity. This is a cluster-level pattern.
- *T1.7.1* — _What inner conditions or orientations enable genuine reception of this characteristic?_
  → Self-examination posture (1Cor 11:31 VCG02 anchor); taste/openness to experience (Psa 34:8 VCG05 anchor: "taste and see").
- *T1.7.2* — _What inner conditions block, distort, or prevent reception?_
  → VCG06 (Gen 3:1): direction-inversion — when the shrewd capacity is turned away from God; VCG04 (Psa 73:16): "when I thought how to understand this, it seemed to me a wearisome task" — the difficulty of discernment when it requires honest engagement with troubling evidence.
- *T1.7.3* — _What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic but does not receive it?_
  → VCG04 (Psa 73:16 anchor): the person who finds discernment too difficult — the "wearisome task" — remains in confusion about the problem they cannot resolve.
- *T1.8.1* — _What is the primary inner-being dimension of this characteristic from the programme's dimension vocabulary?_
  → Cognitive-evaluative (making right distinctions through applied perception). Secondary: moral (distinguishing good from evil), volitional (crediting and imputing). Evidence: 1Cor 11:31 (self-judgment), Isa 52:13 (prudent effective action).
- *T1.8.2* — _What evidence from the verse evidence supports this classification?_
  → 1Cor 11:31: self-judgment. Gen 15:6: crediting act.
- *T1.8.3* — _Does this characteristic carry secondary dimensions — and if so, what are they, and do they compete with the primary classification?_
  → Moral-evaluative and volitional secondary dimensions serve the primary cognitive-evaluative. No competition.

**Key verses for Discernment and practical judgment:**

**Isa 52:13** (H7919A sa.khal) [M15-D-VCG01]
> Isa 52:13 Behold , my servant shall act wisely ; he shall be high and lifted up , and shall be exalted .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "my servant shall act wisely; he shall be high and lifted up" — sa.khal as Servant-mission character

**1Cor 11:31** (G1252 diakrinō) [M15-D-VCG02]
> 1Cor 11:31 But if we judged ourselves truly, we would not be judged .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "if we judged ourselves truly, we would not be judged" — reflexive diakrinō; self-discernment

**Gen 15:6** (H2803H cha.shav) [M15-D-VCG03]
> Gen 15:6 And he believed the Lord , and he counted it to him as righteousness .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "counted it to him as righteousness" — God's inner act of moral reckoning; faith assessed and credited

**Psa 73:16** (H2803J cha.shav) [M15-D-VCG04]
> Psa 73:16 But when I thought how to understand this , it seemed to me a wearisome task,
_Meaning of the term here:_ "when I thought how to understand this, it seemed wearisome" — cha.shav as the sustained inner effort to make sense of a problem

**Psa 34:8** (H2938 ta.am) [M15-D-VCG05]
> Psa 34:8 Oh, taste and see that the Lord is good ! Blessed is the man who takes refuge in him !
_Meaning of the term here:_ "taste and see that the Lord is good" — ta.am as experiential inner apprehension; the invitation to direct inner experience of God's character

**Gen 3:1** (H6175 a.rum) [M15-D-VCG06]
> Gen 3:1 Now the serpent was more crafty than any other beast of the field that the Lord God had made . He said to the woman , “Did God actually say , ‘You shall not eat of any tree in the garden ’?”
_Meaning of the term here:_ "the serpent was more crafty" — a.rum in its dark register; the same shrewdness serving deception

**Rom 2:15** (G3053 logismos) [M15-D-VCG07]
> Rom 2:15 They show that the work of the law is written on their hearts , while their conscience also bears witness , and their conflicting thoughts accuse or even excuse them
_Meaning of the term here:_ "conflicting thoughts accuse or excuse" — logismos as moral inner reasoning functioning alongside conscience


### 5.5 Deliberative planning, counsel, and purposive intent

**T4 — Relational Interfaces**

- *T4.1.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating from God toward the human person — and if so, how?_
  → VCG03 (Isa 14:24): divine counsel is irresistible — moves from divine purpose to historical outcome. VCG08 (pronoia): God's providence as purposive foresight for creation.
- *T4.1.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about the basis on which God extends this characteristic — is it conditional, unconditional, covenantal, or re…_
  → VCG03 (Isa 14:24): divine counsel is self-generating — requires nothing outside itself.
- *T4.1.3* — _What does God's extension of this characteristic reveal about his disposition toward the human person?_
  → VCG03: divine counsel confronts — human either aligns with it or is overridden. VCG08: God-given foresight enables wise provision.
- *T4.2.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in the human person's movement toward God — in seeking, supplication, worship, or…_
  → VCG05 (Pro 16:9): human planning submitted to God's governance. VCG07 inverse (Exo 7:23): Pharaoh's refusal to attend — the blocking of human-to-God movement.
- *T4.2.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about the inner posture required for this movement?_
  → VCG05: the humility to submit the heart's planning to God's governance.
- *T4.2.3* — _What does the human-to-God direction of this characteristic reveal about the person's relationship with God?_
  → Human purposing submitted to divine governance (Pro 16:9 VCG05) reveals the relationship as one of sovereign-creature: the person plans; God establishes the steps. The relationship is neither deterministic (the human plans genuinely) nor autonomous (God governs the outcome).
- *T4.3.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic being extended by one person toward another — and if so, how does it operate in that giving…_
  → VCG04 (2Sa 16:23): counsel as the primary giving form — the counselor gives their inner wisdom to the counselee.
- *T4.3.2* — _What inner conditions or orientations in the giver enable genuine extension of this characteristic?_
  → Oral wisdom offered in governance context (ya.ats as counsel). Considered judgment (gnōmē) shared in community.
- *T4.3.3* — _What does the evidence reveal about what the person must have received or become before they can genuinely give this characteristic?_
  → VCG04: inner wisdom (M15-A) and the ability to form effective counsel (M15-E) are the preconditions of giving wise counsel.
- *T4.4.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic being received by a person from another — and if so, how does it operate in that reception?_
  → VCG04 (2Sa 16:23): the king receives counsel. VCG02 (gnōmē, 1Cor 7:25): the community receiving Paul's considered judgment.
- *T4.4.2* — _What inner conditions enable or block reception of this characteristic from another person?_
  → VCG04: trust in the counselor's wisdom and willingness to be governed by external wisdom.
- *T4.4.3* — _What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic from another but does not receive it?_
  → The person who does not receive counsel (as Rehoboam rejected the elders' counsel, 1Ki 12 proximate context) has an inner state of self-determined autonomy — the purposive faculty closed to external wisdom, turned fully inward and self-directed.
- *T4.5.1* — _Does the evidence indicate whether this characteristic operates differently within existing relational bonds versus across relational distan…_
  → VCG03: divine counsel as the boundary against which human counsel stands — no counsel can override divine purpose (Isa 14:27).
- *T4.5.2* — _Does this characteristic operate within covenantal contexts only, or does it cross covenantal boundaries?_
  → Divine counsel as the absolute boundary of human purposing — no human plan can override it.
- *T4.5.3* — _What does the evidence reveal about the relational scope of this characteristic — who is included and who is not?_
  → VCG04 (governance counseling): within the authority relationship — the counselor speaks to the one who bears authority. VCG03 (divine irresistible counsel): scope is universal — all human and cosmic events fall within it.
- *T4.6.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in relation to other spiritual beings — angelic or adversarial — and if so, how?_
  → VCG03 (Isa 14:24-27): the irresistible divine purpose operating over against human and adversarial counsel.
- *T4.6.4* — _If the evidence is silent on the spiritual beings interface, note this explicitly._
  → Spiritual beings interface is largely silent in M15-E's direct VCG evidence. VCG03 (divine counsel) operates at the divine level, but adversarial spiritual beings are not directly named as engaging with purposive counsel in M15-E's VCGs. Silence confirmed for adversarial interface in M15-E.

**T1 — Definition**

- *T1.1.1* — _What is this characteristic called in the programme — and what does the name itself signal about its essential nature?_
  → H3289 ya.ats (to advise): the act of giving or seeking counsel. G1014 boulomai: purposive willing — the inner volitional intent. H2803I cha.shav (to devise): purposive devising in the heart. G4307 pronoia: foresight — deliberate forward-looking intent. The name signals: counsel and purposing are forward-oriented inner activities — the person reaches forward in intention before acting. 2Sa 16:23 (VCG04 anchor), Jer 29:11 (VCG05 anchor).
- *T1.1.2* — _What do the primary Hebrew and Greek terms reveal at the definitional level — before deeper lexical analysis begins?_
  → Ya.ats (verb/noun): to counsel / the counselor. Boulomai (verb): to will, to purpose. Gnōmē (noun): considered resolution — the formed position. Pronoia (noun): foresight — forward-seeing purposive intent. The terms reveal: purposive intent spans from advice-giving (social) to inner volitional will (personal) to irresistible divine purpose (VCG03 context). Isa 14:24 (VCG03 anchor).
- *T1.1.3* — _Does the name carry directional, relational, or constitutional implications that orient the enquiry from the outset?_
  → Directional forward-orientation: the naming of ya.ats, boulomai, pronoia all point toward the future. Relational: counsel is inherently inter-personal (VCG04 — the counselor/counselee relationship). Constitutional: purposive intent becomes irrevocable in its strongest form (VCG06: za.mam — Lam 2:17).
- *T1.2.1* — _What kind of inner-being phenomenon does this characteristic appear to be — an act, a disposition, a condition, a quality, or something else…_
  → A forward-oriented volitional activity — purposing, planning, willing toward a future state. Jer 29:11 (VCG05 anchor): deliberate purposive devising in the heart.
- *T1.2.2* — _Is this characteristic simple in structure or does it appear to have constituent elements at first encounter?_
  → Constituent elements: volitional willing (VCG01), considered resolution (VCG02), irresistible divine counsel (VCG03), human counseling relationship (VCG04), purposive devising (VCG05), irrevocable human purposing (VCG06), heart-attention directing (VCG07), foresight capacity (VCG08). 2Pe 3:9 (VCG01 anchor).
- *T1.2.3* — _What is the current best working description of this characteristic — encapsulating its constitutional location, the faculties it primarily …_
  → The inner capacity for forward-oriented purposive willing — forming deliberate intent, devising plans, giving and receiving counsel, making irrevocable decisions. Spans from the human counselor's wisdom (2Sa 16:23) to God's irresistible sovereign purpose (Isa 14:24). Primary constitutional location: the heart (Pro 16:9 proximate: "the heart plans its way"). 2Sa 16:23, Jer 29:11, Isa 14:24.
- *T1.3.1* — _What is the structural opposite of this characteristic — the inner-being reality that stands against or excludes it?_
  → The person without inner purpose; the refusal of counsel (VCG03 corpus: nations who refuse God's counsel); VCG07 (Exo 7:23 anchor: Pharaoh "not setting his heart" — the opposite of heart-directed purposive attention).
- *T1.3.2* — _What does this characteristic explicitly exclude or resist?_
  → Purposeless drifting; refusal of counsel; Pharaoh's not-setting-the-heart (VCG07 anchor: Exo 7:23).
- *T1.3.3* — _What is this characteristic not — where does it end and something else begin?_
  → Counsel and purposing (M15-E) is not: mere knowing (M15-C); constituted wisdom (M15-A); discernment as situational evaluation (M15-D). It is the forward-reaching volitional act that produces plan, decision, or counsel.
- *T1.4.1* — _In what distinct ways does this characteristic operate within the inner person?_
  → Eight modes: volitional willing (VCG01: 2Pe 3:9), considered resolution (VCG02: Rev 17:17), irresistible divine counsel (VCG03: Isa 14:24), human counseling relationship (VCG04: 2Sa 16:23), purposive devising (VCG05: Jer 29:11), irrevocable purposing (VCG06: Lam 2:17), heart-attention directing (VCG07: Exo 7:23), foresight (VCG08: Rom 13:14).
- *T1.4.2* — _Does this characteristic operate differently depending on context, direction, or constitutional level?_
  → VCG03 (divine irresistible counsel). VCG04 (human counselor-counselee relationship). VCG01 (individual volitional willing). The purposing operates at divine, communal, and individual levels with different characteristics at each.
- *T1.4.3* — _Does this characteristic have a communicative or speech-based mode of operation — and if so, how does it function?_
  → VCG04 (2Sa 16:23 anchor): counsel is by definition a communicative act — wisdom given through speech. The counseling relationship (VCG04) is the clearest example.
- *T1.5.1* — _What is the first or most immediate inner-being response to receiving or encountering this characteristic?_
  → VCG04 (2Sa 16:23): receiving counsel — the counselee immediately has direction that resolves uncertainty. The immediate response to good counsel received is clarity of path.
- *T1.5.2* — _Is the immediate response consistent across the verse evidence, or does it vary?_
  → Varies: clarity of path (receiving counsel), resolution of will (boulomai), formation of plan (ya.ats).
- *T1.5.3* — _Where the verse evidence is silent on immediate response, note this explicitly._
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T1.6.1* — _What does this characteristic produce in the inner being over time?_
  → 2Sa 16:23 (VCG04 anchor): the trusted counselor's wisdom grows through sustained exercise. The deliberate planner over time becomes the person whose purposes align with outcomes.
- *T1.6.2* — _What states, qualities, capacities, or orientations does sustained exposure to or possession of this characteristic establish?_
  → Trusted wisdom, aligned purposing, effective planning (2Sa 16:23, Jer 29:11).
- *T1.6.3* — _Does the sustained effect differ from the immediate response — and if so, how?_
  → Uniformly yes across all sub-groups. The immediate response is a specific act or opening; the sustained effect is a constituted quality or orientation formed over time. The pattern is consistent across the cluster: encounter/reception → immediate cognitive/volitional/affective opening → sustained formation of character/orientation/capacity. This is a cluster-level pattern.
- *T1.7.1* — _What inner conditions or orientations enable genuine reception of this characteristic?_
  → Humility in seeking counsel (2Sa 16:23 VCG04 context: seeking counsel at all); setting the heart toward God's word (VCG07: the opposite of Pharaoh's refusal, Exo 7:23).
- *T1.7.2* — _What inner conditions block, distort, or prevent reception?_
  → Pharaoh's refusal to set his heart (VCG07: Exo 7:23 anchor): the inner posture of not directing attention toward God's word. Nations' refusal of God's counsel (VCG03 corpus).
- *T1.7.3* — _What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic but does not receive it?_
  → VCG07 (Exo 7:23 anchor): Pharaoh who "did not set his heart to this either" — the inner state is stubbornly oriented elsewhere, immune to signs.
- *T1.8.1* — _What is the primary inner-being dimension of this characteristic from the programme's dimension vocabulary?_
  → Volitional (purposive willing and planning). Secondary: relational (counsel relationship), cognitive (forming the deliberate plan). Evidence: 2Pe 3:9 (boulomai — God's purposive willing), Jer 29:11 (purposive devising in the heart).
- *T1.8.2* — _What evidence from the verse evidence supports this classification?_
  → 2Pe 3:9: God's purposive willing. Jer 29:11: deliberate purposive devising. Isa 14:24: irresistible counsel.
- *T1.8.3* — _Does this characteristic carry secondary dimensions — and if so, what are they, and do they compete with the primary classification?_
  → The relational (counseling relationship) and cognitive (plan formation) are secondary to the volitional primary. No competition; they are modes of the volitional expression.

**Key verses for Deliberative planning, counsel, and purposive intent:**

**2Pe 3:9** (G1014 boulomai) [M15-E-VCG01]
> 2Pe 3:9 The Lord is not slow to fulfill his promise as some count slowness , but is patient toward you , not wishing that any should perish , but that all should reach repentance .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "not wishing that any should perish, but that all should reach repentance" — divine salvific desire

**Rev 17:17** (G1106 gnōmē) [M15-E-VCG02]
> Rev 17:17 for God has put it into their hearts to carry out his purpose by being of one mind and handing over their royal power to the beast , until the words of God are fulfilled .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "God has put it into their hearts to carry out his purpose... until the words of God are fulfilled" — gnōmē divinely placed; human deliberate purpose as instrument of divine sovereignty

**Isa 14:24** (H3289 ya.ats) [M15-E-VCG03]
> Isa 14:24 The Lord of hosts has sworn : “ As I have planned , so shall it be, and as I have purposed , so shall it stand ,
_Meaning of the term here:_ "as I have planned, so shall it be; as I have purposed, so shall it stand"

**2Sa 16:23** (H3289 ya.ats) [M15-E-VCG04]
> 2Sa 16:23 Now in those days the counsel that Ahithophel gave was as if one consulted the word of God ; so was all the counsel of Ahithophel esteemed, both by David and by Absalom .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "counsel of Ahithophel as if one consulted the word of God"

**Jer 29:11** (H2803I cha.shav) [M15-E-VCG05]
> Jer 29:11 For I know the plans I have for you, declares the Lord , plans for welfare and not for evil , to give you a future and a hope .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "plans for welfare and not for evil, to give you a future and a hope"

**Lam 2:17** (H2161 za.mam) [M15-E-VCG06]
> Lam 2:17 The Lord has done what he purposed ; he has carried out his word , which he commanded long ago ; he has thrown down without pity ; he has made the enemy rejoice over you and exalted the might of your foes .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "the Lord has done what he purposed" — divine za.mam fulfilled in Jerusalem's fall

**Exo 7:23** (H7896K shit) [M15-E-VCG07]
> Exo 7:23 Pharaoh turned and went into his house , and he did not take even this to heart .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "he did not take even this to heart" — shit-refusal; heart closed to what should have registered

**Rom 13:14** (G4307 pronoia) [M15-E-VCG08]
> Rom 13:14 But put on the Lord Jesus Christ , and make no provision for the flesh , to gratify its desires .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "make no provision for the flesh, to gratify its desires" — pronoia as forward-provision planning; here refused toward the flesh


### 5.6 Meditative and reflective inner activity

**T4 — Relational Interfaces**

- *T4.1.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating from God toward the human person — and if so, how?_
  → VCG03 (Psa 119:97): God provides the law that becomes the object of meditation. VCG04 (Dan 7:28): God gives the vision that requires meditative holding.
- *T4.1.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about the basis on which God extends this characteristic — is it conditional, unconditional, covenantal, or re…_
  → God's prior giving of the content (law, vision) initiates the meditative cycle.
- *T4.1.3* — _What does God's extension of this characteristic reveal about his disposition toward the human person?_
  → VCG03: sustained meditative engagement produces deeper understanding (Psa 119:99) and love. VCG04: meditative holding of the vision enables appropriate response.
- *T4.2.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in the human person's movement toward God — in seeking, supplication, worship, or…_
  → VCG03 (Psa 119:97): meditation on God's law as a relational act directed toward God in love.
- *T4.2.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about the inner posture required for this movement?_
  → VCG03: love of God's law as the prior affective orientation.
- *T4.2.3* — _What does the human-to-God direction of this characteristic reveal about the person's relationship with God?_
  → Meditation directed toward God through his law (VCG03) reveals the relationship as one of love-sustained dwelling: the person returns to God's word because they love God. The meditative relationship is not mechanical but affective — it is the relationship of one who cannot stop thinking about the one they love.
- *T4.3.2* — _What inner conditions or orientations in the giver enable genuine extension of this characteristic?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T4.3.3* — _What does the evidence reveal about what the person must have received or become before they can genuinely give this characteristic?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T4.3.4* — _If the evidence is silent on the giving direction, note this explicitly._
  → M15-F's giving direction is largely silent in the VCG corpus. Meditation is constitutively inward. The wisdom produced by meditation can be subsequently given through other characteristics (M15-A speech, M15-H logos) but the meditative act itself does not give directly. Silence on direct human-to-human giving through meditation.
- *T4.4.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic being received by a person from another — and if so, how does it operate in that reception?_
  → VCG02 (Matt 1:20 enthumeomai): the meditative-reflective state opens the person to receive divine and human guidance. The receptive inner state is the condition in which disclosure arrives.
- *T4.4.2* — _What inner conditions enable or block reception of this characteristic from another person?_
  → VCG02: the meditative state itself is the condition — being in sustained reflection opens the inner person.
- *T4.4.4* — _If the evidence is silent on the receiving direction, note this explicitly._
  → The receiving direction for M15-F in the human-to-human sense is largely silent. Meditation is not received from another; it is a practice entered into. VCG02 (the meditative state receiving divine disclosure) is a divine-to-human movement, not human-to-human. Silence on human-from-human receiving for M15-F.
- *T4.5.2* — _Does this characteristic operate within covenantal contexts only, or does it cross covenantal boundaries?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T4.5.3* — _What does the evidence reveal about the relational scope of this characteristic — who is included and who is not?_
  → VCG03 (Psa 119:97): the meditating person is the one who loves God's law — the covenantal-devotional circle. The practice presupposes receiving God's word.
- *T4.6.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in relation to other spiritual beings — angelic or adversarial — and if so, how?_
  → VCG02 (Matt 1:20): the angel intervenes in Joseph's meditative state — spiritual beings operate in the meditative-reflective space. VCG04 (Amos 4:13): God declaring what is in the creature's inner reflection.
- *T4.6.2* — _Is this characteristic a site of adversarial activity — something that can be attacked, distorted, or weaponised by adversarial spiritual po…_
  → VCG02 (Matt 1:20): angelic disclosure in the meditative state — positive spiritual being operating through meditation.

**T5 — Formative and Developmental Dimension**

- *T5.1.1* — _Does this characteristic produce transformation in the person — and if so, does it change the person's condition, the person's orientation t…_
  → VCG03 (Psa 119:97-99): sustained meditation produces measurable inner transformation — understanding surpassing teachers.
- *T5.1.2* — _Is the transformation produced by this characteristic reversible or irreversible in the verse evidence?_
  → Both: meditative capacity deepens; and the person is transformed through sustained meditation on God's law (VCG03 — understanding deepens, love grows).
- *T5.1.3* — _If the evidence is silent on transformation, note this explicitly._
  → Slow and cumulative: VCG03 "all the day" suggests sustained, proportional transformation.
- *T5.2.1* — _Does the verse evidence describe a sequence of inner states through which this characteristic moves the person — a before, during, and after…_
  → Meditation sequence: receive God's law → love it → meditate repeatedly → grow in understanding (VCG03). Reflection sequence: face complex situation → enter reflective state → receive disclosure or resolution (VCG02).
- *T5.2.2* — _What are those states, and what does the sequence reveal about how this characteristic works?_
  → VCG03: love of God's law as precondition. VCG02: an unresolved inner situation requiring resolution.
- *T5.2.3* — _If the evidence is silent on sequence, note this explicitly._
  → VCG03: love-deepened-by-understanding; understanding that surpasses teachers.
- *T5.3.1* — _What mechanism does this characteristic use to produce change in the person — discipline, encounter, gradual formation, sudden transformatio…_
  → Formation: sustained repetitive practice (VCG03 "all the day") + divine provision of content. Perversion: the meditative inner activity turned self-ward (VCG01 rich fool's self-enclosed monologue).
- *T5.3.2* — _Does the evidence distinguish between mechanisms in different contexts?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T5.3.3* — _If the evidence is silent on mechanism, note this explicitly._
  → VCG01 (self-enclosed inner monologue): when meditative activity turns inward-self-ward, it becomes futile reasoning. The perversion mechanism: the same inner activity, redirected.
- *T5.4.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in relation to suffering or affliction — as a response to it, a product of it, or…_
  → VCG04 (Dan 7:28): Daniel's meditative holding of the terrifying vision is a form of affliction-management — keeping the vision in heart despite the distress it causes.
- *T5.4.2* — _Does suffering deepen, test, reveal, or produce this characteristic in the person?_
  → VCG04 (Dan 7:28): the terrifying vision requiring meditative holding — suffering/distress as the occasion for deepened meditative engagement.
- *T5.5.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic participating in the longer arc of character formation and sanctification — shaping the per…_
  → VCG03 (Psa 119:97-99): the most explicit sanctification-through-meditation evidence in M15. Sustained meditation on God's law produces understanding greater than teachers.
- *T5.5.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about the role of this characteristic in that longer arc?_
  → VCG03: Christlikeness in M15-F is the formation that comes from sustained dwelling on the mind of God as revealed in law and word — shaped by what one dwells upon.
- *T5.6.2* — _What does the present experience of this characteristic anticipate about its future fullness?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]

  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]

<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch5 — T1 findings for Meditative and reflective inner activity -->

**T1 — Definition**

- *T1.1.1* — _What is this characteristic called in the programme — and what does the name itself signal about its essential nature?_
  → H7878 si.ach / H7881 si.chah (to muse / meditation): the inner activity of turning something over in the mind, dwelling on it. G1260 dialogizomai: to reason within oneself — interior deliberative reasoning. H7920 se.khal: to contemplate with focused attention. The name signals: reflective activity is a sustained inner movement — not static holding but active dwelling. Psa 119:97 (VCG03 anchor), Luk 5:22 (VCG01 anchor).
- *T1.1.2* — _What do the primary Hebrew and Greek terms reveal at the definitional level — before deeper lexical analysis begins?_
  → Si.ach / si.chah (verb/noun): to muse, to meditate, to engage in sustained inner conversation with received material. Dialogizomai (verb): to reason within oneself — interior dialogue. The terms reveal: reflective activity is the inner self in sustained engagement with something beyond itself — it is inherently responsive. Psa 119:97 (VCG03 anchor).
- *T1.1.3* — _Does the name carry directional, relational, or constitutional implications that orient the enquiry from the outset?_
  → Responsive direction: the meditating person turns toward received material (si.ach on God's precepts, Psa 119:97). The direction is inward-and-toward-received-content.
- *T1.2.1* — _What kind of inner-being phenomenon does this characteristic appear to be — an act, a disposition, a condition, a quality, or something else…_
  → A sustained inner activity — the ongoing engagement of the mind with received content. Psa 119:97 (VCG03 anchor): meditation as continuous inner activity ("all the day").
- *T1.2.2* — _Is this characteristic simple in structure or does it appear to have constituent elements at first encounter?_
  → Constituent elements: inner deliberative reasoning (VCG01), sustained reflection producing conceived thoughts (VCG02), meditation on God's precepts (VCG03), focused contemplative attention (VCG04). Psa 119:97 (VCG03 anchor).
- *T1.2.3* — _What is the current best working description of this characteristic — encapsulating its constitutional location, the faculties it primarily …_
  → The sustained inner activity of dwelling on received content — turning over God's precepts, pondering visions, reasoning within oneself about situations. Activity-oriented (distinct from static content). The person is actively engaged in an inner dialogue with something beyond themselves. Primary location: the heart (inner reasoning, Luk 5:22 VCG01 anchor) and the engaged mind (Psa 119:97 VCG03 anchor). Psa 119:97, Luk 5:22.
- *T1.3.1* — _What is the structural opposite of this characteristic — the inner-being reality that stands against or excludes it?_
  → VCG01 (Luk 5:22 corpus): evil reasoning within the heart — the reflective capacity turned toward self-justification rather than formation. Not the absence of reflection but its corruption.
- *T1.3.2* — _What does this characteristic explicitly exclude or resist?_
  → Unreflective living; the thoughtless heart. VCG01 (Luk 5:22): the Pharisees' reasoning within themselves — even corrupt reasoning is excluded from the unreflective state; what it excludes is the formative use of reflection.
- *T1.3.3* — _What is this characteristic not — where does it end and something else begin?_
  → Meditative activity (M15-F) is not: the knowledge content it dwells on (M15-C); the thought-content it produces (M15-G); the wisdom-character it forms over time (M15-A). It is the process of sustained inner engagement, not the content or the character-result.
- *T1.4.1* — _In what distinct ways does this characteristic operate within the inner person?_
  → Four modes: inner deliberative reasoning (VCG01: Luk 5:22), sustained reflection producing conceived thoughts (VCG02: Heb 4:12), meditation on God's precepts (VCG03: Psa 119:97), focused contemplative attention (VCG04: Dan 7:8).
- *T1.4.2* — _Does this characteristic operate differently depending on context, direction, or constitutional level?_
  → VCG01 (Luk 5:22: inner deliberative reasoning — morally neutral process). VCG03 (Psa 119:97: devotional meditation on God's law — formative). The same inner activity operates differently by its object.
- *T1.4.3* — _Does this characteristic have a communicative or speech-based mode of operation — and if so, how does it function?_
  → VCG01 (Luk 5:22 anchor: dialogizomai — to reason, to engage in interior dialogue). The meditative activity has an interior-speech character.
- *T1.5.1* — _What is the first or most immediate inner-being response to receiving or encountering this characteristic?_
  → VCG03 (Psa 119:97): "oh how I love your law!" — the immediate affective response to meditation is love for what is being pondered. VCG02 (Heb 4:12 anchor): the word discerning thoughts — the immediate response to encountering the word's penetrating quality is exposure and transparency.
- *T1.5.2* — _Is the immediate response consistent across the verse evidence, or does it vary?_
  → Consistent in affective dimension: Psa 119:97 shows love arising in meditation; Psa 39 (VCG03 corpus) shows contemplation producing awareness of transience. The affective response is consistent; its content varies.
- *T1.5.3* — _Where the verse evidence is silent on immediate response, note this explicitly._
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T1.6.1* — _What does this characteristic produce in the inner being over time?_
  → Psa 119:97 (VCG03 anchor): "it is my meditation all the day" — sustained meditation on God's law constitutes love for it. Over time, the meditative activity shapes what the inner person loves and values.
- *T1.6.2* — _What states, qualities, capacities, or orientations does sustained exposure to or possession of this characteristic establish?_
  → Formed love for God's law, deepened awareness, contemplative capacity (Psa 119:97).
- *T1.6.3* — _Does the sustained effect differ from the immediate response — and if so, how?_
  → Uniformly yes across all sub-groups. The immediate response is a specific act or opening; the sustained effect is a constituted quality or orientation formed over time. The pattern is consistent across the cluster: encounter/reception → immediate cognitive/volitional/affective opening → sustained formation of character/orientation/capacity. This is a cluster-level pattern.
- *T1.7.1* — _What inner conditions or orientations enable genuine reception of this characteristic?_
  → Love for God's law (Psa 119:97 VCG03 anchor: "oh how I love your law" — love enables and sustains meditation).
- *T1.7.2* — _What inner conditions block, distort, or prevent reception?_
  → VCG01 (Luk 5:22 corpus): evil reasoning in the heart — reflective capacity turned toward self-serving judgment rather than formation. The blocking condition is the direction of the reflection, not its absence.
- *T1.7.3* — _What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic but does not receive it?_
  → VCG01 (Luk 5:22): the Pharisees reasoning within themselves toward wrong conclusions — the reflective capacity active but uncorrected, producing self-justifying rather than formative results.
- *T1.8.1* — _What is the primary inner-being dimension of this characteristic from the programme's dimension vocabulary?_
  → Cognitive-reflective (active mental engagement with received content). Secondary: affective (love formed through meditation, Psa 119:97). Evidence: Psa 119:97 (si.chah — all-day meditation), Luk 5:22 (dialogizomai — interior reasoning).
- *T1.8.2* — _What evidence from the verse evidence supports this classification?_
  → Psa 119:97: all-day meditation. Luk 5:22: interior reasoning.
- *T1.8.3* — _Does this characteristic carry secondary dimensions — and if so, what are they, and do they compete with the primary classification?_
  → The affective secondary dimension (love formed through meditation, Psa 119:97) is a result of, not in competition with, the cognitive-reflective primary.

_Meaning of the term here:_ 'I considered the horns' — se.khal as sustained inner contemplation of the visionary scene; distinct from wisdom/prudence uses in M15-A
