<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch5 — T1 findings for Inner thought-content — the mind's formed thoughts -->

**T1 — Definition**

- *T1.1.1* — _What is this characteristic called in the programme — and what does the name itself signal about its essential nature?_
  → G3540 noēma (mind/thought): the formed content of the mind — thought as an object, not an activity. H7454 re.a / H7476 ra.yon: formed thoughts as inner objects. The name signals: thought-content is static compared to reflective activity (M15-F) — it is what the mind holds, not what the mind does. 2Cor 4:4 (VCG01 anchor), Psa 139:17 (VCG02 anchor).
- *T1.1.2* — _What do the primary Hebrew and Greek terms reveal at the definitional level — before deeper lexical analysis begins?_
  → Noēma (Greek noun): the mind/thought as an object that can be blinded, captured, or guarded (2Cor 4:4, VCG01 anchor). Re.a / ra.yon (Hebrew nouns): formed thoughts as inner objects. The terms reveal: thought-content is an inner object, not a process — it can be acted upon from outside (blinded by Satan, 2Cor 4:4) or from within (guarded).
- *T1.1.3* — _Does the name carry directional, relational, or constitutional implications that orient the enquiry from the outset?_
  → The thought-content is static but directional in its object: God's thoughts (re.a) are directed toward the human person (Psa 139:17); Satan's designs (noēmata) are directed against (2Cor 4:4 VCG01 anchor).
- *T1.2.1* — _What kind of inner-being phenomenon does this characteristic appear to be — an act, a disposition, a condition, a quality, or something else…_
  → Formed inner objects — the mind's content as objects that can be held, captured, blinded, or disclosed. 2Cor 4:4 (VCG01 anchor): noēmata as objects that Satan blinds.
- *T1.2.2* — _Is this characteristic simple in structure or does it appear to have constituent elements at first encounter?_
  → Three constituent categories: formed thoughts as objects that can be blinded or captured (VCG01), thoughts arising in the mind as events (VCG02), knowledge as inner content (VCG03). 2Cor 4:4 (VCG01 anchor).
- *T1.2.3* — _What is the current best working description of this characteristic — encapsulating its constitutional location, the faculties it primarily …_
  → The formed thoughts held within the mind — inner content as objects that can be captured, blinded, or disclosed. Static (distinct from the activity of M15-F). Satan can blind noēmata (2Cor 4:4 VCG01 anchor); God can know the inner thoughts of the heart; the person holds thought-content directed toward God (Psa 139:17 VCG02 anchor). 2Cor 4:4, Psa 139:17.
- *T1.3.1* — _What is the structural opposite of this characteristic — the inner-being reality that stands against or excludes it?_
  → VCG01 (2Cor 4:4 anchor): blinded minds — thought-content capacity sealed from light. The opposite is blindness/captivity of thought-content.
- *T1.3.2* — _What does this characteristic explicitly exclude or resist?_
  → Blindness and captivity (2Cor 4:4 VCG01 anchor); the emptiness of minds without formed content directed toward God.
- *T1.3.3* — _What is this characteristic not — where does it end and something else begin?_
  → Inner thought-content (M15-G) is not: the reflective activity (M15-F) that forms it; the understanding-faculty (M15-B) that grasps it; the counsel-activity (M15-E) that uses it. It is the static formed content, not the process or the using.
- *T1.4.1* — _In what distinct ways does this characteristic operate within the inner person?_
  → Three modes: thought as blindable/capturable object (VCG01: 2Cor 4:4), thought arising as events in the mind (VCG02: Psa 139:17), knowledge as formed inner content (VCG03: 2Ch 1:11).
- *T1.4.2* — _Does this characteristic operate differently depending on context, direction, or constitutional level?_
  → VCG01 (blinded/captured — subject to adversarial action). VCG02 (arising spontaneously — events in the mind). VCG03 (placed knowledge — divinely deposited content). Different operating modes by context.
- *T1.5.1* — _What is the first or most immediate inner-being response to receiving or encountering this characteristic?_
  → VCG02 (Psa 139:17 anchor): "how precious to me are your thoughts" — the immediate response to encountering God's thoughts directed at the person is preciousness/wonder.
- *T1.6.1* — _What does this characteristic produce in the inner being over time?_
  → 2Cor 4:4 (VCG01 anchor) context: thought-content blinded remains blinded — sustained blindness hardens. Psa 139:17 (VCG02 anchor): thought-content directed toward God, over time, constitutes the person's relational orientation.
- *T1.6.2* — _What states, qualities, capacities, or orientations does sustained exposure to or possession of this characteristic establish?_
  → Either: formed orientation toward God (Psa 139:17 if content is directed there), or hardened blindness (2Cor 4:4 if blinded).
- *T1.6.3* — _Does the sustained effect differ from the immediate response — and if so, how?_
  → Uniformly yes across all sub-groups. The immediate response is a specific act or opening; the sustained effect is a constituted quality or orientation formed over time. The pattern is consistent across the cluster: encounter/reception → immediate cognitive/volitional/affective opening → sustained formation of character/orientation/capacity. This is a cluster-level pattern.
- *T1.7.2* — _What inner conditions block, distort, or prevent reception?_
  → VCG01 (2Cor 4:4 anchor): Satan blinds the minds — adversarial blinding is the primary blocking condition in this sub-group.
- *T1.7.3* — _What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic but does not receive it?_
  → VCG01 (2Cor 4:4 anchor): the blinded mind — thought-content capacity closed to the light of the gospel; the person holds thoughts but not the thought of God's glory.
- *T1.8.1* — _What is the primary inner-being dimension of this characteristic from the programme's dimension vocabulary?_
  → Cognitive-static (formed thought-objects held in the mind). Secondary: relational (thought directed toward God or toward the person by God). Evidence: 2Cor 4:4 (noēmata — objects of adversarial blinding), Psa 139:17 (re.a — precious thoughts of God).
- *T1.8.2* — _What evidence from the verse evidence supports this classification?_
  → 2Cor 4:4: blindable noēmata. Psa 139:17: precious thoughts of God directed at person.
- *T1.8.3* — _Does this characteristic carry secondary dimensions — and if so, what are they, and do they compete with the primary classification?_
  → The relational secondary dimension (thought directed toward/from God) gives the cognitive-static content its significance. No competition.

### 5.8 Logos — the word as inner-being engagement

<!-- AI WRITE: Chapter 5 §5.8 (Logos — the word as inner-being engagement)
     LENGTH: ~800-1500 words per characteristic
     FOCUS: Write on how this characteristic moves — between God and the human person, between persons, in covenant, against opposition — and how it is formed, deepens, is tested, is transformed across time. Use the evidence below.
     CITE (must quote at least 2 verbatim): Col 3:16; 1Cor 14:19; Rom 14:12
     SOURCE: All evidence for this characteristic on this lens is in the blocks below.

<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch5 — T4 findings for Logos — the word as inner-being engagement -->

**T4 — Relational Interfaces**

- *T4.1.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating from God toward the human person — and if so, how?_
  → VCG01 (1Cor 1:18; Col 3:16): the divine logos as power (for those being saved) and dwelling-word (richly in the inner person). VCG01 (Jn 15:3): divine speech as the constituting act of the person's inner purity.
- *T4.1.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about the basis on which God extends this characteristic — is it conditional, unconditional, covenantal, or re…_
  → VCG01: God sends the logos — divine initiative precedes all human reception.
- *T4.1.3* — _What does God's extension of this characteristic reveal about his disposition toward the human person?_
  → VCG01 (Jn 15:3): inner cleansing. VCG01 (Col 3:16): community formation, wisdom, thankfulness.
- *T4.2.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in the human person's movement toward God — in seeking, supplication, worship, or…_
  → VCG02 (Col 4:6 corpus): gracious human speech in response to God's word offered in God's service. VCG03 (Gal 5:14): fulfilling the logos of the law as human-to-God movement.
- *T4.2.2* — _What does the evidence reveal about the inner posture required for this movement?_
  → Internalised divine word → disciplined expression → gracious speech offered in service.
- *T4.2.3* — _What does the human-to-God direction of this characteristic reveal about the person's relationship with God?_
  → Gracious human speech in response to and in service of God's word (VCG02 Col 4:6) and fulfilling the logos of the law (VCG03 Gal 5:14) reveal the relationship as responsive: the human word is the creature's response to the divine word. The relationship is a dialogue in which God speaks first and the human's whole communicative life is the response.
- *T4.3.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic being extended by one person toward another — and if so, how does it operate in that giving…_
  → VCG02 (Col 4:6): gracious, timely, appropriate speech as the primary giving form. VCG01 (1Cor 14:19): intelligible speech that reaches the inner person of the hearer.
- *T4.3.2* — _What inner conditions or orientations in the giver enable genuine extension of this characteristic?_
  → Gracious, seasoned speech (VCG02). Intelligible, meaning-bearing verbal communication (VCG01 1Cor 14:19).
- *T4.3.3* — _What does the evidence reveal about what the person must have received or become before they can genuinely give this characteristic?_
  → The internalised divine logos (VCG01 Col 3:16 "dwelling richly") is the precondition of gracious human speech (VCG02).
- *T4.4.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic being received by a person from another — and if so, how does it operate in that reception?_
  → VCG01 (Col 3:16 "richly"): the community receiving the word of Christ mutually.
- *T4.4.2* — _What inner conditions enable or block reception of this characteristic from another person?_
  → VCG01 (Col 3:16): the open, receptive inner community that "lets" the word dwell.
- *T4.4.3* — _What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic from another but does not receive it?_
  → VCG01 (1Cor 1:18): the person who encounters the logos of the cross and does not receive it is "those who are perishing" — the inner state is one of active rejection/dismissal. The same word that is power to the saved is folly to those who are perishing. The non-receiving inner state is spiritual blindness confirmed by the encounter.
- *T4.5.1* — _Does the evidence indicate whether this characteristic operates differently within existing relational bonds versus across relational distan…_
  → VCG01 (1Cor 1:18): the logos of the cross draws a boundary — those perishing and those being saved differentiated by their reception.
- *T4.5.2* — _Does this characteristic operate within covenantal contexts only, or does it cross covenantal boundaries?_
  → Inner state of the hearer (perishing vs being saved) is the boundary-defining condition for the logos's effect.
- *T4.5.3* — _What does the evidence reveal about the relational scope of this characteristic — who is included and who is not?_
  → VCG01 (1Cor 1:18): the logos of the cross draws the defining boundary — the saved and the perishing. VCG03 (Gal 5:14): the love-your-neighbour logos extends to the neighbour — potentially universal in human relational scope.
- *T4.6.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in relation to other spiritual beings — angelic or adversarial — and if so, how?_
  → VCG01 (Eph 6:17 corpus): the word of God as the sword of the Spirit — weaponry in spiritual warfare. VCG01 (1Cor 1:18): the logos operates in the domain of spiritual contestation.
- *T4.6.2* — _Is this characteristic a site of adversarial activity — something that can be attacked, distorted, or weaponised by adversarial spiritual po…_
  → VCG01 (1Cor 1:18): the logos confronts and overcomes the power of the adversary — divine word as the spiritual warfare instrument.
- *T4.6.3* — _Is this characteristic communicated, strengthened, or mediated through angelic ministry in the evidence?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]

<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch5 — T1 findings for Logos — the word as inner-being engagement -->

**T1 — Definition**

- *T1.1.1* — _What is this characteristic called in the programme — and what does the name itself signal about its essential nature?_
  → G3056 logos: the word — in its inner-engaging mode. The word that addresses the inner person: divine word (VCG01), human speech (VCG02), moral principle (VCG03). The name signals: the logos as an inner-being phenomenon is the word received into and operating on the person's inner life. Col 3:16 (VCG01 anchor).
- *T1.1.2* — _What do the primary Hebrew and Greek terms reveal at the definitional level — before deeper lexical analysis begins?_
  → Logos (Greek noun): word/speech/reason/account. In M15-H's inner-being mode: the word as address to and content for the inner person. 1Cor 14:19 (VCG02 anchor): "five words with my mind" — the logos here is the unit of inner-reaching communication.
- *T1.1.3* — _Does the name carry directional, relational, or constitutional implications that orient the enquiry from the outset?_
  → Bidirectional: the divine word is addressed TO the inner person (VCG01); the human speech (VCG02) is addressed outward FROM the inner person. The logos name carries both receiving and expressing directions.
- *T1.2.1* — _What kind of inner-being phenomenon does this characteristic appear to be — an act, a disposition, a condition, a quality, or something else…_
  → A received inner content / an expressed inner quality — bidirectional. Col 3:16 (VCG01 anchor): the word dwelling in the person as inner-constituting content; 1Cor 14:19 (VCG02 anchor): the word as the expression of the mind outward.
- *T1.2.2* — _Is this characteristic simple in structure or does it appear to have constituent elements at first encounter?_
  → Three constituent modes: divine-apostolic word engaging the inner person (VCG01), human speech as outer expression of inner quality (VCG02), word as comprehensive moral principle (VCG03). Col 3:16 (VCG01 anchor), 1Cor 14:19 (VCG02 anchor), Gal 5:14 (VCG03 corpus).
- *T1.2.3* — _What is the current best working description of this characteristic — encapsulating its constitutional location, the faculties it primarily …_
  → The word as inner-being engagement — the divine or apostolic word that addresses, constitutes, and evaluates the inner person; the human speech that expresses the inner quality outward; the comprehensive moral principle held as inner standard. The logos characteristic spans receiving (divine word entering) and expressing (human speech proceeding from inner quality). Col 3:16, 1Cor 14:19, Gal 5:14.
- *T1.3.1* — _What is the structural opposite of this characteristic — the inner-being reality that stands against or excludes it?_
  → Eph 5:6 (VCG02 corpus): "empty words" — the structural opposite of logos as inner-being engagement is the speech that carries no inner reality, that deceives rather than constitutes.
- *T1.3.2* — _What does this characteristic explicitly exclude or resist?_
  → Empty speech (Eph 5:6); unintelligible speech (1Cor 14:9 VCG02 corpus: "speaking into the air").
- *T1.3.3* — _What is this characteristic not — where does it end and something else begin?_
  → Logos as inner-being engagement (M15-H) is not: wisdom as constituted character (M15-A); the understanding faculty that receives it (M15-B); the knowledge content it conveys (M15-C). It is the word in its address-and-constituting function — the mode in which the word engages and forms the inner person.
- *T1.4.1* — _In what distinct ways does this characteristic operate within the inner person?_
  → Three modes: divine word engaging the inner person (VCG01: Col 3:16), human speech as expression of inner quality (VCG02: 1Cor 14:19), word as comprehensive moral principle (VCG03: Gal 5:14).
- *T1.4.2* — _Does this characteristic operate differently depending on context, direction, or constitutional level?_
  → VCG01 (divine word entering). VCG02 (human speech proceeding). VCG03 (moral principle held). Bidirectional operation: receiving and expressing.
- *T1.4.3* — _Does this characteristic have a communicative or speech-based mode of operation — and if so, how does it function?_
  → This sub-group IS the communicative/speech characteristic. The logos is inherently speech-and-word-based in its operation.
- *T1.5.1* — _What is the first or most immediate inner-being response to receiving or encountering this characteristic?_
  → VCG01 (Col 3:16): the word dwelling richly → teaching, admonishing, singing. The immediate response to the word's indwelling is community formation activity. VCG02 (1Cor 14:19): intelligible speech → instruction of others. The word's intelligible expression immediately produces formation in the hearer.
- *T1.5.2* — _Is the immediate response consistent across the verse evidence, or does it vary?_
  → Consistent: the word received → formation; the word spoken intelligibly → instruction.
- *T1.5.3* — _Where the verse evidence is silent on immediate response, note this explicitly._
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T1.6.1* — _What does this characteristic produce in the inner being over time?_
  → Col 3:16 (VCG01 anchor): the word dwelling richly → all wisdom. The sustained presence of the word in the person produces: teaching capacity, worship, wisdom in community life.
- *T1.6.2* — _What states, qualities, capacities, or orientations does sustained exposure to or possession of this characteristic establish?_
  → Wisdom, teaching capacity, worship, community formation (Col 3:16).
- *T1.6.3* — _Does the sustained effect differ from the immediate response — and if so, how?_
  → Uniformly yes across all sub-groups. The immediate response is a specific act or opening; the sustained effect is a constituted quality or orientation formed over time. The pattern is consistent across the cluster: encounter/reception → immediate cognitive/volitional/affective opening → sustained formation of character/orientation/capacity. This is a cluster-level pattern.
- *T1.7.1* — _What inner conditions or orientations enable genuine reception of this characteristic?_
  → Openness to instruction (Gal 6:6 VCG01 corpus: "let the one who is taught the word share all good things"); receiving posture (Eph 1:13 VCG01 corpus: "when you heard the word of truth").
- *T1.7.2* — _What inner conditions block, distort, or prevent reception?_
  → Eph 5:6 (VCG02 corpus): "empty words" — deceiving speech that prevents receipt of the true logos. 1Cor 1:17 (VCG02 corpus): "words of eloquent wisdom" that empty the cross of power — the packaging that substitutes for the word itself.
- *T1.7.3* — _What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic but does not receive it?_
  → 1Cor 1:18 (VCG01 corpus): "the word of the cross is folly to those who are perishing" — the inner state of the person who encounters the logos but does not receive it is one where the word registers as foolishness, not power. The inner condition determines how the logos is received.
- *T1.8.1* — _What is the primary inner-being dimension of this characteristic from the programme's dimension vocabulary?_
  → Communicative-formative (the word in its inner-being-engaging mode). Secondary: moral (VCG03: comprehensive moral principle), cognitive (the word as content received). Evidence: Col 3:16 (word dwelling richly — constituting wisdom), 1Cor 14:19 (logos as intelligible speech).
- *T1.8.2* — _What evidence from the verse evidence supports this classification?_
  → Col 3:16: word dwelling and constituting. 1Cor 14:19: intelligible speech.
- *T1.8.3* — _Does this characteristic carry secondary dimensions — and if so, what are they, and do they compete with the primary classification?_
  → The moral and cognitive secondary dimensions are modes of the communicative-formative primary. No competition.

### 6.1 Wisdom as holistic inner character and orientation

**T6 — Structural Relationships with Other Characteristics**

- *T6.1.1* — _Which adjacent characteristics appear most frequently alongside this one in the verse evidence?_
  → VCG03/VCG09 (Pro 10:14, Pro 9:10): wisdom co-occurs with knowledge (M15-C) and understanding (M15-B) — the triad is the consistent co-occurrence pattern. VCG04 (froneō): co-occurs with peace (M17 proximate) and life (eschatological vocabulary).
- *T6.1.2* — _What does the pattern of co-occurrence reveal about this characteristic's place in the inner-being landscape?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T6.1.3* — _If no significant co-occurrence patterns emerge, note this explicitly._
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T6.2.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic consistently preceding, following, or accompanying another characteristic in a sequence?_
  → VCG09: fear of the LORD precedes wisdom ("beginning of wisdom"). Wisdom then precedes right speech (VCG01), right living (VCG04), right governance (VCG03), and right community (VCG05).
- *T6.2.2* — _What does the sequence reveal — is the relationship causal, developmental, or correlational?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T6.3.1* — _Does this characteristic produce another characteristic in the verse evidence — and if so, which one, and by what mechanism?_
  → M15-A is both caused and causes. Caused by: fear of the LORD (VCG09 — prior reverence), divine endowment (VCG02 — prior Spirit-work), and knowledge (M15-C provides content). Causes: effective governance (VCG03), right speech (VCG01), community unity (VCG05), and creative excellence (VCG10).
- *T6.3.2* — _Is this characteristic produced by another — and if so, which one?_
  → M15-A (wisdom) is produced by: fear of the LORD (VCG09 — prior reverence); divine Spirit-endowment (VCG02 — Spirit as origin channel); and accumulated knowledge of God's character and ways (M15-C provides the content that wisdom integrates). Wisdom is also deepened by discernment (M15-D) and sustained by meditation (M15-F).
- *T6.3.3* — _Is this characteristic a constituent element of another, or does another characteristic constitute part of this one?_
  → M15-A (constituted wisdom character) is a constituent element of M15-E (effective counsel): the counselor's inner wisdom IS the resource from which counsel is given (VCG04). M15-A is also constituted in part by M15-C (knowledge as content) and M15-D (discernment as the evaluative faculty that wisdom governs). Relationship: M15-A governs and integrates the cluster's other characteristics.
- *T6.4.1* — _Does this characteristic share vocabulary terms with other characteristics in the programme?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T6.4.2* — _Does vocabulary sharing extend to root-level architecture — a shared root that generates terms across two or more characteristics?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T6.4.3* — _What does vocabulary sharing reveal about the conceptual relationship between characteristics?_
  → Cha.kham shared across M15-A, M15-C, M15-D, M15-E reveals that wisdom-character is not isolated but woven into the knowledge, discernment, and counsel vocabulary. The root family appears wherever the cluster is describing its most integrated inner function. Vocabulary sharing confirms: wisdom is the character that integrates the cluster's capacities.
- *T6.5.1* — _Which adjacent characteristic most closely resembles this one — and what precisely distinguishes them?_
  → Wisdom (M15-A) is the constituted character-orientation; understanding (M15-B) is the perceptive faculty that receives and enables. Wisdom is what the person IS; understanding is how the person GRASPS. The distinction is one of kind: constituted being (A) vs exercised faculty (B).

---

Wisdom is the constituted character that directs; knowledge is the relational content that informs. Wisdom provides direction; knowledge provides content. The distinction: orientation (A) vs content (C).
- *T6.5.2* — _Where the evidence shows apparent overlap, what is the precise boundary?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T6.5.3* — _Is the distinction between this characteristic and its nearest neighbour one of degree, kind, direction, or constitutional level?_
  → The distinction is one of KIND: wisdom (M15-A) is constituted character; understanding (M15-B) is exercised faculty. They are not the same thing at different intensities — they are different categories of inner-being phenomena. One is the person's constituted orientation (A); the other is the perceptive act (B).
- *T6.6.1* — _Does any verse in this characteristic's evidence base also function as a primary anchor in another characteristic's study?_
  → Anticipated shared anchors for M15-A: Pro 10:14 (shared with M15-C — "the wise lay up knowledge" — wisdom and knowledge co-anchored); Pro 9:10 (shared with M15-C and potentially fear/reverence clusters — "fear of the LORD is the beginning of wisdom"); 1Cor 1:24 (shared with M15-H and cross/salvation clusters — "Christ the wisdom of God and power of God"). The wisdom sub-group's anchors are most likely to be shared with knowledge (M15-C) and logos (M15-H) within the cluster, and with fear/reverence vocabulary outside the cluster.
- *T6.6.2* — _What does the shared anchor reveal about the relationship between the two characteristics?_
  → Where wisdom (M15-A) shares anchor verses with knowledge (M15-C) — as in Pro 10:14 and the broader Wisdom literature — the shared anchor reveals that wisdom and knowledge are not merely related but are co-constitutive: the same texts hold them simultaneously without tension, suggesting they describe the same inner reality from different perspectives.
- *T6.7.1* — _How many of this characteristic's confirmed analytical dimensions are shared with another characteristic in the programme?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T6.7.2* — _What does the pattern of dimensional sharing reveal about the relationship between this characteristic and those it shares dimensions with?_
  → Where wisdom (M15-A) shares dimensions with knowledge (M15-C) and understanding (M15-B), the pattern reveals that the triad is not three separate characteristics but three aspects of a single inner complex. Dimensional sharing confirms: these characteristics are designed to operate together and can only be properly understood in relation to each other.

_Meaning of the term here:_ "set their minds on things of flesh / Spirit" — froneō as the determinative inner orientation; flesh-minded or Spirit-minded describes the whole person

**Phili 2:2** (G5426 froneō) [M15-A-VCG05]

**Pro 26:12** (H2450 cha.kham) [M15-A-VCG06]
> Pro 26:12 Do you see a man who is wise in his own eyes ? There is more hope for a fool than for him .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "a man who is wise in his own eyes — more hope for a fool" — self-attributed wisdom as worse than foolishness; inner self-assessment as the problem

**1Cor 1:21** (G4678 sofia) [M15-A-VCG07]
> 1Cor 1:21 For since , in the wisdom of God , the world did not know God through wisdom , it pleased God through the folly of what we preach to save those who believe .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "world did not know God through wisdom" — sophia as the instrument that failed to reach God

**Neh 8:8** (H0995 bin) [M15-A-VCG08]
> Neh 8:8 They read from the book , from the Law of God , clearly , and they gave the sense , so that the people understood the reading .
_Meaning of the term here:_ "they gave the sense so that the people understood the reading" — bin activated by clear exposition; the inner faculty grasps meaning when the word is made clear

**Psa 111:10** (H7922 se.khel) [M15-A-VCG09]
> Psa 111:10 The fear of the Lord is the beginning of wisdom ; all those who practice it have a good understanding . His praise endures forever !
_Meaning of the term here:_ "all who practice it have good understanding" — se.khel as the fruit of practicing the fear of the Lord

**Exo 31:4** (H2803G cha.shav) [M15-A-VCG10]

_Meaning of the term here:_ "to devise artistic designs" — cha.shav explicitly names the inner act of design, not just execution

### 6.8 Logos — the word as inner-being engagement

<!-- AI WRITE: Chapter 6 §6.8 (Logos — the word as inner-being engagement)
     LENGTH: ~400-800 words per characteristic
     FOCUS: Write on this characteristic's relationship to other inner characteristics — what it is paired with, what it is opposed by, what produces it, what it itself produces. Use the evidence below.
     CITE (must quote at least 2 verbatim): Col 3:16; 1Cor 14:19; Rom 14:12
     SOURCE: All evidence for this characteristic on this lens is in the blocks below.
     AVOID: jargon; do not cite finding-id, tier code, or VCG code in the prose
-->

<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch6 — T6 findings for Logos — the word as inner-being engagement -->

**T6 — Structural Relationships with Other Characteristics**

- *T6.1.1* — _Which adjacent characteristics appear most frequently alongside this one in the verse evidence?_
  → VCG01 (Col 3:16): wisdom (M15-A), understanding (M15-B), knowledge (M15-C). VCG02 (Col 4:6 corpus): grace (C17) and community vocabulary.
- *T6.1.2* — _What does the pattern of co-occurrence reveal about this characteristic's place in the inner-being landscape?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T6.1.3* — _If no significant co-occurrence patterns emerge, note this explicitly._
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T6.2.1* — _Does the verse evidence show this characteristic consistently preceding, following, or accompanying another characteristic in a sequence?_
  → The logos received precedes: wisdom and worship (Col 3:16), gracious speech (VCG02 — the internalised word enables the expressed word).
- *T6.2.2* — _What does the sequence reveal — is the relationship causal, developmental, or correlational?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T6.3.1* — _Does this characteristic produce another characteristic in the verse evidence — and if so, which one, and by what mechanism?_
  → M15-H is less caused than causing: the divine logos initiates (VCG01 Col 3:16), causes inner cleansing (VCG01 Jn 15:3), and forms community (VCG01 Col 3:16). The logos is the divine initiating cause; human reception enables the causing to operate.
- *T6.3.2* — _Is this characteristic produced by another — and if so, which one?_
  → M15-H (logos) as received is produced by divine initiative (the word is sent, not generated by the human). As expressed, M15-H is enabled by: the internalised logos (Col 3:16 — the richly dwelling word enables gracious speech); wisdom (M15-A); and the counsel/discernment sub-groups (M15-D and M15-E — evaluating what to say and how to say it).
- *T6.3.3* — _Is this characteristic a constituent element of another, or does another characteristic constitute part of this one?_
  → M15-H (logos) is constituent of the transmission and communication of all cluster characteristics: wisdom, understanding, knowledge, discernment, and counsel are all given through and expressed via the word. M15-H is constituted by: the internalised divine word (VCG01) and the gracious character-orientation of M15-A (which enables the gracious speech of VCG02).

### 7.1 Wisdom as holistic inner character and orientation

<!-- AI WRITE: Chapter 7 §7.1 (Wisdom as holistic inner character and orientation)
     LENGTH: ~400-500 words per characteristic (or grouped)
     FOCUS: Short overview of what human / clinical sciences observe about the human capacity corresponding to Wisdom as holistic inner character and orientation. Use general scientific knowledge — the analytical record is thin on this lens. Note explicitly where the record offers no view-from-outside material.

<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch7 — T7 findings for Wisdom as holistic inner character and orientation -->

**T7 — Evidential and Methodological Foundation**

- *T7.1.1* — _What are the primary Hebrew and Greek terms for this characteristic — and what do their root meanings reveal?_
  → Primary terms: H2450 cha.kham (adj — wise person), H2449 cha.kham (verb — to be wise), H2451 chok.mah (noun — wisdom), G4678 sophia (wisdom), G5428 fronēsis (practical wisdom/prudence), G4920 suniēmi (in wisdom corpus), G5426 froneō (to set the mind, be minded). Root H-ch-k-m: the root conveys a constituted skill or mastery — originally referring to craft skill before extending to moral and intellectual excellence. The root meaning reveals wisdom as a formed inner competence, not a raw capacity. G sophia: breadth of practical and theoretical excellence. The root reveal: wisdom is constituted character, not momentary insight (Pro 16:23 — "the heart of the wise").
- *T7.1.10* — _What does the full vocabulary arc reveal about this characteristic's complete semantic range?_
  → Arc: divine wisdom as God's attribute (Pro 8:22-31 — wisdom present at creation) → Christ as the wisdom of God (1Cor 1:24 — christological identity) → Spirit-endowed wisdom given to craftsmen (Exo 31:3) and rulers (1Ki 3:12) → constituted wisdom-character of the wise person (Pro 16:23 — "the heart of the wise") → wisdom expressed in governance, speech, and community (VCG03-05) → directed wisdom-orientation (froneō Spirit, Rom 8:5) → its absence: the fool (Pro 1:7 inverse). The arc reveals wisdom as spanning from divine pre-creation attribute through personal christological identity through Spirit-gift through constituted human character to directed orientation. The characteristic's complete range runs from the most transcendent to the most quotidian.
- *T7.1.2* — _What is the grammatical range of the primary term (noun, verb, adjective, participle) — and what does that range reveal about how the charac…_
  → Cha.kham: both adjective (wise person — Pro 16:23 "the heart of the wise") and verb (to become wise, to act wisely). The adjectival form dominates in the wisdom literature, revealing wisdom as constituted character rather than momentary act. G sophia: noun only (the state of wisdom). G froneō: verb (to be minded, to set the mind on). The predominance of adjectives and nouns reveals M15-A as a characteristic of being rather than doing — wisdom is what the person IS, expressed in what they do.
- *T7.1.3* — _What is the semantic range of the primary term — across what breadth of meaning does it operate?_
  → Cha.kham/chok.mah spans: craft skill (Exo 36:1 — craftsmen wise-hearted for tabernacle construction), governance capacity (1Ki 3:12 — Solomon's wisdom for ruling), moral discernment (Pro 9:10 — wisdom begins with fear of the LORD), communal harmonisation (Phil 2:2 — froneō in shared wisdom-orientation), and divine nature (1Cor 1:24 — Christ the wisdom of God). The semantic range reveals wisdom as the most integrative characteristic in M15: it operates across creative, governance, moral, relational, and theological domains simultaneously.
- *T7.1.4* — _Does the vocabulary include terms that distinguish distinct aspects of this characteristic — disposition versus act, received versus given, …_
  → Yes. Cha.kham (adj): the wise person as a constituted type — disposition/quality. Cha.kham (verb): to become wise, to act wisely — the act. Chok.mah: wisdom as the state or attribute. G froneō (verb): the act of setting the mind on a direction — the directional act. G sophia (noun): wisdom as possessed attribute. The verb/adjective/noun distinction in M15-A captures wisdom as character-quality (adj), as exercised act (verb), and as attribute possessed (noun) — three distinct aspects of the same characteristic.
- *T7.1.5* — _Does the vocabulary include a term for the structural opposite or absence of this characteristic?_
  → Yes. H3684 cha.sil (fool — Pro 10:1 "a foolish son is a grief to his mother"), H5036 naval (fool, senseless — Psa 14:1 "the fool says in his heart"), H191 e.vil (foolish — Pro 1:7 "fools despise wisdom"). G mōria (folly — 1Cor 1:18 — the logos of the cross is folly to those perishing). The structural opposite reveals wisdom's stakes: the fool is not merely less wise but constitutively opposed — the negative character-type whose inner constitution closes them to wisdom.
- *T7.1.6* — _Does the vocabulary include a person-type term — a term for the one who habitually possesses or exercises this characteristic?_
  → Yes. H2450 cha.kham: the wise person (adj used as substantive — Pro 16:23 "the heart of the wise"). G5429 fronimos: the prudent/thoughtful person (Matt 7:24 — "the wise man who built on the rock"). G4680 sophos: the wise person (1Cor 1:20 — "where is the wise man?"). The person-type term for wisdom is well-developed: both Hebrew and Greek name the constituted wise person as a recognisable human type.
- *T7.1.7* — _Does the vocabulary include a supplication or seeking term — a term for the act of seeking this characteristic from another?_
  → Yes. Jas 1:5 (proximate corpus): "If any of you lacks wisdom, let him ask God." The seeking of wisdom uses standard prayer vocabulary (aiteō — to ask, request) applied to wisdom as the object. No specialised seeking term is unique to wisdom, but the prayer-pattern for wisdom is established: asking God as the standard mode of seeking. Solomon's request (1Ki 3:9 — "give your servant") also uses standard petition language.
- *T7.1.9* — _Is there a term newly coined in the NT period for this characteristic — and if so, what does that coinage reveal?_
  → G5428 fronēsis: practical wisdom/prudence in the NT (Luk 1:17 — "the wisdom of the righteous"; Eph 1:8 — "wisdom and insight"). Fronēsis is not entirely new (Aristotle) but its NT application to the wisdom of the righteous and to the Spirit's endowment reveals a distinctive NT development: practical wisdom as a Spirit-given capacity for godly living. Also: G4678 sophia applied to Christ personally (1Cor 1:24, 30 — "Christ the wisdom of God") — the personalisation of the abstract attribute as divine Person is a NT development building on Wisdom literature's personification.
- *T7.2.1* — _What is the function of this characteristic's primary term within its primary verse — what role does it play in the sentence and argument?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T7.2.2* — _What literary form carries the primary verse evidence (narrative, psalm, wisdom, prophecy, epistle, apocalyptic) — and what does that form r…_
  → Primary anchor Pro 16:23 is Wisdom literature (Proverbs — didactic aphorism). The form requires attending to the aphoristic generalisation: Pro 16:23 does not describe one event but states a general truth about the wise person's character. The didactic form means the claim is about pattern, not occasion. Secondary evidence 1Cor 1:18-25 is Pauline epistle (community crisis context — worldly wisdom dividing the Corinthian community). The epistolary form requires attending to the audience and the polemic: Paul is correcting, not simply describing.
- *T7.2.3* — _What is the logical structure of key arguments in the verse evidence — what are the premises and conclusions?_
  → Pro 16:23: premise — a wise heart exists as constituted character; conclusion — it guides speech with appropriate teaching. The argument moves from inner constitution to outer expression. 1Cor 1:18-24: premise — worldly wisdom judges by worldly standards; premise — God has made the cross foolishness to the wise; conclusion — the wisdom of God (Christ crucified) is inaccessible to self-attributed wisdom. The argument is an inversion: the very possession of worldly wisdom closes access to divine wisdom.
- *T7.2.4* — _What contextual setting carries the primary verse evidence (judicial, liturgical, covenantal, communal, eschatological) — and what does that…_
  → Primary settings: Wisdom literature (Proverbs — didactic/instructional, for the passing on of the wise life); Pauline epistle (1Cor 1 — community crisis, where worldly wisdom has caused division, requiring reorientation to the cross). The settings reveal: wisdom is both a personal formational reality (Proverbs) and a community-critical issue (1Cor 1). Both settings are polemical: Proverbs warns against foolishness; 1Cor 1 warns against worldly-wisdom orientation.
- *T7.2.5* — _Does any verse function as the primary anchor for this characteristic — the verse that most fully and directly expresses its essential chara…_
  → Pro 16:23: "The heart of the wise makes his speech judicious and adds persuasiveness to his lips." Primary anchor: names the inner location (heart), the character-quality (wise — cha.kham), and the expressive-functional outcome (speech judicious, lips persuasive). It captures the constituted inner character producing its characteristic outer expression in a single verse.
- *T7.2.6* — _What does the primary anchor verse reveal that no other verse reveals?_
  → Pro 16:23 alone names the inner-to-outer movement of wisdom with this precision: it is not that the wise person speaks wisely, but that wisdom guides the mouth — the wise heart is the source and the speech is the fruit. No other verse in M15-A names this causal chain so directly.

  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T7.3.2* — _Where the human science framework illuminates the verse evidence — making a finding more coherent or complete — what does it reveal?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]

  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]

  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]

### 7.2 Understanding as inner perceptive faculty

<!-- AI WRITE: Chapter 7 §7.2 (Understanding as inner perceptive faculty)
     LENGTH: ~400-500 words per characteristic (or grouped)
     FOCUS: Short overview of what human / clinical sciences observe about the human capacity corresponding to Understanding as inner perceptive faculty. Reflect on (a) synergies with the biblical picture, (b) gaps where science is silent on what Scripture emphasises, (c) differences where the scientific framing diverges from the biblical framing. Use general scientific knowledge — the analytical record is thin on this lens. Note explicitly where the record offers no view-from-outside material.
     SOURCE: T7 findings below (sparse).
     AVOID: jargon; do not overclaim — be explicit where the analytical record is silent

<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch7 — T7 findings for Understanding as inner perceptive faculty -->

**T7 — Evidential and Methodological Foundation**

- *T7.1.1* — _What are the primary Hebrew and Greek terms for this characteristic — and what do their root meanings reveal?_
  → Primary terms: H0995 bin (verb — to perceive, discern), H0998 binah (noun — understanding), H8394 te.vu.nah (noun — understanding as formed faculty), G4907 sunesis (understanding, comprehension), G4920 suniēmi (verb — to understand, bring together). Root H-b-y-n: "to separate, distinguish, perceive between" — the root reveals understanding as a discriminating perceptive act, the bringing apart of what is confused to see it clearly. G sunesis: from sun + hiēmi ("to send together") — the grasping that brings separate things into unified comprehension (1Ki 3:9 — "an understanding mind").
- *T7.1.10* — _What does the full vocabulary arc reveal about this characteristic's complete semantic range?_
  → Arc: God's unsearchable understanding (Isa 40:28 — his understanding is inscrutable) → understanding placed in the person by God (Job 38:36 — who put understanding in the mind?) → understanding as governance faculty (1Ki 3:9 — discerning heart) → understanding trained through practice (Heb 5:14 — trained aisthētērion) → understanding transmitted through teaching (Neh 8:8) → Christ's definitive opening of understanding (Luk 24:45) → its absence: asunetos (Rom 1:21 — senseless). The arc reveals understanding as a faculty that belongs first to God, is then given and formed in the creature, and reaches its fullest opening only through Christ's act.
- *T7.1.2* — _What is the grammatical range of the primary term (noun, verb, adjective, participle) — and what does that range reveal about how the charac…_
  → Bin: primarily verb (to perceive, discern — 1Ki 3:9 "give your servant an understanding mind"). Also noun forms te.vu.nah and binah. G suniēmi: verb (to understand, bring together). The verbal dominance reveals understanding as a perceptive act — an ongoing, exercised capacity, not a static possession. G sunesis: noun (the grasped comprehension). The verb-noun pair reveals understanding as both act (suniēmi — perceiving) and result (sunesis — what has been grasped).
- *T7.1.3* — _What is the semantic range of the primary term — across what breadth of meaning does it operate?_
  → Bin/suniēmi spans: governance discernment (1Ki 3:9 — understanding for ruling), comprehension of Scripture (Luk 24:45 — opened minds to understand), instruction-reception (Neh 8:8 — causing to understand), strategic intelligence (1Chr 12:32 — understanding of the times), and moral formation (Heb 5:14 — understanding trained for good/evil). The semantic range reveals understanding as a perceptive-receptive faculty operating across all domains where the person must grasp the meaning-structure of something.
- *T7.1.4* — _Does the vocabulary include terms that distinguish distinct aspects of this characteristic — disposition versus act, received versus given, …_
  → Yes. Bin (verb): the act of perceiving, discerning — the act. Te.vu.nah (noun): understanding as a formed faculty or quality — the condition. Binah (noun): understanding as the resulting comprehension — the product. G suniēmi (verb): the act of comprehending. G sunesis (noun): comprehension as a quality or possession. The verb/noun distinction captures understanding as act (suniēmi — bringing things together) and as condition (sunesis — the quality of one who comprehends). 1Ki 3:9 (binah — asking for the faculty) vs Luk 24:45 (suniēmi — the act of opening).
- *T7.1.5* — _Does the vocabulary include a term for the structural opposite or absence of this characteristic?_
  → Yes. G0801 asunetos (without understanding — Rom 1:21 "their foolish hearts were darkened"; Rom 10:19 "a senseless nation"). H0995 bin negative forms (not-perceiving). The structural opposite names the constitutive absence of the perceptive faculty — not merely a failure of understanding in a moment but a condition of non-perceiving.
- *T7.1.6* — _Does the vocabulary include a person-type term — a term for the one who habitually possesses or exercises this characteristic?_
  → Yes. G4908 sunetos: the intelligent/understanding person (Matt 11:25 — "hidden from the wise and understanding"). G1990 epistēmōn: the skilled/knowing person (Jas 3:13 — "who is wise and understanding among you?"). The person-type for understanding names the one whose perceptive faculty is well-formed and reliably exercised.
- *T7.1.7* — _Does the vocabulary include a supplication or seeking term — a term for the act of seeking this characteristic from another?_
  → S — No specialised supplication term for understanding in M15-B's vocabulary. Understanding is sought through standard prayer (Solomon's request in 1Ki 3:9 uses petition vocabulary, not understanding-specific supplication terms) and through the discipline of sustained practice (Heb 5:14 — training). The absence of a specialised seeking term confirms understanding is not primarily petitioned for but formed through engagement.
- *T7.1.9* — _Is there a term newly coined in the NT period for this characteristic — and if so, what does that coinage reveal?_
  → G4907 sunesis: understanding as comprehension (Mk 12:33 — "to love God is worth more than all burnt offerings" — spoken with sunesis). The NT deployment of sunesis in specifically Christological and ethical contexts (Col 1:9 — "understanding in all wisdom") reveals a NT development: understanding as the faculty that grasps the mystery of Christ. G4908 sunetos: the understanding person (Matt 11:25 — hidden from "the wise and understanding"). The NT pattern of Christ opening understanding (Luk 24:45 — suniēmi) is a distinctively NT Christological development.
- *T7.2.1* — _What is the function of this characteristic's primary term within its primary verse — what role does it play in the sentence and argument?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T7.2.2* — _What literary form carries the primary verse evidence (narrative, psalm, wisdom, prophecy, epistle, apocalyptic) — and what does that form r…_
  → Primary anchor 1Ki 3:9 is narrative (historical narrative — Solomon's prayer at Gibeon). The narrative form requires attending to what the narrator commends: Solomon's request is presented approvingly by the narrator (1Ki 3:10 — "it pleased the LORD"). Responsible interpretation treats this as an endorsed model, not merely a report. Secondary evidence Heb 5:14 is Pauline epistle (pastoral argument — the author rebuking immaturity). The epistolary form requires attending to the context of rebuke: the claim about trained understanding is made in a context where the community has failed to develop it.
- *T7.2.3* — _What is the logical structure of key arguments in the verse evidence — what are the premises and conclusions?_
  → Heb 5:14: premise — solid food belongs to the mature; premise — maturity is a faculty trained by constant practice; conclusion — trained discernment for moral distinction marks maturity. Argument moves from developmental claim through mechanism to outcome. 1Ki 3:9: premise — governing justly is beyond unaided human capacity; premise — a discerning heart enables just governance; conclusion — the discerning heart must be asked for from God.
- *T7.2.4* — _What contextual setting carries the primary verse evidence (judicial, liturgical, covenantal, communal, eschatological) — and what does that…_
  → Primary settings: Narrative (1Ki 3 — prayer and response in covenant context); Epistle (Heb 5:14 — pastoral argument about maturity); Gospel (Luk 24:45 — post-resurrection commissioning). The narrative setting reveals that the request for understanding is a covenant event. The epistle setting reveals that understanding-formation is a community formation concern. The gospel setting reveals that the definitive opening of understanding is a Christological event.
- *T7.2.5* — _Does any verse function as the primary anchor for this characteristic — the verse that most fully and directly expresses its essential chara…_
  → 1Ki 3:9: "Give your servant therefore an understanding mind to govern your people, that I may discern between good and evil, for who is able to govern this your great people?" Primary anchor: the perceptive faculty (understanding mind) explicitly requested, its governance purpose named, its moral-discernment function specified, and its creaturely-insufficiency acknowledged. The verse holds the full structure of M15-B's essential character.
- *T7.2.6* — _What does the primary anchor verse reveal that no other verse reveals?_
  → 1Ki 3:9 alone holds the covenantal-request structure in this complete form: the inadequacy (who is able?), the specific faculty needed (understanding mind), the relational object (your people), and the moral function (discerning good from evil) — all in one asking. No other verse captures the creaturely-insufficiency + specific-request + covenantal-purpose structure simultaneously.

  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]

  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]

  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]

### 7.3 Knowledge as inner content and covenantal knowing

<!-- AI WRITE: Chapter 7 §7.3 (Knowledge as inner content and covenantal knowing)
     LENGTH: ~400-500 words per characteristic (or grouped)
     FOCUS: Short overview of what human / clinical sciences observe about the human capacity corresponding to Knowledge as inner content and covenantal knowing. Reflect on (a) synergies with the biblical picture, (b) gaps where science is silent on what Scripture emphasises, (c) differences where the scientific framing diverges from the biblical framing. Use general scientific knowledge — the analytical record is thin on this lens. Note explicitly where the record offers no view-from-outside material.
     SOURCE: T7 findings below (sparse).
     AVOID: jargon; do not overclaim — be explicit where the analytical record is silent

<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch7 — T7 findings for Knowledge as inner content and covenantal knowing -->

**T7 — Evidential and Methodological Foundation**

- *T7.1.1* — _What are the primary Hebrew and Greek terms for this characteristic — and what do their root meanings reveal?_
  → Primary terms: H3045 ya.da (verb — to know, the primary root), H1847 da.at (noun — knowledge), H1843 de.a (noun — knowledge), H1844 de.ah (noun — knowledge), H4486 man.da (Aramaic — knowledge), G6063 oida (to know with settled conviction, perfect aspect), G1097 ginōskō (to know, ongoing acquaintance). Root H-y-d-a: the most semantically rich root in M15 — the same root covers knowing a fact (Gen 3:5), knowing a person intimately (Gen 4:1), knowing God covenantally (Hos 6:3), and God's elective knowing of Israel (Amos 3:2). The root reveals knowing as fundamentally relational and personal, not merely propositional.
- *T7.1.10* — _What does the full vocabulary arc reveal about this characteristic's complete semantic range?_
  → Arc: divine comprehensive knowing of the human (Psa 139:6 — "too wonderful") → divine elective knowing (Amos 3:2 — "you only have I known") → redemptive knowing-disclosure (Exo 7:5 — they shall know that I am the LORD) → covenantal human pursuit of knowing God (Hos 6:3 — press on) → knowledge as accumulated inner content (Pro 10:14 — lay up) → moral knowing (Gen 2:9 — good and evil) → conviction-knowledge through suffering (Job 19:25 — I know that my Redeemer lives) → culpable ignorance (Act 17:30) → intimate union-knowing (Gen 4:1) → eschatological fullness (Hab 2:14 — earth filled). The arc is the widest in the cluster — from divine omniscience to eschatological universality with every human mode of knowing between them.
- *T7.1.2* — _What is the grammatical range of the primary term (noun, verb, adjective, participle) — and what does that range reveal about how the charac…_
  → Ya.da: verb (to know — Hos 6:3 "let us press on to know"). Da.at, de.a, de.ah: nouns (knowledge as state or possession — Pro 10:14 "the wise lay up knowledge"). G oida: perfect-form verb (to know as settled conviction — Job 19:25 "I know that my Redeemer lives"). G ginōskō: present-progressive verb (knowing as ongoing acquaintance). The full grammatical range — active verb (knowing), passive noun (knowledge held), and perfect conviction (oida) — reveals M15-C as operating across the full spectrum from relational encounter to settled possession.
- *T7.1.3* — _What is the semantic range of the primary term — across what breadth of meaning does it operate?_
  → Ya.da spans the widest range in M15: divine comprehensive knowing (Psa 139:6 — God's knowing of the human), elective covenantal knowing (Amos 3:2 — "you only have I known"), redemptive disclosure (Exo 7:5 — "you shall know that I am the LORD"), volitional pursuit (Hos 6:3 — "press on to know"), moral discrimination (Gen 2:9 — knowledge of good and evil), settled conviction (Job 19:25 — "I know that my Redeemer lives"), practical recognition (Gen 12:11 — Abraham perceives Sarah's beauty), intimate personal union (Gen 4:1 — Adam knew Eve), and eschatological fullness (Hab 2:14 — earth full of the knowledge of the LORD). The range confirms M15-C as the most semantically broad sub-group in the cluster.
- *T7.1.4* — _Does the vocabulary include terms that distinguish distinct aspects of this characteristic — disposition versus act, received versus given, …_
  → Yes. Ya.da (verb): knowing as an ongoing act (Hos 6:3 — "press on to know"). Da.at (noun): knowledge as the state or content possessed (Pro 10:14 — "lay up knowledge"). G oida (perfect-aspect): knowing as settled conviction already held (Job 19:25 — "I know"). G ginōskō (present-progressive): knowing as ongoing acquaintance. The distinction between oida (settled, completed knowing) and ginōskō (active, growing knowing) is unique in M15 — it distinguishes the conviction-character of knowing (oida) from its relational-progressive character (ginōskō).
- *T7.1.5* — _Does the vocabulary include a term for the structural opposite or absence of this characteristic?_
  → Yes. H0050 agnoeō (G — to not know, to be ignorant — Act 17:30 "the times of ignorance"). H0051 agnoia (G — ignorance). Lo ya.da (H — literally "not-knowing" — 1Sa 2:12 "they did not know the LORD"). The structural opposite in M15-C covers both culpable ignorance (agnoeō — Act 17:30, where ignorance produces accountability) and chosen relational not-knowing (lo ya.da — the person who refuses covenantal knowing).
- *T7.1.6* — _Does the vocabulary include a person-type term — a term for the one who habitually possesses or exercises this characteristic?_
  → S — No dedicated person-type term for the one who characteristically possesses da.at in M15-C's term set. The wise person (cha.kham) possesses knowledge, but cha.kham belongs to M15-A. The knower is characterised by the possession (da.at-possessor) but is not given a dedicated nominal in M15-C's vocabulary.
- *T7.1.7* — _Does the vocabulary include a supplication or seeking term — a term for the act of seeking this characteristic from another?_
  → Yes, indirectly. H3045 ya.da with volitional forward motion: "let us press on to know" (Hos 6:3) — the pursuit-seeking mode. This is not a supplication term but a pursuit term: the seeking of knowing-God is expressed through the verb ya.da itself used in the volitional cohortative ("let us know"). The seeking is characterised as pursuit, not petition.
- *T7.1.9* — _Is there a term newly coined in the NT period for this characteristic — and if so, what does that coinage reveal?_
  → G0050 agnoeō: to be ignorant (Act 17:30 — "times of ignorance God overlooked"). While agnoeō exists in classical Greek, its NT moral-theological loading (ignorance as culpable, as the condition that produces accountability rather than excusing it) is a distinctively NT development. Also: the gnōsis/epignōsis distinction in Paul (Col 1:9 — "knowledge [epignōsis] of his will") — epignōsis as full or thorough knowledge is a NT intensification of the knowing vocabulary applied to knowing God and his will.
- *T7.2.1* — _What is the function of this characteristic's primary term within its primary verse — what role does it play in the sentence and argument?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T7.2.2* — _What literary form carries the primary verse evidence (narrative, psalm, wisdom, prophecy, epistle, apocalyptic) — and what does that form r…_
  → Primary anchor Hos 6:3 is prophetic oracle (covenant renewal call — the prophet calling the people back to covenantal knowing). The prophetic form requires attending to the covenant lawsuit context: the "let us" is not abstract aspiration but response to prophetic rebuke. Secondary evidence Psa 139:6 is Psalmic poetry (first-person address to God). The confessional poetic form requires attending to the personal-relational register: the psalmist is not making a theological proposition about divine omniscience but confessing overwhelming personal experience of being known.
- *T7.2.3* — _What is the logical structure of key arguments in the verse evidence — what are the premises and conclusions?_
  → Hab 2:14 (VCG12): premise — the earth shall be filled with the knowledge of the Lord; premise — as waters cover the sea. The argument is analogical: the completeness of eschatological knowing is like the completeness of oceanic water covering — no gap, no exception. Hos 6:3: premise — pressing on to know the LORD is possible; premise — his going out is as sure as the dawn; conclusion — pursuing knowing of God is not futile. Argument from divine reliability to human pursuit.
- *T7.2.4* — _What contextual setting carries the primary verse evidence (judicial, liturgical, covenantal, communal, eschatological) — and what does that…_
  → Primary settings: Prophetic oracle (Hos 6:3 — covenant renewal call; Hab 2:14 — eschatological vision); Wisdom narrative (Job 19:25 — crisis of sustained suffering); Historical narrative (Gen 4:1 — intimate knowing in covenant context). The prophetic setting reveals that knowledge of God is a covenant-relational category; the wisdom setting reveals it as conviction forged in the crucible; the narrative setting reveals it as the most intimate form of personal knowing.
- *T7.2.5* — _Does any verse function as the primary anchor for this characteristic — the verse that most fully and directly expresses its essential chara…_
  → Hos 6:3: "Let us know; let us press on to know the LORD; his going out is sure as the dawn; he will come to us as the showers, as the spring rains that water the earth." Primary anchor: covenantal community pursuit ("let us"), volitional press ("press on"), relational object ("know the LORD"), divine reliability as the basis of the pursuit, and divine-initiative response ("he will come to us"). The full structure of M15-C's covenantal-pursuit knowing.
- *T7.2.6* — _What does the primary anchor verse reveal that no other verse reveals?_
  → Hos 6:3 alone names the dynamic pursuit-of-knowing in communal first-person plural form ("let us"). It is the only M15-C anchor that is simultaneously communal, volitional, pursuit-oriented, and grounded in divine reliability. No other verse in M15-C holds all four elements together.

### 7.4 Discernment and practical judgment

<!-- AI WRITE: Chapter 7 §7.4 (Discernment and practical judgment)

<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch7 — T7 findings for Discernment and practical judgment -->

**T7 — Evidential and Methodological Foundation**

- *T7.1.1* — _What are the primary Hebrew and Greek terms for this characteristic — and what do their root meanings reveal?_
  → Primary terms: H7919A sa.khal (verb — to act wisely, succeed, discern), H7922 se.khel (noun — prudence, insight), H0995 bin (shared with M15-B), H2803G/H/I cha.shav (verb — to think, reckon, devise, impute), H6175 a.rum (adj — prudent, shrewd), H2938 ta.am (verb — to taste, discern by tasting), G1252 diakrinō (to discriminate, evaluate, judge, doubt), G3049 logizomai (to reckon, credit, calculate), G1261 logismos (reasoning, argument), G3053 logismos (a reckoning). Root sa.khal: "to look at, consider carefully, act prudently" — the root reveals discernment as careful evaluative attention producing successful action (Isa 52:13 — "my servant shall sa.khal"). Root ta.am: "to taste" — the gustatory root reveals discernment as a direct inner-contact perception.
- *T7.1.10* — _What does the full vocabulary arc reveal about this characteristic's complete semantic range?_
  → Arc: the Servant's sa.khal as divinely-attributed discernment (Isa 52:13 — acts wisely, is exalted) → divine crediting of faith as righteousness (Gen 15:6 — logizomai) → self-examination (1Cor 11:31 — diakrinō) → evaluative assessment from observation (Gen 38:15 — cha.shav) → gustatory-testing discernment (Job 12:11 — ta.am) → trained discernment for moral distinction (Heb 5:14 — aisthētērion) → prudent social navigation (Pro 12:23 — a.rum conceals knowledge) → inner argumentation as strongholds (2Cor 10:4-5 — logismos) → diakrinō as doubt/self-division (Jas 1:6). The arc spans forensic reckoning through trained moral perception to inner adversarial contestation.
- *T7.1.2* — _What is the grammatical range of the primary term (noun, verb, adjective, participle) — and what does that range reveal about how the charac…_
  → Sa.khal: verb (to act wisely, discern, succeed — Isa 52:13). Se.khel: noun (prudence, insight). Cha.shav: verb (to think, reckon, devise, impute — Gen 15:6). Diakrinō: verb (to discriminate, evaluate, judge — 1Cor 11:31). Logizomai: verb (to reckon, credit — Gen 15:6 LXX). The predominance of verbs reveals M15-D as a characteristically active, exercised capacity — discernment is something done, not something possessed. The noun se.khel is the capacity; the verbs name its exercise.
- *T7.1.3* — _What is the semantic range of the primary term — across what breadth of meaning does it operate?_
  → Sa.khal spans: prudent wise action (Isa 52:13 — the Servant acts wisely), governance success (Neh 8:13 — those skilled in the law), self-examination (1Cor 11:31 — diakrinō for self-evaluation), evaluative crediting (Gen 15:6 — logizomai for divine imputing), gustatory testing (Job 12:11 — ta.am as tasting/discerning), inner argumentation (2Cor 10:4-5 — logismos as strongholds), and adversarial reasoning (Rom 2:15 — logismos in accusation/excuse). The semantic range reveals M15-D as encompassing both the prudential-practical and the forensic-moral dimensions of inner evaluation.
- *T7.1.4* — _Does the vocabulary include terms that distinguish distinct aspects of this characteristic — disposition versus act, received versus given, …_
  → Yes. Sa.khal (verb): the act of discerning wisely — the active exercise. Se.khel (noun): the capacity for prudent insight — the condition/quality. Cha.shav: the act of evaluative thinking/reckoning — the cognitive act. Logizomai: the act of crediting/reckoning — the forensic act. Diakrinō: the act of discriminating/judging. The vocabulary distinguishes: the capacity (se.khel), the act (sa.khal, cha.shav, diakrinō), and the forensic-constitutive act (logizomai — Gen 15:6 — credited as righteousness). These are not synonyms but distinct aspects of discernment's operation.
- *T7.1.5* — _Does the vocabulary include a term for the structural opposite or absence of this characteristic?_
  → Yes. The undiscerning person who swallows without testing (ta.am inverse — the one who does not taste/test what is given to them). G0175 akarpos (unfruitful — in contexts where discernment's absence produces no fruit). The structural opposite of sa.khal is failure in wise action — producing defeat or foolish outcome rather than success. Diakrinō negative: the self-divided person who doubts (Jas 1:6 — "let him ask in faith, with no diakrinō").
- *T7.1.6* — _Does the vocabulary include a person-type term — a term for the one who habitually possesses or exercises this characteristic?_
  → Yes. H6175 a.rum: the prudent/shrewd person (Pro 12:23 — "the prudent conceals knowledge"). H7919 sa.khal in person-type form: the one who acts wisely. G5429 fronimos (shared with M15-A): the thoughtful, prudent person. The person-type for discernment is the a.rum — a recognisable wisdom literature character who is distinguished by careful evaluation before acting.
- *T7.1.9* — _Is there a term newly coined in the NT period for this characteristic — and if so, what does that coinage reveal?_
  → G1252 diakrinō acquires a distinctive second NT meaning: doubt, self-division (Jas 1:6 — "ask in faith, with no doubting [diakrinō]"; Rom 4:20 — "he did not diakrinō with respect to the promise of God"). This is a significant NT development: the discrimination/evaluation root is turned inward to name the self-divided state of the one whose inner evaluative faculty is split between faith and doubt. This meaning does not appear in the LXX or classical usage.
- *T7.2.1* — _What is the function of this characteristic's primary term within its primary verse — what role does it play in the sentence and argument?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T7.2.2* — _What literary form carries the primary verse evidence (narrative, psalm, wisdom, prophecy, epistle, apocalyptic) — and what does that form r…_
  → Primary anchor Isa 52:13 is Prophetic servant song (Fourth Servant Song — redemptive poetry). The form requires attending to the typological-eschatological register: the Servant's sa.khal is not primarily a prudential observation but a redemptive announcement. Responsible interpretation requires reading the verse within its servant-song context, not extracting sa.khal as a general wisdom claim. Secondary evidence Gen 15:6 is narrative (covenant-establishment narrative). The form requires attending to the covenant context: the divine crediting is a constitutive covenant act, not merely a moral assessment.
- *T7.2.3* — _What is the logical structure of key arguments in the verse evidence — what are the premises and conclusions?_
  → Gen 15:6 (VCG03): premise — Abraham believed God; conclusion — God credited it to him as righteousness. The argument is forensic: a moral act (believing) precedes a divine evaluative act (crediting); the crediting is constitutive of the status (righteous), not merely descriptive. Isa 52:13: premise — the Servant acts wisely; premise — wise action produces exaltation; conclusion — the Servant will be lifted up. Argument from character to outcome.
- *T7.2.4* — _What contextual setting carries the primary verse evidence (judicial, liturgical, covenantal, communal, eschatological) — and what does that…_
  → Primary settings: Prophetic servant song (Isa 52:13 — redemptive-servant context); Genesis narrative (Gen 15:6 — covenant-establishment context); Pastoral epistle (Heb 5:14 — community maturity argument); Pauline epistle (1Cor 11:31 — Eucharistic community context). M15-D is active across the full range of the inner life's covenantal contexts.
- *T7.2.5* — _Does any verse function as the primary anchor for this characteristic — the verse that most fully and directly expresses its essential chara…_
  → Isa 52:13: "Behold, my servant shall act wisely [sa.khal]; he shall be high and lifted up, and shall be exalted." Primary anchor for the positive pole of M15-D: the Servant's discerning-wise action (sa.khal) as the ground of his exaltation. The verse names the character (acting wisely), the subject (the Servant — paradigmatic person), and the consequence (exaltation). Gen 15:6 is the co-anchor for M15-D's evaluative sub-functions.
- *T7.2.6* — _What does the primary anchor verse reveal that no other verse reveals?_
  → Isa 52:13 alone names sa.khal in its redemptive-servant form and directly connects it to eschatological exaltation. No other verse establishes this sa.khal → exaltation sequence in a redemptive-covenantal frame.

- *T7.1.7* — _Does the vocabulary include a supplication or seeking term — a term for the act of seeking this characteristic from another?_

### 7.5 Deliberative planning, counsel, and purposive intent

<!-- AI WRITE: Chapter 7 §7.5 (Deliberative planning, counsel, and purposive intent)

Use general scientific knowledge — the analytical record is thin on this lens. Note explicitly where the record offers no view-from-outside material.
     SOURCE: T7 findings below (sparse).
