-->

<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch7 — T7 findings for Deliberative planning, counsel, and purposive intent -->

**T7 — Evidential and Methodological Foundation**

- *T7.1.1* — _What are the primary Hebrew and Greek terms for this characteristic — and what do their root meanings reveal?_
  → Primary terms: H3289 ya.ats (verb — to counsel, advise), H6098 e.tsah (noun — counsel, plan, purpose), H2161 za.mam (verb — to plan, devise, purpose), H1897B ha.gah (to meditate, plan — in purposive function), H2803I cha.shav (to devise, plan — in purposive function), H2161 za.mam, G1013 boulēma (deliberate will), G1011 bouleuō (to deliberate, plan), G1012 boulē (counsel, purpose, plan), G4286 prothesis (purpose, plan), G1106 gnōmē (considered judgment, opinion), G4307 pronoia (foresight, providence). Root ya.ats: "to give counsel" — reveals purposive counsel as a relational act, counsel given from one person to another. Root boulē: "to will deliberately" — reveals a decisive, considered act of the will, not impulse (Isa 14:24 — "as I have purposed, so shall it stand").
- *T7.1.10* — _What does the full vocabulary arc reveal about this characteristic's complete semantic range?_
  → Arc: divine irresistible counsel sworn by oath (Isa 14:24 — as I have purposed) → divine providential foresight (Rom 13:14 — pronoia, negatively; God's pronoia, positively) → apostolic considered judgment (1Cor 7:25 — gnōmē) → the counselor's wisdom given to the king (2Sa 16:23 — ya.ats as oracle of God) → deliberate human willing (Matt 1:19 — Joseph's boulomai) → inner cognitive devising (Pro 16:9 — cha.shav) → human unified purposing (Gen 11:6 — za.mam) → malicious scheming (Mic 2:1 — cha.shav/za.mam negative). The arc runs from God's sovereign irresistible counsel through human deliberate planning to its perversion in malicious scheming.
- *T7.1.2* — _What is the grammatical range of the primary term (noun, verb, adjective, participle) — and what does that range reveal about how the charac…_
  → Ya.ats: verb (to counsel, advise — 2Sa 16:23). E.tsah: noun (counsel, purpose — Isa 14:24 "as I have purposed"). Boulomai: verb (to will deliberately — Matt 1:19). Boulē: noun (deliberate purpose, plan). Gnōmē: noun (considered judgment — 1Cor 7:25). The verb-noun pairs reveal M15-E's dual character: the act of purposing (verbs — boulomai, ya.ats) and the formed counsel/plan that results (nouns — boulē, e.tsah). Both are essential to the characteristic: the deliberate willing and the purpose produced.
- *T7.1.3* — _What is the semantic range of the primary term — across what breadth of meaning does it operate?_
  → Ya.ats/e.tsah spans: interpersonal counsel (2Sa 16:23 — Ahithophel's counsel as oracle of God), divine irresistible purpose (Isa 14:24 — as I have purposed, so shall it stand), governance planning (2Chr 25:16 — counsel refused), inner deliberate devising (Pro 16:9 — the heart devises its way), malicious scheming (Mic 2:1 — devising wickedness), communal unified purposing (Gen 11:6 — nothing will be impossible for them), and apostolic considered judgment (1Cor 7:25 — gnōmē of the apostle). The semantic range reveals M15-E as the volitional-directive characteristic: it spans from inner deliberation through interpersonal counsel to divine irresistible purpose.
- *T7.1.4* — _Does the vocabulary include terms that distinguish distinct aspects of this characteristic — disposition versus act, received versus given, …_
  → Yes. Boulomai (verb): the deliberate willing — the volitional act (Matt 1:19 — Joseph's deliberate intention). Boulē (noun): the formed deliberate purpose — the product. Bouleuō (verb): the process of deliberating — the process. Ya.ats (verb): the act of counseling another — the relational act. E.tsah (noun): the counsel or purpose formed — the product. Gnōmē (noun): the considered judgment or opinion — a disposition/quality. The verb/noun pairs distinguish the act of purposing (boulomai, bouleuō, ya.ats) from the formed purpose itself (boulē, e.tsah) and the character of considered judgment (gnōmē).
- *T7.1.5* — _Does the vocabulary include a term for the structural opposite or absence of this characteristic?_
  → Yes. Rashness/impetuosity — acting without deliberate purposing (the inverse of the deliberate will of boulomai). The structural opposite of divine counsel is human counsel that attempts to override it and fails (Isa 14:27 — "who can frustrate it?" — the implied answer: no one). H5039 ne.va.lah in some contexts: the person who acts without purposive wisdom. The absence of purposive counsel produces directionless or self-destructive action.
- *T7.1.6* — _Does the vocabulary include a person-type term — a term for the one who habitually possesses or exercises this characteristic?_
  → Yes. H3289 ya.ets used as substantive: the counselor (Isa 9:6 — "Wonderful Counselor"; 2Sa 16:23 — Ahithophel as the counselor). G5429 fronimos (shared): the prudent planner. The person-type for counsel is most prominently the ya.ets — the one whose inner wisdom is reliably formed into effective counsel for others.
- *T7.1.7* — _Does the vocabulary include a supplication or seeking term — a term for the act of seeking this characteristic from another?_
  → Yes. H3289 ya.ats in the relational counsel mode: seeking counsel from another is the standard use of ya.ats — the king goes to the counselor, the person seeks ya.ats (wisdom counsel). 2Sa 16:23: the people sought Ahithophel's counsel. The seeking of counsel from another person is named in M15-E's vocabulary — the counselor-counselee relationship presupposes the seeking act.
- *T7.1.9* — _Is there a term newly coined in the NT period for this characteristic — and if so, what does that coinage reveal?_
  → G4307 pronoia in NT acquires moral-ethical loading: "make no provision [pronoia] for the flesh to gratify its desires" (Rom 13:14). In classical and LXX usage pronoia is primarily cognitive foresight (planning ahead). The NT application to the moral discipline of not planning for fleshly gratification is a NT development — foresight as a morally charged responsibility. Also: G1013 boulēma (Rom 9:19 — "who has resisted his boulēma?") — divine boulēma as irresistible divine will is given specific Pauline development.
- *T7.2.1* — _What is the function of this characteristic's primary term within its primary verse — what role does it play in the sentence and argument?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T7.2.2* — _What literary form carries the primary verse evidence (narrative, psalm, wisdom, prophecy, epistle, apocalyptic) — and what does that form r…_
  → Primary anchor Isa 14:24 is prophetic oracle (taunt-oracle against the king of Babylon). The form requires attending to the polemical context: God's irresistible counsel is declared against a human power that believed itself invincible. Responsible interpretation places the claim about counsel's irresistibility in a context of divine polemic against human pride, not in a context of abstract theodicy. Secondary evidence Pro 16:9 is Wisdom literature (aphorism). The didactic form requires attending to its generalising character: Pro 16:9 states a principle about the God-human relationship in planning, not an occasion.
- *T7.2.3* — _What is the logical structure of key arguments in the verse evidence — what are the premises and conclusions?_
  → Isa 14:24 (VCG03): premise — God has purposed; premise — as he purposed, so shall it stand; conclusion — all opposing counsel is demolished. The argument is from divine self-attestation to irresistible outcome. Pro 16:9 (VCG05): premise — the heart of man plans his way; premise — but the LORD establishes his steps; conclusion — human purposing and divine governance are non-competing. The argument is complementary, not adversarial: both are real and neither overrides the other.
- *T7.2.4* — _What contextual setting carries the primary verse evidence (judicial, liturgical, covenantal, communal, eschatological) — and what does that…_
  → Primary settings: Prophetic oracle (Isa 14:24 — divine sovereign purpose against historical kingdoms); Wisdom literature (Pro 16:9 — individual life-wisdom); Narrative (2Sa 16:23 — governance and political counsel). M15-E spans the full range: cosmic level (Isa 14), individual level (Pro 16:9), and political level (2Sa 16).
- *T7.2.5* — _Does any verse function as the primary anchor for this characteristic — the verse that most fully and directly expresses its essential chara…_
  → Isa 14:24: "The LORD of hosts has sworn: 'As I have planned, so shall it be, and as I have purposed, so shall it stand.'" Primary anchor: names the agent (LORD of hosts), the act (sworn — irrevocably declared), the content (planned and purposed), and the outcome (shall it be, shall it stand). The essential character of M15-E's most significant dimension in one declaration.
- *T7.2.6* — _What does the primary anchor verse reveal that no other verse reveals?_
  → Isa 14:24 alone records the divine oath-structure of irresistible counsel ("the LORD of hosts has sworn"). No other verse establishes the divine self-attestation of counsel's irresistibility with this authority-form. The oath makes the irresistibility not just asserted but bound.

### 7.6 Meditative and reflective inner activity

<!-- AI WRITE: Chapter 7 §7.6 (Meditative and reflective inner activity)
     LENGTH: ~400-500 words per characteristic (or grouped)
     FOCUS: Short overview of what human / clinical sciences observe about the human capacity corresponding to Meditative and reflective inner activity. Reflect on (a) synergies with the biblical picture, (b) gaps where science is silent on what Scripture emphasises, (c) differences where the scientific framing diverges from the biblical framing. <!-- EVIDENCE: Ch7 — T7 findings for Meditative and reflective inner activity -->

**T7 — Evidential and Methodological Foundation**

- *T7.1.1* — _What are the primary Hebrew and Greek terms for this characteristic — and what do their root meanings reveal?_
  → Primary terms: H7878 si.ach (verb — to muse, meditate, speak), H7881 si.chah (noun — meditation, musing), H1900 ha.gut (noun — meditation, musing), H1901 ha.gig (noun — meditation), H1902H hig.ga.von (noun — meditation, solemn sound), H7808 se.ach (noun — thought, meditation), H7919A sa.khal (shared with M15-D, in contemplative function), H8394 te.vu.nah (shared with M15-B), G1260 dialogizomai (to reason, deliberate, reflect), G1261 dialogismos (deliberation, reasoning, thought), G1760 enthumeomai (to ponder, reflect within — en + thumos), G1761 enthumēsis (thought arising from pondering). Root si.ach: "to muse, murmur to oneself" — the auditory-internal quality reveals meditation as inner speech, not silent abstraction. Root enthumeomai: "in the deep inner movement" — the thumos root reveals reflection as engaging the whole inner person (Psa 119:97 — "my meditation all the day").
- *T7.1.10* — _What does the full vocabulary arc reveal about this characteristic's complete semantic range?_
  → Arc: loving meditation on God's law all the day (Psa 119:97 — si.ach) → Daniel keeping the vision in heart (Dan 7:28 — se.khal) → Joseph's pre-angelic reflection (Matt 1:20 — enthumeomai) → awed contemplation of God's acts (Psa 143:5 — si.ach on mighty works) → self-deliberative inner monologue (Luk 12:17 — dialogizomai) → futile inner reasoning (Rom 1:21 — dialogismos negative). The arc spans from the richest devotional meditation through ordinary reflection to self-enclosed futile deliberation. The characteristic's range is determined entirely by the object and direction of the activity.
- *T7.1.2* — _What is the grammatical range of the primary term (noun, verb, adjective, participle) — and what does that range reveal about how the charac…_
  → Si.ach: verb (to muse, meditate, speak — Psa 119:97 "my meditation"). Si.chah: noun (meditation as practice). Ha.gut: noun (murmuring, meditation). Dialogizomai: verb (to reason, deliberate — Luk 12:17). Dialogismos: noun (deliberation, reasoning). Enthumeomai: verb (to ponder — Matt 1:20). The verb dominance reveals M15-F as constitutively active — meditative reflection is an activity being performed. The noun forms name the practice or the state that the activity produces (si.chah — the meditation one engages in; dialogismos — the deliberation underway).
- *T7.1.3* — _What is the semantic range of the primary term — across what breadth of meaning does it operate?_
  → Si.ach/dialogizomai spans: devotional meditation on God's law (Psa 119:97 — my meditation all the day), self-deliberative inner monologue (Luk 12:17 — the rich fool's dialogizomai), Joseph's pre-angelic reflection (Matt 1:20 — enthumeomai), Daniel's vision-holding (Dan 7:28 — se.khal), and divine declaring of the creature's inner reflection (Amos 4:13 — God declares to man his thought). The semantic range reveals M15-F as spanning from God-directed devotional meditation to self-enclosed anxious deliberation — morally neutral in form, determined by direction.
- *T7.1.4* — _Does the vocabulary include terms that distinguish distinct aspects of this characteristic — disposition versus act, received versus given, …_
  → Yes. Si.ach (verb): the act of musing, meditating — the active exercise (Psa 119:97 — "it is my meditation"). Si.chah (noun): the meditation as practice or condition. Ha.gut (noun): the murmuring/meditation as an inner state. Dialogizomai (verb): the act of deliberative reasoning. Dialogismos (noun): the deliberation as a formed inner state or product. Enthumeomai (verb): the act of pondering within. The vocabulary distinguishes: the active meditative practice (verbs) from the meditative state or condition (nouns — ha.gut, si.chah). This reveals M15-F as having both an activity and a condition aspect.
- *T7.1.5* — _Does the vocabulary include a term for the structural opposite or absence of this characteristic?_
  → Yes. Dialogismos in its negative form (futile/corrupt inner reasoning — Rom 1:21 "their thinking became futile"). The structural opposite of productive meditation on God's law (VCG03 Psa 119:97) is the self-enclosed futile inner monologue (VCG01 dialogizomai inverse — Luk 12:17 rich fool). The structural opposite is not the absence of inner reflection but its misdirection — the same inner activity producing worthless or corrupt output.
- *T7.1.9* — _Is there a term newly coined in the NT period for this characteristic — and if so, what does that coinage reveal?_
  → G1760 enthumeomai: to ponder within (Matt 1:20 — Joseph's pondering before angelic disclosure; Matt 9:4 — Jesus perceiving the scribes' inner thoughts). The en + thumos compound root is NT-period usage: the emphasis on reflective activity within the deep inner movement (thumos) is a distinctive NT emphasis on the reflective-affective depth of inner deliberation. Not an entirely new coinage but a NT-specific deployment.
- *T7.2.1* — _What is the function of this characteristic's primary term within its primary verse — what role does it play in the sentence and argument?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T7.2.2* — _What literary form carries the primary verse evidence (narrative, psalm, wisdom, prophecy, epistle, apocalyptic) — and what does that form r…_
  → Primary anchor Psa 119:97 is Psalmic poetry (acrostic devotional poem — the longest psalm). The form requires attending to the hyperbolic devotional register: "all the day" is not a literal time claim but an expression of the psalmist's total orientation. Responsible interpretation reads the psalm as devotional poetry whose hyperbolic form expresses intensity of commitment, not as a prescriptive rule about meditation hours. The acrostic form itself models the meditative practice the psalm describes: sustained, structured return to the same content.
- *T7.2.3* — _What is the logical structure of key arguments in the verse evidence — what are the premises and conclusions?_
  → Psa 119:97-99 (VCG03): premise — I love your law; premise — it is my meditation all the day; premise — through it I have more understanding than all my teachers; conclusion — meditation on God's law produces superior understanding. The argument is developmental: love → meditative practice → cognitive outcome. The result is also the evidence that the practice is effective.
- *T7.2.4* — _What contextual setting carries the primary verse evidence (judicial, liturgical, covenantal, communal, eschatological) — and what does that…_
  → Primary settings: Psalmic poetry (Psa 119 — covenantal devotional poetry); Prophetic narrative (Dan 7:28 — visionary reception context); Gospel narrative (Matt 1:20 — Joseph's pre-angelic reflection). M15-F is the inner activity of the devout person in every ordinary and extraordinary moment.
- *T7.2.5* — _Does any verse function as the primary anchor for this characteristic — the verse that most fully and directly expresses its essential chara…_
  → Psa 119:97: "Oh how I love your law! It is my meditation all the day." Primary anchor: affective love of God's law as the precondition ("oh how I love"), the meditative activity as the practice ("my meditation"), and the temporal commitment as the scope ("all the day"). The verse holds the full structure of M15-F's essential character: loving, meditative, sustained dwelling on God's word.
- *T7.2.6* — _What does the primary anchor verse reveal that no other verse reveals?_
  → Psa 119:97 alone holds love and meditation in explicit mutual relationship in a single declaration. No other verse in M15-F makes the affective precondition (love) and the cognitive practice (meditation) explicit in the same statement.

**T7 — Evidential and Methodological Foundation**

- *T7.1.6* — _Does the vocabulary include a person-type term — a term for the one who habitually possesses or exercises this characteristic?_
  → No dedicated person-type term in M15-F's vocabulary. The meditating person is characterised by the practice (the one who meditates "all the day" — Psa 119:97), not by a dedicated nominal. M15-F names the activity and the state but not a recognisable human type distinguished by the practice.
- *T7.1.7* — _Does the vocabulary include a supplication or seeking term — a term for the act of seeking this characteristic from another?_
  → No specialised supplication or seeking term for meditation in M15-F's vocabulary. Meditation is entered, not sought from another. The practice is initiated by the person themselves.

### 7.7 Inner thought-content — the mind's formed thoughts

**T7 — Evidential and Methodological Foundation**

- *T7.1.1* — _What are the primary Hebrew and Greek terms for this characteristic — and what do their root meanings reveal?_
  → Primary terms: G3540 noēma (noun — thought, mind, purpose — from noeō), G1270 dianoēma (noun — thought, intention), G1771 ennoia (noun — inner thought, disposition — en + nous), G1963 epinoia (noun — thought, purpose — epi + nous), G5424 frēn (noun — mind, thinking capacity — in M15-G's formed-content role), H4093 mad.da (noun — knowledge, thought — Hebrew/Aramaic), H6248 ash.tut (noun — thought — in Daniel), H6250 esh.to.nah (noun — thought), H7454 re.a (Aramaic noun — thought, purpose), H7476 ra.yon (Aramaic noun — thought, reflection). Root noēma: from noeō (to perceive, understand) — reveals thought-content as the product of prior cognitive activity, not raw sensation. Root ra.yon/re.a: Aramaic thought/reflection roots — used in Daniel for the king's alarming thoughts, revealing thought-content as inner states arising from the person's whole situation (2Cor 4:4 — "blinded the minds [noēmata]").
- *T7.1.10* — _What does the full vocabulary arc reveal about this characteristic's complete semantic range?_
  → Arc: God's thoughts directed toward the human person (Psa 139:17 — his thoughts toward us are precious) → God-given knowledge content placed in Solomon (2Chr 1:10 — mad.da) → alarming night-thoughts arising from inner distress (Dan 4:5 — ra.yon) → thought-content forming plans and intentions (G1963 epinoia) → inner disposition (G1771 ennoia) → formed thought-content as contested inner territory (2Cor 4:4 — noēmata blinded) → thought-content brought captive to Christ (2Cor 10:5 — taking every noēma captive). The arc reveals M15-G as ranging from divine thought-content directed toward the creature through divinely bestowed inner knowledge to adversarially contested and volitionally governed thought-content.
- *T7.1.2* — _What is the grammatical range of the primary term (noun, verb, adjective, participle) — and what does that range reveal about how the charac…_
  → Noēma, dianoēma, ennoia, epinoia: all nouns (formed thought-content — 2Cor 4:4 "blinded the noēmata"). Ra.yon, re.a: nouns (thought, reflection — Dan 4:5). Mad.da: noun (knowledge-content placed in the person — 2Chr 1:10). The overwhelming nominal dominance reveals M15-G as a content-holding characteristic — it names the product of cognitive activity, not the activity itself. No primary verbs in M15-G's term set: the characteristic is the stored, formed thought, not the forming.
- *T7.1.3* — _What is the semantic range of the primary term — across what breadth of meaning does it operate?_
  → Noēma/ra.yon spans: adversarially blinded thought-content (2Cor 4:4 — noēmata blinded by the god of this age), thought-content to be captured (2Cor 10:5 — taking every noēma captive), alarming night-thoughts arising from inner states (Dan 4:5 — ra.yon troubled the king), and divinely placed knowledge-content (2Chr 1:10 — mad.da given to Solomon). The semantic range reveals M15-G as naming thought-content in all its modes: contested, governed, spontaneous, and divinely bestowed.
- *T7.1.4* — _Does the vocabulary include terms that distinguish distinct aspects of this characteristic — disposition versus act, received versus given, …_
  → Yes. Noēma (noun): formed mind-content — the product of cognitive activity. Ennoia (noun): inner disposition, thought — a quality of the inner person. Epinoia (noun): thought as formed intention — the purposive aspect. The three Greek nouns distinguish: raw formed thought (noēma — 2Cor 4:4), the dispositional inner quality (ennoia), and the purposive directed thought (epinoia). All are nouns — M15-G's vocabulary does not include verbs, confirming it names the product, not the producing activity.
- *T7.1.5* — _Does the vocabulary include a term for the structural opposite or absence of this characteristic?_
  → Yes. Blinded noēmata (2Cor 4:4 — the blinded thought-content as the structural opposite of governed, Christ-aligned thought-content). The structural opposite of M15-G in its redeemed form is M15-G in its adversarially captured form: the same thought-content, one governed by Christ's obedience (2Cor 10:5), one blinded by the god of this age (2Cor 4:4).
- *T7.1.9* — _Is there a term newly coined in the NT period for this characteristic — and if so, what does that coinage reveal?_
  → G3540 noēma: the mind's formed content (2Cor 4:4; 2Cor 10:5 — "taking every noēma captive"). While noēma exists in classical Greek (Plato uses it for the mind's grasp), its NT deployment in a spiritual warfare context (adversarial blinding, taking captive) is a distinctively Pauline theological development. The noēma as contested inner cognitive territory — simultaneously the object of adversarial attack and of volitional governance — is a NT development of the term.
- *T7.2.1* — _What is the function of this characteristic's primary term within its primary verse — what role does it play in the sentence and argument?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T7.2.2* — _What literary form carries the primary verse evidence (narrative, psalm, wisdom, prophecy, epistle, apocalyptic) — and what does that form r…_
  → Primary anchor 2Cor 4:4 is Pauline epistle (apologetic argument — Paul defending his ministry against accusations). The epistolary form requires attending to the apologetic context: Paul is explaining why the gospel is not being received in Corinth, not making a general psychological claim about unbelief. Responsible interpretation places the blinding of noēmata within the specific missionary context Paul is addressing. Secondary evidence 2Cor 10:5 is Pauline epistle (same letter, different section — spiritual warfare argument). The military metaphor in 2Cor 10:4-5 requires responsible interpretation of the warfare imagery: the demolishing of strongholds is the work of the gospel's power, not literal military action.
- *T7.2.3* — _What is the logical structure of key arguments in the verse evidence — what are the premises and conclusions?_
  → 2Cor 4:4 (VCG01): premise — the god of this age has blinded the minds of unbelievers; premise — to keep them from seeing the light of the gospel; conclusion — the blindness of the mind explains the failure to see the gospel. The argument is causal and adversarial. 2Cor 10:5 (VCG01): premise — strongholds of thought oppose the knowledge of God; premise — weapons have divine power to demolish them; conclusion — the inner cognitive domain can be brought into Christ's obedience. Argument from capability through instrument to outcome.
- *T7.2.4* — _What contextual setting carries the primary verse evidence (judicial, liturgical, covenantal, communal, eschatological) — and what does that…_
  → Primary settings: Pauline epistle (2Cor 4 and 10 — community conflict and spiritual warfare context); Chronicles narrative (2Chr 1:10 — covenant inauguration of Solomon's reign). The same characteristic is contested in the community setting (2Cor) and bestowed in the governance setting (2Chr).
- *T7.2.5* — _Does any verse function as the primary anchor for this characteristic — the verse that most fully and directly expresses its essential chara…_
  → 2Cor 4:4: "In their case the god of this age has blinded the minds [noēmata] of the unbelievers, to keep them from seeing the light of the gospel of the glory of Christ, who is the image of God." Primary anchor: names the thought-content (noēmata), the adversarial agent (the god of this age), the mechanism (blinding), and the consequence (inability to see the gospel). The verse holds the most theologically significant claim about M15-G: it is the contested inner territory.
- *T7.2.6* — _What does the primary anchor verse reveal that no other verse reveals?_
  → 2Cor 4:4 alone names both the adversarial agent (the god of this age) and the adversarial mechanism (blinding) and the adversarial goal (preventing gospel-sight) in direct relation to the noēmata. No other verse in M15-G establishes the full adversarial targeting of thought-content with this specificity.

### 7.8 Logos — the word as inner-being engagement

<!-- AI WRITE: Chapter 7 §7.8 (Logos — the word as inner-being engagement)
     LENGTH: ~400-500 words per characteristic (or grouped)
     FOCUS: Short overview of what human / clinical sciences observe about the human capacity corresponding to Logos — the word as inner-being engagement. Reflect on (a) synergies with the biblical picture, (b) gaps where science is silent on what Scripture emphasises, (c) differences where the scientific framing diverges from the biblical framing. Use general scientific knowledge — the analytical record is thin on this lens. Note explicitly where the record offers no view-from-outside material.

<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch7 — T7 findings for Logos — the word as inner-being engagement -->

**T7 — Evidential and Methodological Foundation**

- *T7.1.1* — _What are the primary Hebrew and Greek terms for this characteristic — and what do their root meanings reveal?_
  → Primary term: G3056 logos (noun — word, reason, account, matter). Root leg-: "to gather, to say" — the root reveals logos as both rational ordering (gathering/arranging) and speech (saying). This dual root meaning is the foundation of the logos's double function in M15-H: the word as divine rational principle (Jn 1:1) and the word as spoken/written communication (Col 3:16). No Hebrew equivalent in M15-H's term set — logos is the sole term. The single-term character of M15-H reveals it as the Greek conceptual crystallisation of what Hebrew required multiple roots to express (Col 3:16 — "let the word of Christ dwell in you richly").
- *T7.1.10* — _What does the full vocabulary arc reveal about this characteristic's complete semantic range?_
  → Arc: logos as pre-existent divine Person (Jn 1:1 — in the beginning was the logos) → logos as divine cleansing word (Jn 15:3 — clean through the word I have spoken) → logos of the cross as power of God (1Cor 1:18) → logos dwelling richly and forming community (Col 3:16) → logos as gracious human speech (Col 4:6) → logos as single moral principle (Gal 5:14 — love your neighbour) → logos as the unintelligible word that does not reach the inner person (1Cor 14:19 inverse). The arc spans from the eternal divine Person through the specific word that cleanses through the community-forming word through gracious speech to the moral principle that summarises all law. The complete range runs from the most transcendent (divine Person) to the most practical (gracious daily speech).
- *T7.1.2* — _What is the grammatical range of the primary term (noun, verb, adjective, participle) — and what does that range reveal about how the charac…_
  → G3056 logos: noun only (the word, reason, account — Col 3:16 "the word of Christ"). The singular nominal character of M15-H reveals the logos as an entity or content — the word as something existing, dwelling, being received, and being expressed. The corresponding verbal form (legō — to say) is not part of M15-H's term set; the noun alone constitutes the characteristic. This reveals M15-H as naming the word as communicative reality, not merely the act of speaking.
- *T7.1.3* — _What is the semantic range of the primary term — across what breadth of meaning does it operate?_
  → G3056 logos spans: divine word as power and cleansing agent (1Cor 1:18 — the logos of the cross; Jn 15:3 — clean through the word spoken), community-forming word dwelling richly (Col 3:16), gracious communicated speech (Col 4:6), moral principle summarising the law (Gal 5:14 — love your neighbour as yourself), reasoned disputation (Acts 17:2 — dialegō using logos), and divine Person (Jn 1:1 — in the beginning was the logos). The semantic range is the widest of any single term in M15-H — logos alone spans divine nature, communal formation, moral principle, and personal communication.
- *T7.1.4* — _Does the vocabulary include terms that distinguish distinct aspects of this characteristic — disposition versus act, received versus given, …_
  → The logos has no internal vocabulary differentiation in M15-H's term set — G3056 is the sole term. However, logos itself carries internal semantic differentiation by context: logos as divine personal word (Col 3:16 — "word of Christ"), logos as spoken communicative word (Col 4:6 — "let your speech"), logos as moral principle (Gal 5:14 — "the whole law is fulfilled in one logos"). The single term carries received/given, inward/outward, and normative/communal distinctions through context rather than through vocabulary differentiation. S — No additional vocabulary distinction evidenced within M15-H's term set itself.
- *T7.1.5* — _Does the vocabulary include a term for the structural opposite or absence of this characteristic?_
  → Yes. The unintelligible word — the tongue without interpretation (1Cor 14:19 — Paul would rather speak five intelligible logos-words than ten thousand in a tongue). The structural opposite of the logos that reaches the inner person (Col 3:16) is the unintelligible utterance that reaches no one's inner being. Also: silence or the withheld word — the word that could be spoken but is not.
- *T7.1.9* — _Is there a term newly coined in the NT period for this characteristic — and if so, what does that coinage reveal?_
  → G3056 logos as divine Person (Jn 1:1 — "in the beginning was the logos, and the logos was with God, and the logos was God"). This is the most theologically radical NT development in the cluster and arguably in the NT. The word-as-divine-Person transcends all classical or LXX uses: the logos is no longer merely the rational principle (Stoic), the divine word (OT prophetic tradition), or the wisdom-as-agent (Wisdom literature) — it is the pre-existent divine Person who becomes flesh (Jn 1:14). This coinage reveals that M15-H's characteristic is grounded in a Person, not merely in a principle or phenomenon.
- *T7.2.1* — _What is the function of this characteristic's primary term within its primary verse — what role does it play in the sentence and argument?_
  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
- *T7.2.2* — _What literary form carries the primary verse evidence (narrative, psalm, wisdom, prophecy, epistle, apocalyptic) — and what does that form r…_
  → Primary anchor Col 3:16 is Pauline epistle (household code context — instruction for community life in Christ). The epistolary form requires attending to the communal-practical register: Col 3:16 is instruction for how the community is to live together, not primarily a theological proposition about the word. Responsible interpretation treats the verse as describing a community practice (word dwelling richly) that produces communal outcomes (teaching, admonishing, worship). Secondary evidence 1Cor 1:18 is Pauline epistle (apologetic/community-correction context). The form requires attending to the polemic: the logos of the cross is declared foolish by the worldly-wise in a specific community context of division.
- *T7.2.3* — _What is the logical structure of key arguments in the verse evidence — what are the premises and conclusions?_
  → 1Cor 1:18 (VCG01): premise — the same logos is heard by all; premise — those perishing perceive it as folly; premise — those being saved perceive it as power; conclusion — the inner state of the hearer determines the effect of the logos. The argument reveals the logos as diagnostically revealing — it does not change between hearers but its reception reveals their inner condition. Col 3:16 (VCG01): premise — the word of Christ can dwell in the person; premise — let it dwell richly; conclusion — from that dwelling come wisdom, teaching, and worship. Argument from inner possession to communal outcome.
- *T7.2.4* — _What contextual setting carries the primary verse evidence (judicial, liturgical, covenantal, communal, eschatological) — and what does that…_
  → Primary settings: Pauline epistle (Col 3:16 — community formation instruction; Gal 5:14 — ethical summary; 1Cor 1:18 — apologetic/community crisis); Gospel prologue tradition (Jn 1 — cosmic origin of the word). M15-H operates in community formation (Col 3), ethical life (Gal 5), apologetic crisis (1Cor 1), and cosmic theology (Jn 1). The word is relevant to every register of the community's life.
- *T7.2.5* — _Does any verse function as the primary anchor for this characteristic — the verse that most fully and directly expresses its essential chara…_
  → Col 3:16: "Let the word of Christ dwell in you richly, teaching and admonishing one another in all wisdom, singing psalms and hymns and spiritual songs, with thankfulness in your hearts to God." Primary anchor: the logos (word of Christ) as its content, dwelling (inward possession) as its location, richly (depth of possession) as its quality, and teaching/admonishing/singing/thankfulness as its communal fruits. The verse holds M15-H's full cycle: received → dwelling → expressing → worshipping.
- *T7.2.6* — _What does the primary anchor verse reveal that no other verse reveals?_
  → Col 3:16 alone holds the complete M15-H cycle in a single verse: the word's content (Christ), its mode (dwelling), its quality (richly), and its communal fruits (wisdom, teaching, admonishing, worship). No other verse in M15-H captures the full inner-possession to communal-formation sequence simultaneously.

  → [Sub-group not separately addressed in source — see cluster-level finding for this prompt]
<!-- /EVIDENCE -->

<!-- EVIDENCE: Ch7 — T7 silences for Logos — the word as inner-being engagement -->

**T7 — Evidential and Methodological Foundation**

- *T7.1.6* — _Does the vocabulary include a person-type term — a term for the one who habitually possesses or exercises this characteristic?_
  → No dedicated person-type term in M15-H's term set. The logos-speaker (Col 4:6) and the logos-receiver (Col 3:16) are defined by their relationship to the word, not by a dedicated nominal that names them as a recognisable human type.
- *T7.1.7* — _Does the vocabulary include a supplication or seeking term — a term for the act of seeking this characteristic from another?_
  → No specialised seeking term for the logos in M15-H's vocabulary. The logos is received, not primarily petitioned for. The mode of receiving is openness and dwelling (Col 3:16 — "let it dwell"), not supplication. The seeking-the-word pattern is present in the wisdom tradition broadly but not as a dedicated term in M15-H's vocabulary.
<!-- /EVIDENCE -->

  → LXX investigation required for M15-A. The LXX rendering of cha.kham/chok.mah by sophia establishes the primary Greek-Hebrew lexical bridge for wisdom, but the full range of LXX uses and any semantic shifts require external tool investigation. [FLAG-M15-002 — parked, Logos Bible Software session required]

- *T7.1.8* — _What does the LXX use of the vocabulary reveal about continuity or development of this characteristic across the Testaments?_
  → LXX investigation required for M15-C. The LXX rendering of ya.da vocabulary and the relationship between Hebrew relational knowing and Greek oida/ginōskō requires external tool investigation. [FLAG-M15-004 — parked]
- *T7.1.8* — _What does the LXX use of the vocabulary reveal about continuity or development of this characteristic across the Testaments?_
  → LXX investigation required for M15-D. The LXX rendering of sa.khal, cha.shav, ta.am and their relationship to NT diakrinō and logizomai requires external tool investigation. [FLAG-M15-005 — parked]

  → LXX investigation required for M15-G. The LXX rendering of ra.yon/re.a/mad.da and their relationship to NT noēma/ennoia/epinoia requires external tool investigation. [FLAG-M15-011 — parked]
- *T7.1.8* — _What does the LXX use of the vocabulary reveal about continuity or development of this characteristic across the Testaments?_
